فهو خبر يحتمل الصدق والكذب. ولا دليل على صدقه، وكما أن في الناس أشراراً دأبهم الكذب والتلاعب بعقول الناس، فإن في الجن أيضاً كذلك. فمن أين لك أن الذي يناجيك أو يكتب لك جواب أسئلتك من قاع السلة، ليس شيطاناً مريداً جاء ليلبس عليك دينك ويلهو بمخادعتك ويلتذ بالكذب عليك؟ أولم تقرأ أن أكثر أسباب الحماقة في المنحرفين أو المجانين الذين ادعوا أنهم أنبياء أو عظماء إنما هو هواجس من هؤلاء الشياطين، إذ هتفوا في أعماق أفئدتهم أو على طبلة آذانهم أنهم أحباء الله وعظماؤه.. وأن الله قد أكرمهم بإسقاط تكاليفه عنهم. فربا الغرور في أوداجهم وثقلت رؤوسهم الفارغة بالخديعة وراحت تهتز منهم الأعطاف.. وأيقنوا أنهم وزراء الله المدللون في الأرض بينه وبينهم نسب الأرواح الطاهرة التي تناجيهم، مع أنها ليست إلا أرواحاً حقيرة من أرواح مردة الشياطين التي تحط عادة فوق قمامات العقول والأفكار تتلهى بإغوائها واللعب بها فالأرواح لاشك في وجودها، ولكنها لا ينبغي أن تكون صادقة، إذا قالت لك إحداها أنها روح أحد الأنبياء، ثم راحت تقدم لك المبادئ والعظات بناء على أنها كذلك. إنها بدون ريب روح شريرة تلهو بمخادعتك!..
So it is a report that admits of truth and falsehood. There is no proof of its truthfulness. Just as there are among people evil ones whose habit is lying and manipulating people's minds, so too among the jinn there are likewise. How do you know that the one who whispers to you or writes you an answer to your questions from the bottom of the basket is not a rebellious devil who has come to confuse your religion for you, to amuse himself by deceiving you, and to delight in lying to you? Have you not read that most of the causes of foolishness in the deviant or the insane who claimed to be prophets or great men are but whisperings from these devils, when they shout in the depths of their hearts or on the eardrums of their ears that they are the beloved of Allah and His great ones, and that Allah has honored them by dropping His obligations from them. So arrogance grew in their veins, their empty heads became heavy with deception, and their shoulders began to sway.. And they became convinced that they are the pampered ministers of Allah on earth, between Him and them a kinship of pure spirits that whisper to them, while they are nothing but base spirits from the spirits of rebellious devils that usually descend upon the trash heaps of minds and thoughts, amusing themselves by seducing and playing with them. So spirits exist beyond doubt, but they ought not to be truthful. If one of them tells you that it is the spirit of one of the prophets, and then proceeds to present principles and sermons based on that, it is without doubt an evil spirit amusing itself by deceiving you!..
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the deceptive nature of spirits. The author states that any report from a spirit (like through mediumship) can be true or false. Since there are liars among humans and jinn, one cannot trust such a spirit. He compares those who claim prophethood due to whispers to insane people who were fooled by devils. The devils make them believe they are beloved of God and exempt from obligations. The author stresses that these spirits are actually evil and deceptive, not pure as claimed. He concludes that such spirits are lying.

God's Wisdom in Using Angels as Intermediaries in the Unseen
Buti explains the wisdom behind God's use of angels and causes in the unseen realm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God uses angels and other intermediaries in the unseen realm, and why this does not imply any need in God.

Core Idea
God uses intermediaries not out of need, but to match human understanding.

You may wonder: why does God, who is all-powerful, use angels to record deeds, weigh actions, or punish? This passage from Buti explains that God's wisdom and mercy led Him to establish a system of causes in the unseen world, so that humans—who are accustomed to means and causes—can grasp these realities. The lesson clarifies that God is independent of these intermediaries; He merely accommodates our limited imagination.

Guided Path
1
Understand the human context
Read how Buti describes human life as embedded in a system of means and causes. This sets the stage for why God adapts unseen realities to that framework.
Notice the phrase 'ألف فيها نظام الوسائط والأسباب' – humans are habituated to intermediaries.
2
Identify the examples given
List the specific unseen events God informs us about: two recording angels, the scale of deeds, the Zabaniyya, the angels carrying the Throne, guardian angels, and the angel of death.
These are all instances of God using intermediaries in the ghayb (unseen).
3
Grasp the key point: God's independence
Buti emphasizes that it is 'معلوم بالبداهة' (axiomatically known) that God is not in need of any of these intermediaries. He created them and their power; they do not add anything to His sovereignty.
This refutes any misconception that God needs help.
4
Connect to divine wisdom
Understand that the purpose is to manifest God's power in a form familiar to humans. This is a mercy from God, making the unseen comprehensible.
The passage ends with a reference to a clear example from the Qur'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن الله عز وجل لما اقتضت حكمته ورحمته بعباده ذلك ، وعاش الإنسان حياة ألف فيها نظام الوسائط والأسباب ، وأصبح خياله لا يتصور الأمور إلا منوطة بمقدماتها ووسائطها - اقتضت حكمته جل جلاله أن يقيم الأحداث الغيبية أيضاً على نظام الأسباب ، ليتصورها الإنسان حسب مألوفه وكما اعتاد فكره وخياله . فأخبره عن مراقبة الله لكل أعماله وتصرفاته في الدنيا وأوضح له أن ذلك يتم بواسطة ملكين يراقبان ذلك منه ويحصيان كل حركاته وسكناته وأخبره أن من رجحت حسناته على سيأته كان من المفلحين يوم القيامة ، وأوضح له أن الكشف ذلك عن يتم بميزان توزن فيه الأعمال . وأخبره عن النار وأن لها زبانية يقومون بشأنها وبتعذيب الكافرين فيها ، وأن ملائكة تحمل العرش ، وملائكة تحافظ على الإنسان ، وملكاً يقبض الأرواح ، ومعلوم بالبداهة أن الله عز وجل - وهو الذي خلق هؤلاء الملائكة وأولاهم هذه الطاقة ـ غير محتاج إلى وساطتهم وسببيتهم في شيء ، ولكن شاء الله عز وجل أن يظهر سلطانه وقوته لعباده بالشكل الذي ألفوه في حياتهم وتعودتـه أخيلتهم وأفكارهم . ولعل أقرب مثال لذلك ما جاء في صريح تبيانـه جل جلاله
Then, since God's wisdom and mercy towards His servants necessitated that, and man lived a life in which he was accustomed to the system of means and causes, and his imagination could not conceive of matters except as attached to their premises and means – His wisdom, exalted be His majesty, required that He establish the unseen events also upon a system of causes, so that man might conceive them according to his familiar way and as his mind and imagination were accustomed. So He informed him about God's watch over all his deeds and actions in this world and explained to him that this occurs by means of two angels who watch him from that and enumerate all his movements and stillnesses. And He informed him that whoever's good deeds outweigh his bad deeds will be among the successful on the Day of Resurrection, and He explained to him that the disclosure of that occurs by a scale in which deeds are weighed. And He informed him about the Fire and that it has guardians (Zabaniyya) who attend to it and to the punishment of the disbelievers therein, and that angels carry the Throne, and angels protect humans, and an angel takes the souls. And it is known axiomatically that God, may He be glorified and exalted – He who created these angels and granted them this energy – is not in need of their mediation or causality in anything. But God, may He be glorified and exalted, willed to manifest His sovereignty and power to His servants in the form they were accustomed to in their lives and to which their imaginations and thoughts were habituated. And perhaps the closest example of that is what came in the clear revelation of His, exalted be His majesty.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage explains the wisdom behind God's establishment of a system of causes in the unseen realm. The author notes that human beings have become accustomed to a life of means and causes, so their imagination can only conceive of events as linked to their premises and intermediaries. Therefore, God's wisdom required that He also establish unseen events (al-ghaybiyya) upon a system of causes, so that humans can understand them according to their familiar frame of reference. The author then provides examples: God informed humans that He watches over their deeds through two angels who record every action; that judgment on the Day of Resurrection occurs by a scale; that the Fire has guardians (Zabaniyya) who punish disbelievers; that angels carry the Throne, protect humans, and take souls. The author emphasizes that it is axiomatic that God, the Creator of these angels and their power, has no need for their mediation or causality. Rather, God willed to manifest His sovereignty and power in a form familiar to humans. Thus, the use of angels and other intermediaries is not due to any need in God, but out of mercy and wisdom to facilitate human comprehension. The passage closes by hinting at a Qur'anic example (likely referring to verses mentioning angels).

Correction: Buti explicitly states that it is axiomatically known that God is not in need of any mediation or causality. He created angels and their power; they are tools for human comprehension, not helpers for God.

Key Takeaway
God uses angels and other intermediaries in the unseen not because He needs them, but to help humans—who are accustomed to causes—comprehend divine actions.

?
The passage says God is not in need of any intermediary. He could have acted directly, but He chose a familiar form. Are you using this familiar form as a bridge to believe more firmly, or have you taken it for granted? What will you do today to let this knowledge renew your awe of Allah?

The Wisdom Behind the Testimony of Limbs on Judgment Day
Buti explains the unique value of the testimony of hands and feet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind the testimony of the hands and feet on Judgment Day and why it demonstrates Allah's power more than mere knowledge.

Core Idea
The testimony of limbs on Judgment Day exposes human helplessness, proving Allah's absolute sovereignty.

This lesson explores a profound question: since Allah already knows everything, why will He cause the disbelievers' limbs to testify against them? Dr. Buti, drawing on Quranic verse 36:65, explains that this testimony serves to strip away any illusion of escape or deception, manifesting Allah's divinity in a way that pure knowledge alone does not.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Begin by reading the verse in Arabic and translation. Notice that Allah seals mouths and makes hands and feet speak.
This sets the context.
2
Identify the key question
The author asks: what value does this testimony add, since Allah already knows everything? Identify this question in the Arabic.
This is the crux of the lesson.
3
Understand the answer
The answer is that the testimony reveals that the person cannot use any deception or mediation. It is a demonstration of Allah's power.
Focus on the phrase 'لا سبيل له' (no way for him).
4
Compare with alternative
The author contrasts this with a hypothetical statement that Allah knows everything. Notice why the actual ordeal is more powerful.
This shows the wisdom behind the event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أنه سبحانه وتعالى يختم يوم القيامة على أفواه الكافرين ويأمر أيديهم وأرجلهم فتشهد بما اقترفوا ، وذلك في قوله جل جلاله : ﴿ اليَومَ نَخْتِمُ على أَفْوَاهِهِمْ وَتُكَلِّمُنا أَيْديهِمْ وَتَشْهَدُ أَرْجُلُهُمْ بما كانوا يكسبونَ ﴾ [ يس : ٦٥ ] فما قيمة شهادة الأيدي والأرجل لصاحبها أو عليه مع ما هو ثابت من أن الله عز وجل مطلع على كل خافية منه ؟ إن قيمة ذلك محصورة في أن هذه الشهادة توضح للإنسان أن لا سبيل له في ذلك الموقف إلى استعمال شيء مما كان اعتاده في الدنيا من مختلف مظاهر التوسط أو التحايل أو التخفي . إن من اليسير على الله جل جلاله أن يبطل ذلك كله بمثله . فإن زورت في النطق بين يديه جل جلاله أنطق طرفاً من أطرافك بما يكشف عن تزوير لسانك . وفي هذا من تجلّي ألوهية الله وعظيم سلطانه ما لا تجده في قوله مثلاً : اليوم لا يخفى علينا شيء من سابق شؤونهم وسوف نحاسبهم على كل ذلك
Because He, glorified and exalted, will seal the mouths of the disbelievers on the Day of Resurrection and command their hands and feet, so they will testify to what they committed. That is in His statement, majestic is His glory: 'Today We seal their mouths, and their hands speak to Us, and their feet bear witness to what they used to earn' [Ya Sin: 65]. So what is the value of the testimony of the hands and feet for or against their owner, given that it is established that Allah, mighty and majestic, is aware of every secret of his? Its value is limited to the fact that this testimony makes clear to a person that he has no way in that situation to use anything of what he was accustomed to in the world of various forms of mediation, deception, or concealment. It is easy for Allah, majestic is His glory, to nullify all that by its like. For if you falsify in speech before Him, majestic is His glory, He makes a part of your limbs speak revealing the falsification of your tongue. And in this is such a manifestation of Allah's divinity and the greatness of His authority that you do not find in, for example, His statement: 'Today nothing of their past affairs is hidden from Us, and We will account them for all of that.'
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the wisdom behind the testimony of the limbs on the Day of Judgment. The author begins by citing the Quranic verse in which Allah says He will seal the mouths of the disbelievers and cause their hands and feet to testify. He then raises a question: since Allah already knows everything hidden, what additional value does this testimony have? The answer is that this testimony demonstrates to the person that in that situation, he cannot resort to any of the means he used in this world—such as mediation, deception, or hiding. It is easy for Allah to nullify all that. If a person tries to lie with his tongue, Allah will make a limb speak and expose the lie. This manifestation of Allah's divinity and power is even greater than if He had simply said that nothing is hidden from Him and He will account them. The point is the display of His power to the creation, not just His knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The testimony of limbs is unnecessary since God already knows everything.
Correction: Buti explains that its purpose is not to inform God but to demonstrate the person's helplessness and manifest God's power.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of limbs on Judgment Day is not for Allah's knowledge but to reveal the creature's utter incapacity and to manifest divine power.

Today, acknowledge one area where you have been acting as if you can hide from Allah, and repent right now.

Death: the Witnessed Reality and Its Lessons
Buti affirms death as an observable reality and its theological implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that death is an observable, tangible reality that affirms Allah's unique sovereignty and humbles all creation.

Core Idea
Death is the great witnessed reality that proves Allah's sole divinity.

Before discussing the unseen aspects of death, the author first establishes that death itself is not an unseen matter. All people witness death daily. He then elaborates on the profound impact of this reality, which silences every tyrant and points to the Oneness of Allah. This lesson explores that foundational claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on death as witnessed
Read the Arabic passage from 'أولا حقائق تعلق بالموت' to 'ولا غالب على أمره'. Follow with the translation.
Notice the poetic language used to describe death's universality.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that death is a 'حقيقة مشاهدة محسوسة' (observable, tangible reality). Underline this phrase and note its contrast with the unseen.
3
Reflect on theological implications
Consider how death itself declares Allah's oneness and sovereignty. What does the author say about tyrants and atheists in the face of death?
This connects the empirical fact to a core Islamic belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولا حقائق تعلق بالموت أما الموت فقد علم الناس كلهم أنه حقيقة مشاهدة محسوسة ، وليس من الغيبيات في شيء . وهو قصة الحقيقة الكبرى في هذا الوجود !.. الحقيقة التي يسقط عندها جبروت المتجبرين وعناد الملحدين ، وطغيان البغاة والمتألهين !.. إنها الحقيقة التي تمد صفحة هذا الوجود المائج ، بغاشية الانتهاء والفناء ، وتصبغ الحياة البشرية كلها بصبغة العبودية والذل القهار السموات والأرض ، حقيقة تسربل بها ، طوعاً أو كرهاً ، العصاة والطائعون ، والرؤساء والمتألهون ، والرسل والأنبياء ، والمقربون والأصفياء ، والأغنياء والفقراء ، وأرباب العلم والاختراع . إنها الحقيقة التي تعلن على مدى الزمان والمكان ، وفي أذن كل سامع وعقل كل مفكر : أن لا ألوهية إلا لذاك الذي تفرد بالبقاء ، فهو الذي لا لقضائه مرد ولا حدود لسلطانه ، ولا مخرج عن حكمه ، ولا غالب على أمره . فهذه الحقيقة ، أمر مشاهد محسوس ، كما قلنا ، ولا علاقة له بالمغيبات غير أن ثمة أموراً أخرى تحيط به من بين يديه ومن خلفه . لا مجال للعلم بها إلا عن طريق الخبر اليقيني الوارد في شأنها : إذ لا تكشف ، على سبيل الحس والمعاينة ، إلا لمن وقع في سياق الموت وأخذ يعاني من سكراته ، ولمن تجاوزه إلى الحياة البرزخية القائمة من وراء الموت . ولذلك كانت هذه الأمور مغيبات
First: Realities related to death. As for death, all people know that it is an observable, tangible reality, and it is not at all among the unseen things. It is the story of the great reality in this existence! The reality before which the tyranny of the tyrants, the obstinacy of the atheists, and the transgression of the oppressors and the would-be gods collapse! It is the reality that spreads over the surface of this surging existence the covering of termination and annihilation, and dyes all of human life with the dye of servitude and overwhelming humility – heavens and earth – a reality that is cloaked, willingly or unwillingly, by the disobedient and the obedient, the leaders and the would-be gods, the messengers and the prophets, the close ones and the chosen ones, the rich and the poor, and the people of knowledge and invention. It is the reality that proclaims throughout time and space, and in the ear of every listener and the mind of every thinker: that there is no divinity except the One who is unique in remaining, for His decree cannot be repelled, there is no limit to His authority, no escape from His judgment, and no one prevails over His command. So this reality is an observable, tangible matter, as we have said, and it has no relation to the unseen. However, there are other matters surrounding it from before and behind. There is no way to know them except through the certain report (al-khabar al-yaqīnī) concerning them: for they are not disclosed, by way of sense perception and direct observation, except to those who have fallen into the context of death and are experiencing its throes (sakarāt), and to those who have passed beyond it to the intervening life (al-ḥayāt al-barzakhiyya) that exists beyond death. Therefore these matters are unseen (ghaybiyyāt).
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion of the first category of unseen realities: those related to death. The author first emphasizes that death itself is not an unseen reality; it is an observable, tangible fact witnessed by all people. He then poetically describes death as the great reality that humbles all tyrants and atheists, and affects all human beings regardless of their status. Death proclaims the oneness of God, the Only Eternal. After affirming that death is a witnessed reality, the author points out that there are other matters surrounding death—what happens before it (the throes of death), and what comes after it (the barzakh, or intermediary life). These cannot be known through sense perception or direct observation except by those who experience death or have passed into the barzakh. Therefore, these surrounding matters are unseen realities (ghaybiyyāt) that can only be known through certain reports from revelation. The passage establishes a clear distinction between the empirical fact of death and the metaphysical events associated with it.

Key Terms
الموت
حقيقة مشاهدة محسوسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Death is entirely an unseen matter and nothing about it is known empirically.
Correction: Death itself is a witnessed reality; it is the events surrounding death (sakarāt and barzakh) that are unseen.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does death proclaim?
A) The power of tyrants
B) The oneness of God
C) The value of wealth
D) The mystery of afterlife

Key Takeaway
Death is the universally witnessed reality that declares the sole divinity and eternal sovereignty of Allah.

Unseen Matters

The Unseen Matters Surrounding Death
Buti explains the unseen events before and after death and their reliance on revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the details of death's throes (sakarāt) and the barzakh life are unseen realities that can only be known through authentic revelation (al-khabar al-yaqīnī).

Core Idea
What happens at death and after it is hidden from the living and known only through revelation.

After affirming that death itself is a witnessed fact, the author turns to the matters that surround it: the throes of death (sakarāt) and the intermediary life (barzakh). These are not observable to the living and fall into the category of the unseen (ghaybiyyāt). This lesson explains why they are considered unseen and how they are known.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on unseen aspects of death
Read the Arabic passage from 'غير أن ثمة أموراً أخرى' to 'مغيبات'. Then read the translation.
Look for the terms سكرات الموت and الحياة البرزخية.
2
Distinguish between death and its surroundings
The author contrasts death itself (observable) with 'أموراً أخرى تحيط به' (other matters surrounding it). Identify these two categories.
The surrounding matters are the sakarāt and barzakh.
3
Understand the source of knowledge
The passage states that these matters are known only through 'الخبر اليقيني' (the certain report). Why is sense perception insufficient?
Only those experiencing death or in barzakh can perceive them directly.

?

?

?

Death: The Witnessed Reality and Its Divine Message
Buti establishes death as a witnessed reality and describes its theological significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why death, though a witnessed reality, serves as a profound sign of Allah's sole divinity and the futility of human arrogance.

Core Idea
Death is the greatest reality that humbles all and proclaims Allah's eternal lordship.

Buti begins by affirming that death is not an unseen matter—it is witnessed by all. Yet its universal nature carries a powerful message about the Creator. This lesson explores Buti's vivid description of death as the reality that strips all pretense of power and divinity from creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on death being witnessed
Read the Arabic passage where Buti states that death is a witnessed reality, not part of the unseen. Pay attention to his confident tone.
Notice the contrast he sets up between death and ghaybiyyat.
2
Reflect on Buti's rhetorical description
Buti describes death as 'the greatest reality' that humbles the arrogant and atheists. Think about the imagery he uses: a veil of end and annihilation, dyeing life with servitude.
He uses strong emotional language to drive the point home.
3
Identify the theological message
Death's universality leads Buti to declare that only Allah is eternal and has absolute authority. This is the central theological lesson from death as a witnessed reality.
This connects death directly to tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولا
حقائق تعلق بالموت
أما الموت فقد علم الناس كلهم أنه حقيقة مشاهدة محسوسة ، وليس من الغيبيات في شيء .
وهو قصة الحقيقة الكبرى في هذا الوجود !.. الحقيقة التي يسقط عندها جبروت المتجبرين وعناد الملحدين ، وطغيان البغاة والمتألهين !.. إنها الحقيقة التي تمد صفحة هذا الوجود المائج ، بغاشية الانتهاء والفناء ، وتصبغ الحياة البشرية كلها بصبغة العبودية والذل القهار السموات والأرض ، حقيقة تسربل بها ، طوعاً أو كرهاً ، العصاة والطائعون ، والرؤساء والمتألهون ، والرسل والأنبياء ، والمقربون والأصفياء ، والأغنياء والفقراء ، وأرباب العلم والاختراع
•
إنها الحقيقة التي تعلن على مدى الزمان والمكان ، وفي أذن كل سامع وعقل كل مفكر : أن لا ألوهية إلا لذاك الذي تفرد بالبقاء ، فهو الذي لا
ولا حدود لسلطانه ، ولا مخرج عن حكمه ، ولا غالب على أمره
(۱)
لقضائه مرد
(1) من كتاب فقه السيرة للمؤلف : ص ٥٣٨ الطبعة الثانية
فهذه الحقيقة ، أمر مشاهد محسوس ، كما قلنا ، ولا علاقة له بالمغيبات غير أن ثمة أموراً أخرى تحيط به من بين يديه ومن خلفه . لا مجال للعلم بها إلا عن طريق الخبر اليقيني الوارد في شأنها : إذ لا تكشف ، على سبيل الحس والمعاينة ، إلا لمن وقع في سياق الموت وأخذ يعاني من سكراته ، ولمن تجاوزه إلى الحياة البرزخية القائمة من وراء الموت . ولذلك كانت هذه الأمور مغيبات
بالنسبة إلينا ، مادمنا لا نزال نسير في معبر هذه الدنيا . ولم نصل بعد إلى هذه
النهاية التي إليها مصير كل حي من المخلوقات
وهذه الأمور الغيبية هي :
أ - ملك الموت وقبضه الأرواح .
ب - سؤال القبر .
ج - عذاب القبر ونعيمه
ولنبدأ في بيان كل منها على حدة .
First: Realities pertaining to death. As for death, all people know that it is a witnessed, tangible reality, and it is not among the unseen matters at all. It is the story of the greatest reality in this existence! The reality before which the tyranny of the arrogant, the obstinacy of the atheists, and the transgression of the oppressors and those who claim divinity fall! It is the reality that extends over the page of this surging existence with a veil of end and annihilation, and dyes all of human life with the dye of servitude and humiliation, the Subjugator of the heavens and the earth, a reality which the disobedient and the obedient, the leaders and those who claim divinity, the messengers and the prophets, the near ones and the pure ones, the rich and the poor, the people of knowledge and invention have donned, willingly or unwillingly. It is the reality that proclaims across time and space, and in the ear of every listener and the mind of every thinker: that there is no divinity except for the One who is unique in eternity, for He is the one who has no limits to His authority, no escape from His judgment, no victor over His command, and to His decree is the return. (1) From the book Fiqh al-Sirah by the author, p. 538, second edition. So this reality is a witnessed, tangible matter, as we said, and has no relation to the unseen. However, there are other matters that surround it from before it and behind it. There is no way to knowledge of them except through the certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini) that has come concerning them, because they are not disclosed by sense and direct observation except to one who has fallen into the throes of death and is suffering its agonies, and to one who has passed beyond it to the barzakh life that lies beyond death. Therefore these matters are unseen (ghaybiyyat) relative to us, as long as we are still walking in the crossing of this world, and have not yet reached this end to which every living creature is destined. And these unseen matters are: A) The Angel of Death and his seizing of souls. B) The questioning of the grave. C) The punishment of the grave and its pleasure. And we will begin to explain each one separately.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the realities related to death. The author begins by affirming that death is a witnessed, tangible reality, known to all people, and not part of the unseen (ghaybiyyat). He then poetically describes death as the greatest reality before which all forms of human arrogance and defiance fall. Death proclaims the exclusive divinity of Allah, Who alone is eternal and has absolute authority. After establishing this, the author pivots to the unseen matters surrounding death. He states that while death itself is witnessed, there are other realities that come before and after it—such as the process of dying, the barzakh life—which cannot be known through the senses but only through certain reports (al-khabar al-yaqini) from revelation. These matters are unseen for us while we are still in this world. He then lists three specific unseen matters: the Angel of Death and his seizing of souls, the questioning of the grave, and the punishment and pleasure of the grave. The passage ends with a statement that each will be explained separately.

Key Terms
الموت
الغيبيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Death is an unseen matter because we don't experience it directly before it happens.
Correction: Buti states that death is a witnessed reality known to all people through observation of others, not an unseen matter.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the main message that death proclaims to humanity?
A) That life is meaningless
B) That only Allah is eternal and has absolute authority
C) That the rich and poor are equal in death
D) That death is a punishment for sin

Key Takeaway
Death is a witnessed, tangible reality that powerfully affirms the exclusive divinity and eternal nature of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever truly confronted the reality of your own death as the certain end that awaits you, and not as a distant abstraction? How would your priorities change today if you lived with that certainty every moment?
?
The passage says death 'dyes all of human life with the dye of servitude and humiliation.' In what specific areas of your life are you still acting as if you are independent of Allah, refusing to accept that dye? Will you surrender those areas to Him today?
?
Death proclaims that there is no divinity except Allah. What other 'divinities'—people, possessions, status, ambitions—are you still clinging to as if they have ultimate power over you? Will you let death's message free you from those attachments before it is too late?

Unseen Matters

Unseen Matters Surrounding Death: The Angel, the Questioning, and the Grave
Buti enumerates the three unseen matters surrounding death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three unseen matters related to death—the Angel of Death, the questioning of the grave, and the punishment/pleasure of the grave—and why they can only be known through revelation.

Core Idea
Details of what happens at and after death are unseen, known only through certain reports.

Buti has established death as a witnessed reality. Now he turns to the realities that accompany it but are hidden from our senses. He lists three specific matters that are ghaybiyyat: the Angel of Death, the grave's questioning, and its reward or punishment. This lesson introduces these and emphasizes that only revelation gives us certain knowledge of them.

Guided Path
1
Read Buti's explanation of unseen matters
Read the passage from 'So this reality is a witnessed matter' to the end. Note how he distinguishes death itself from the surrounding unseen matters.
He says these matters are 'from before it and behind it'.
2
Identify the source of knowledge
Buti states that there is no way to know these matters except through 'al-khabar al-yaqini', the certain report. Understand why sense experience cannot reach them.
Only those who have died or are dying experience them, but they cannot report back to us.
3
List the three unseen matters
Buti enumerates three: the Angel of Death seizing souls, the questioning of the grave, and the punishment/pleasure of the grave. Commit them to memory.
These are foundational beliefs in Islamic eschatology.

It is the story of the greatest reality in this existence! The reality before which the tyranny of the arrogant, the obstinacy of the atheists, and the transgression of the oppressors and those who claim divinity fall! It is the reality that extends over the page of this surging existence with a veil of end and annihilation, and dyes all of human life with the dye of servitude and humiliation, the Subjugator of the heavens and the earth, a reality which the disobedient and the obedient, the leaders and those who claim divinity, the messengers and the prophets, the near ones and the pure ones, the rich and the poor, the people of knowledge and invention have donned, willingly or unwillingly. It is the reality that proclaims across time and space, and in the ear of every listener and the mind of every thinker: that there is no divinity except for the One who is unique in eternity, for He is the one who has no limits to His authority, no escape from His judgment, no victor over His command, and to His decree is the return. (1) From the book Fiqh al-Sirah by the author, p. 538, second edition. So this reality is a witnessed, tangible matter, as we said, and has no relation to the unseen. However, there are other matters that surround it from before it and behind it. There is no way to knowledge of them except through the certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini) that has come concerning them, because they are not disclosed by sense and direct observation except to one who has fallen into the throes of death and is suffering its agonies, and to one who has passed beyond it to the barzakh life that lies beyond death. Therefore these matters are unseen (ghaybiyyat) relative to us, as long as we are still walking in the crossing of this world, and have not yet reached this end to which every living creature is destined. And these unseen matters are: A) The Angel of Death and his seizing of souls. B) The questioning of the grave. C) The punishment of the grave and its pleasure. And we will begin to explain each one separately.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the realities related to death. The author begins by affirming that death is a witnessed, tangible reality, known to all people, and not part of the unseen (ghaybiyyat). He then poetically describes death as the greatest reality before which all forms of human arrogance and defiance fall. Death proclaims the exclusive divinity of Allah, Who alone is eternal and has absolute authority. After establishing this, the author pivots to the unseen matters surrounding death. He states that while death itself is witnessed, there are other realities that come before and after it—such as the process of dying, the barzakh life—which cannot be known through the senses but only through certain reports (al-khabar al-yaqini) from revelation. These matters are unseen for us while we are still in this world. He then lists three specific unseen matters: the Angel of Death and his seizing of souls, the questioning of the grave, and the punishment and pleasure of the grave. The passage ends with a statement that each will be explained separately.

Correction: Buti states that these matters are only known through the certain report of revelation, not through sense experience.

The Angel of Death and Divine Delegation
Buti explains that Allah delegates soul-taking to the Angel of Death, citing Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's delegation of soul-taking to the Angel of Death is consistent with His sole power over life and death, as affirmed by the Quran.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death is Allah's appointed agent, not an independent power.

Buti begins by firmly establishing that Allah alone gives life and takes it. Yet, in His wisdom, He delegates the actual seizing of souls to a specific angel, the Angel of Death. This passage explains the scriptural basis for this delegation and introduces the angel's name, Azrael.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the flow from the general principle to the specific delegation.
The passage begins with a clear affirmation of Allah's sole power.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the two verses cited: 39:42 and 32:11. Understand how the first establishes the general principle and the second specifies the delegation.
Both verses are essential to the argument.
3
Understand the concept of delegation (tawkeel)
Buti compares the delegation of soul-taking to the general pattern of causation in creation. Reflect on why Allah might delegate while remaining the ultimate cause.
This shows the wisdom behind delegation.
4
Recognize the authority of the 'certain report'
The passage calls Quran 32:11 'al-khabar al-yaqini' (the certain report) that does not admit probability. Note that this is a foundational source for this belief.
Certainty is a key concept in kalam.
5
Reflect on the angel's name and significance
Buti mentions that the angel is called 'Angel of Death' by Allah, and in some traditions his name is Azrael (meaning servant of the All-Compelling). Consider why names matter in Islamic theology.
The name reflects the angel's role and subservience.

A) The Angel of Death and his seizing of souls: There is no doubt that the Giver of life and the Taker of life is Allah, Mighty and Majestic. He is the one who takes the souls and causes them to die whenever He wills. In explanation of that, Allah Almighty says: "Allah takes the souls at the time of their death" [az-Zumar: 42]. But the wisdom of Allah Almighty required that He entrust the seizing of souls to one of His close angels, just as His wisdom required that He entrust the existence of His various creatures to created causes which He brought together by a connection of pure will. That has been indicated by the certain report (al-khabar al-yaqini) which does not admit of possibility: the saying of Allah Most High: "Say: The Angel of Death who has been entrusted with you will take you; then to your Lord you will be returned" [as-Sajdah: 11]. A great angel whom Allah named, as you have seen, the Angel of Death. And it has been reported in some traditions that his name is Azrael, meaning servant of the All-Compelling (Abd al-Jabbar). And he is well-known by this name. Mujahid said in...

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the explanation of the first unseen matter: the Angel of Death and his taking of souls. The author starts by affirming a foundational principle: the Giver of life and the Taker of life is solely Allah, Mighty and Majestic. He supports this with Quran 39:42. However, the author then explains that Allah's wisdom required that the actual seizing of souls be entrusted to one of His close angels. This is analogous to the general pattern of causation in creation: Allah creates causes and effects. The proof for this delegation is another Quranic verse, 32:11, which directly states that the Angel of Death will take the souls. The author describes this angel as a great angel, named 'Angel of Death' by Allah. He then mentions that in some traditions (athar), the angel's name is Azrael, meaning 'servant of the All-Compelling' (Abd al-Jabbar), and that this name is well-known. The passage ends abruptly with 'Mujahid said in...' indicating a citation that continues on the next page.

?

The Angel of Death and His Helpers
Discusses the Angel of Death, his helpers, and the ease of death based on one's state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Angel of Death, his angelic assistants, and how the ease or hardship of death relates to a person's faith and deeds, as established by certain reports.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death has helpers, and death's ease reflects one's faith.

This passage from a classical theological work addresses a fundamental question about the Angel of Death: does he work alone or with assistants? It presents the majority view, supported by Quranic verses, and then connects the circumstances of death to a person's spiritual state. As you read, notice how the author moves from description to evidence to practical implication, always grounding the discussion in scriptural authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's flow of thought—description, question, answer, evidence, elaboration, and conclusion—sink in.
2
Identify the core question and answer
Find where the author poses the question about helpers and states the majority view. Notice how he frames it as a matter of ijtihad (scholarly reflection).
The question is: 'Does he have assistants or is the matter solely to him?'
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Look at the two Quranic verses cited (4:97 and 6:61). Understand how each supports the existence of multiple angels involved in taking souls.
The first verse mentions 'angels' (plural) taking the souls of wrongdoers; the second says 'Our messengers' take the soul.
4
Reflect on the roles of the Angel of Death and his helpers
Note the author's explanation: the Angel of Death seizes, the assistants extract, and God causes the soul to depart. This clarifies the division of labor.
5
Consider the hadiths on ease and harshness of death
The passage adds that the ease or harshness of death corresponds to one's righteousness or sin, though it is not an absolute law. Ask yourself why this might be the case and how it reinforces the importance of faith.
The passage stresses that these are unseen realities to be believed with certainty due to certain reports.

وصفه : طويت له الأرض فجعلت مثل الطست يتناول منها متى يشاء ، قال ابن كثير : ورواه زهير بن محمد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، مرسلاً ، وقاله ابن عباس أيضا) ولكن ، هل له أعوان من الملائكة يعالجون نزع الأرواح من أجسادها ، أم الأمر كله موكول إليه وحده ؟ والجواب ، أن هذه المسألة داخلة في حيز الاجتهاد والنظر ، والذي ذهب إليه الجمهور أن لملك الموت أعواناً كثيرين من الملائكة أقامهم الله عز وجل معه في هذا الأمر . ودليل ذلك قوله تعالى : إنَّ الَّذِينَ تَوَفَّاهُمُ المَلائِكَةُ ظَالِمِي أَنفُسهمْ ، قالوا فيمَ كُنتُم .. ) [ النساء : ٩٧ ] الآية . وقوله تعالى : ﴿ حَتَّى إذا جاءَ أَحَدَكُمُ الموتُ تَوَفَّتُهُ رُسُلُنَا وَهُم لا يُفَرِّطُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٦١ ] . والمعنى : أن الله تعالى خلق ملك الموت وجعل على يديه قبض الأرواح وانتزاعها من الأجسام وإخراجها منها ، وخلق الله تعالى جنداً يكونون معه يعملون عملـه بأمره . فملك الموت يقبض ، والأعوان يعالجون ، والله تعالى يزهق الروح" (۲) ثم إن متفرقات الأحاديث والآثار دلت على أن الإنسان كلما كان أصلح حالاً أثناء حياته ، كان ملك الموت به أرفق وكان الموت عليه أهون . وكلما كان الإنسان أوغل في السوء والعصيان أثناء حياته كان الملك في معالجته أغلظ وكان الموت عليه أشد على أن هذا ليس قانوناً دائماً فهذه أولى الحقائق الغيبية المتعلقة بالموت ، وعلى المسلم أن يعتقد بها اعتقاداً جازماً لورود الخبر اليقيني بها .
His description: The earth was folded for him so it became like a basin from which he takes whenever he wills. Ibn Kathir said: Zuhayr ibn Muhammad narrated it from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, as a mursal report, and Ibn Abbas also said it. But does he have assistants from the angels who undertake the extraction of souls from their bodies, or is the matter entirely entrusted to him alone? The answer: This issue falls within the domain of ijtihad and reflection. The view held by the majority is that the Angel of Death has many assistants from the angels whom God Almighty has appointed with him in this matter. The evidence for that is His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, those whom the angels take in death while they are wronging themselves, they will say, "In what [condition] were you?"' [Quran 4:97] and His statement, the Exalted: 'Until when death comes to one of you, Our messengers take him, and they do not fail [in their duties]' [Quran 6:61]. The meaning: God Almighty created the Angel of Death and placed at his hands the seizure of souls, their extraction from bodies, and their removal from them, and God Almighty created a host who are with him carrying out his work by His command. So the Angel of Death seizes, the assistants undertake the extraction, and God Almighty causes the soul to depart. Then the scattered hadiths and reports indicate that the more righteous a person is during his life, the gentler the Angel of Death is with him and the easier death is for him. And the more a person is deeply engaged in evil and disobedience during his life, the harsher the angel is in his treatment and the more severe death is for him, although this is not an absolute law. These are the first of the unseen realities related to death, and it is incumbent upon the Muslim to believe in them with firm conviction because of the certain report that has come regarding them.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation about the Angel of Death and the circumstances of death. It begins by quoting a description of the Angel of Death: that the earth is folded for him like a basin, so he can take from wherever he wishes. It then raises a question: does the Angel of Death have angelic assistants who physically extract souls, or is he alone responsible? The author states that this is a matter of scholarly investigation (ijtihad). The majority view (jumhur) is that the Angel of Death has many assistants appointed by God. Evidence is provided from two Quranic verses: Surah an-Nisa (4:97) speaks of angels taking the souls of wrongdoers, and Surah al-An'am (6:61) mentions messengers (rusul) who take souls. The author explains that God created the Angel of Death to grasp souls and created a host of assistants who work with him: the Angel of Death seizes, the assistants undertake the extraction, and God causes the soul to depart. The passage then adds a secondary point from scattered hadiths and reports: the ease or harshness of death corresponds to the person's state of righteousness or sin, though this is not an absolute law. The passage concludes by affirming that these are unseen realities that a Muslim must believe with certainty because they are established by certain reports (al-khabar al-yaqini).

The Nature of the Grave Questioning
Describes the ordeal of the grave questioning and its outcomes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the grave questioning as described by Islamic teachings, including the role of the two angels and the differing responses of believers and disbelievers.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is a real trial where only true faith inspires the correct answer.

After death, every soul is tested. Two angels appear in a terrifying form to ask about one's faith in this world. This passage from al-Buti explains what happens to the believer and the disbeliever during this trial.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the grave questioning
Read the opening lines of the passage that describe what happens after death. Notice the two angels and their appearance.
2
Compare the believer and the disbeliever
See how each responds and what God does for them. The believer is made firm and inspired; the disbeliever is terrified and unable to answer.
This contrast shows the importance of faith during life.
3
Reflect on the unseen nature
The passage says this is an unseen reality. Ask yourself why it is important to believe in it even though we cannot observe it.

عبد
B - The Question of the Grave:
When a person dies, God sends to him two angels in a terrifying, frightening form, and they ask him about the religion he lived upon and about his knowledge of this man he heard about, namely Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. Whoever God has made firm with the firm word, died upon the truth, and was sealed with goodness, God inspires him with the answer to the two angels' question, without being affected by anything of their terrifying appearance. And whoever was not clinging to the rope of faith in his worldly life, died upon what he lived upon of amusement, disobedience, and turning away from the truth, God fills his heart with terror from them, so the required answer disappears from his mind and he gives no answer to what they say.
These are among the unseen realities that no one perceives except one who has reached that fate, and each of us is about to reach it. Many authentic hadiths, which in their totality reach the level of tawatur, have indicated them. Therefore, all Muslims have reached consensus on believing in that according to what the certain report indicates.
Among the hadiths reported in that regard is what al-Bukhari and Muslim and others narrated: that the Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace, once led the people in the eclipse prayer, then stood up, praised God, and then said: 'There is nothing I had not seen that I did not see in this place of mine, even Paradise and Hell. And it has been revealed to me that you will be tried in the graves like or close to the trial of the Dajjal. One of you will be brought and it will be said to him: "What is your knowledge of this man?" As for the believer or the certain one—a variation by the narrators—he says: "He is Muhammad, the Messenger of God; he brought us clear proofs and guidance, so we responded, believed, and followed." It will be said to him: "Sleep in peace; we knew you were a believer." As for the hypocrite or the doubter—also a variation—he says: "I do not know, I heard the people saying something and I said it."
That is what the two Shaykhs narrated with their chains that the Prophet said: 'When the servant is placed in his grave and his companions depart, and he indeed hears the sound of their sandals, two angels come to him, make him sit up, and say to him: "What did you used to say about this man?" As for the believer, he says: "I bear witness that he is God's servant and His messenger." He said: It will be said to him: "Look at your seat in Hell; it has been replaced for you with a seat in Paradise."'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the trial of the grave (fitnat al-qabr). It begins by describing that after death, God sends two terrifying angels who ask the deceased about his religion and about the Prophet Muhammad. For those whom God has made firm (al-qawl al-thabit), they are inspired with the correct answer and are not frightened by the angels' appearance. For those who lived in sin and disbelief, their hearts are filled with terror and they fail to answer. The author emphasizes that this is an unseen reality (haqiqa ghaybiyya) that each person will experience. The passage then notes that many authentic hadiths, reaching the level of tawatur (indisputable mass transmission), support this, leading to unanimous consensus (ijma') among Muslims. Two hadiths are cited: the first from Bukhari and Muslim about the eclipse prayer and the trial of the grave, where the Prophet describes the questioning and the answers of the believer and the hypocrite; the second is also from Bukhari and Muslim (al-Shaykhan) describing the two angels who make the deceased sit up and ask about the Prophet, and the believer's response leads to his seat in Hell being replaced with Paradise. The passage thus grounds the belief in the grave questioning in scriptural sources and consensus.

Correction: The passage affirms it is a real unseen event based on certain proof.

Scriptural Proofs for the Grave Questioning
Provides the scriptural and consensual basis for the grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the belief in the grave questioning is established through mutawatir hadith and unanimous consensus of the Muslim community.

Core Idea
Certainty in unseen matters comes from multiple, mutually reinforcing chains of narration.

How do we know the grave questioning is real? The author explains that the hadith on this topic have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission), leading to consensus. Two key hadiths are cited to demonstrate this.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of tawatur
Read how the author says many hadiths in their totality reach tawatur. This means they are undeniably authentic.
Tawatur is the strongest form of hadith authentication.
2
Read the first hadith from the eclipse prayer
This hadith from Bukhari and Muslim reports the Prophet's description of the grave trial. Note the answers of the believer and hypocrite.
3
Read the second hadith about the two angels
This hadith gives more detail: the angels make the deceased sit up and ask about Muhammad. The believer's response leads to Paradise.
Both hadiths confirm the same reality.
4
Connect to consensus
The author states that all Muslims have agreed on this belief. Why does consensus matter in Islamic theology?
Consensus is a source of certainty.

عبد
B - The Question of the Grave:
When a person dies, God sends to him two angels in a terrifying, frightening form, and they ask him about the religion he lived upon and about his knowledge of this man he heard about, namely Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. Whoever God has made firm with the firm word, died upon the truth, and was sealed with goodness, God inspires him with the answer to the two angels' question, without being affected by anything of their terrifying appearance. And whoever was not clinging to the rope of faith in his worldly life, died upon what he lived upon of amusement, disobedience, and turning away from the truth, God fills his heart with terror from them, so the required answer disappears from his mind and he gives no answer to what they say.
These are among the unseen realities that no one perceives except one who has reached that fate, and each of us is about to reach it. Many authentic hadiths, which in their totality reach the level of tawatur, have indicated them. Therefore, all Muslims have reached consensus on believing in that according to what the certain report indicates.
Among the hadiths reported in that regard is what al-Bukhari and Muslim and others narrated: that the Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace, once led the people in the eclipse prayer, then stood up, praised God, and then said: 'There is nothing I had not seen that I did not see in this place of mine, even Paradise and Hell. And it has been revealed to me that you will be tried in the graves like or close to the trial of the Dajjal. One of you will be brought and it will be said to him: "What is your knowledge of this man?" As for the believer or the certain one—a variation by the narrators—he says: "He is Muhammad, the Messenger of God; he brought us clear proofs and guidance, so we responded, believed, and followed." It will be said to him: "Sleep in peace; we knew you were a believer." As for the hypocrite or the doubter—also a variation—he says: "I do not know, I heard the people saying something and I said it."
That is what the two Shaykhs narrated with their chains that the Prophet said: 'When the servant is placed in his grave and his companions depart, and he indeed hears the sound of their sandals, two angels come to him, make him sit up, and say to him: "What did you used to say about this man?" As for the believer, he says: "I bear witness that he is God's servant and His messenger." He said: It will be said to him: "Look at your seat in Hell; it has been replaced for you with a seat in Paradise."'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the trial of the grave (fitnat al-qabr). It begins by describing that after death, God sends two terrifying angels who ask the deceased about his religion and about the Prophet Muhammad. For those whom God has made firm (al-qawl al-thabit), they are inspired with the correct answer and are not frightened by the angels' appearance. For those who lived in sin and disbelief, their hearts are filled with terror and they fail to answer. The author emphasizes that this is an unseen reality (haqiqa ghaybiyya) that each person will experience. The passage then notes that many authentic hadiths, reaching the level of tawatur (indisputable mass transmission), support this, leading to unanimous consensus (ijma') among Muslims. Two hadiths are cited: the first from Bukhari and Muslim about the eclipse prayer and the trial of the grave, where the Prophet describes the questioning and the answers of the believer and the hypocrite; the second is also from Bukhari and Muslim (al-Shaykhan) describing the two angels who make the deceased sit up and ask about the Prophet, and the believer's response leads to his seat in Hell being replaced with Paradise. The passage thus grounds the belief in the grave questioning in scriptural sources and consensus.

Correction: It is based on many authentic hadiths reaching tawatur and unanimous consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Not based on your upbringing or what people say, but on your own conviction—would your answer be 'I know he is the Messenger of God' or 'I don't know, I just said what others said'? What concrete step can you take before the day ends to strengthen your knowledge of Muhammad and his message so that your answer in the grave is one of certainty?
?
You will experience the grave questioning alone. No one will answer for you. If you were to die tonight, would you face the angels with confidence or with hesitation? What is the one thing you need to change or learn so that you can say 'I bear witness that he is God's servant and messenger' with absolute sincerity?

Universality of Grave Questioning (Answer to an Objection)
Author proves grave questioning applies to all dead, answers objection, quotes Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the questioning in the grave applies to all deceased, regardless of burial, and how the answer to the objection relies on the principle of possibility and the unseen nature of spiritual realities.

Core Idea
Grave questioning is universal; Allah can restore life to any particles, wherever they are.

In this passage, the author establishes that the questioning in the grave is not limited to those physically buried. He addresses a common objection: how can questioning occur if the body is destroyed? The answer lies in understanding that what is possible for Allah includes restoring life to scattered particles, and that the afterlife belongs to a different order of existence, beyond physical perception. The author supports this with a quotation from Imam al-Ghazali.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
First, read the Arabic passage aloud if possible, then the translation. Notice the author's argumentative style: he states the evidence, clarifies a point, raises an objection, and replies.
Pay attention to the phrase 'تغليباً' (by predominance) – it's key to understanding why the grave is mentioned.
2
Identify the objection and answer
Locate the objection (فإن قلت) and the answer (والجواب). The objection questions how questioning can happen if the body is destroyed. The answer invokes the category of the possible (الممكنات) and distinguishes between what is impossible and what is merely unfamiliar.
Notice the author's use of 'غاية الأمر' to indicate the core of the answer.
3
Analyze the principle of possibility
The author argues that the matter falls within the realm of possibilities (الممكنات). Reflect on the distinction between something being logically impossible (مستحيل) and something being possible but unfamiliar (ممكن غير مألوف). The author gives examples of scattered particles.
This principle is central to rational theology (ilm al-kalam) – nothing is impossible for Allah except logical contradictions.
4
Examine the Ghazali quote
The author quotes Imam al-Ghazali to support the answer. Ghazali argues that the physical eye is not suited for perceiving the malakut (celestial realm), just as the Companions believed in Jibril without seeing him. This reinforces that the dead can perceive angels without physical sight.
Consider the analogy: if you accept that the Prophet saw Jibril while others did not, why not accept that the dead see angels in a different state?
5
Connect to the key takeaway
The passage concludes that questioning is universal for all deceased. The ascription to the grave is by predominance, not exclusivity. The key is that Allah can restore life to any particles, and the afterlife operates on a different order.
This resolves the common misunderstanding that only buried people experience grave questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا هو دليل التواتر الذي لا يقبل الريب أو الاحتمال. ثم إن إسناد السؤال إلى القبر جار على وجه التغليب إذ غالب من يموتون يدفنون في القبور، فيكون سؤال الملكين بالنسبة إليهم في القبر بعد أن يتولى عنهم أصحابهم كما قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. فأسند السؤال إلى القبر تغليباً. وإلا فلا جرم أنه شيء ثابت بالنسبة لكل من مات سواء دفن في القبر أم غرق في البحر أم أكلته السباع أم التهمته النيران. فإن قلت: ولكن كيف يتم السؤال والجواب رغم موته في هذه الأحوال كلها؟ والجواب أن الأمر داخل في حيز الممكنات، وليس من قبيل المستحيلات. غاية الأمر أن من الممكنات أموراً لم نشاهدها ولم نتعود على تصورها وهضم كيفيتها، ومنها ما ذللته المشاهدة والرؤية المستمرة، فيتخيل الإنسان لأول وهلة أن الأول مستحيل والثاني وحده الممكن. فليس عسيراً على الله جل جلاله أن يعكس الحياة مرة أخرى على ذرات الجسم سواء كانت مجتمعة في قبر، أم موزعة في فلاة أم متفرقة في بطن سبع، بذلك السؤال والجواب، ويرى الملك الذي يسأله ويكلمه. وليس ثمة مطمع في أن تعلم كيفية ذلك تحليلاً، إذ إن حقائق ما بعد الموت متعلقة بنظام آخر مختلف كل الاختلاف عن نظام هذا العالم المرئي للأحياء، ولننقل لك في بيان هذه المسألة ما يقوله الإمام الغزالي رحمه الله: إن هذه العين لا تصلح لمشاهدة الأمور الملكوتية، وكل ما يتعلق بالآخرة فهو من عالم الملكوت. أما ترى الصحابة رضي الله عنهم كيف كانوا يؤمنون بنزول جبريل، وما كانوا يشاهدونه، ويؤمنون بأنه عليه السلام يشاهده. فإن كنت لا تؤمن بهذا فتصحيح أصل الإيمان بالملائكة والوحي أهم عليك، وإن كنت آمنت به وجوزت أنه يشاهد النبي مالا تشاهده الأمة فكيف لا تجوز هذا في الميت؟
This is the evidence of tawatur (تواتر) that does not admit doubt or possibility. Then indeed, ascribing the questioning to the grave is done by way of predominance, since most of those who die are buried in graves. So the questioning of the two angels is with respect to them in the grave after their relatives have taken charge of them, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said. So the questioning was ascribed to the grave by way of predominance. Otherwise, there is no doubt that it is a matter established for everyone who dies, whether buried in the grave, or drowned in the sea, or eaten by beasts, or consumed by fire. If you say: But how does the questioning and answer take place despite his death in all these cases? The answer is that the matter falls within the realm of possibilities (mumkinat), not impossibilities. The only thing is that among possibilities there are things we have not witnessed and are not accustomed to conceiving and digesting their modality, and among them are things that constant observation and sight have tamed. So a person imagines at first glance that the first is impossible and the second alone is possible. So it is not difficult for Allah, Exalted is His Majesty, to restore life again to the particles of the body, whether they are gathered in a grave, or scattered in a desert, or dispersed in the stomach of a predator, for that questioning and answer, and he sees the angel who questions him and speaks to him. And there is no hope of knowing the modality of that through analysis, for the realities of the afterlife are related to another system completely different from the system of this visible world of the living. And we will convey to you in explaining this matter what Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah have mercy on him) says: 'Indeed, this eye is not fit for observing the malakut (ملكوت) matters, and everything related to the afterlife is from the world of malakut. Do you not see the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, how they believed in the descent of Jibril, and they did not see him, and they believed that he (peace be upon him) saw him? If you do not believe in this, then correcting the foundation of belief in the angels and revelation is more important for you. And if you believe in it and allow that he sees the Prophet what the ummah does not see, then how do you not allow this in the case of the dead?'
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author first asserts that the established truth about the questioning in the grave applies to all dead, regardless of burial. He clarifies that ascribing the questioning to the grave is by predominance, not exclusivity. He then raises an objection: how can questioning occur if the body is destroyed by drowning, predators, or fire? The answer relies on the principle of possibility (mumkinat): what is possible for Allah includes restoring life to the particles wherever they are. The author distinguishes between what is impossible and what is merely unfamiliar, and he supports his answer by quoting Imam al-Ghazali, who argues that the physical eye cannot perceive spiritual realities, just as the Companions believed in Jibril without seeing him. Thus, the dead can see and hear the angels through a different order of existence.

السؤال في القبر
الممكنات

Misconception: Only those physically buried in a grave experience the questioning in the grave.
Correction: The questioning is universal for all deceased; the ascription to the grave is by predominance because most are buried, but Allah can restore life to any particles.

Key Takeaway

Evidence for Punishment and Bliss of the Grave
Author introduces the reality of grave punishment and bliss, citing Quranic verses as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment and bliss of the grave are proven by certain mutawatir reports, particularly Quranic verses, and how the author addresses potential objections.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is an unseen reality proven by certain reports, not reason.

In this passage, the author introduces a new topic: the punishment and bliss of the grave. He immediately establishes that these are unseen realities that can only be known through certain transmitted reports (khabr yaqini mutawatir). As a sample of such evidence, he cites two Quranic verses that describe the anguish of death for wrongdoers. He then addresses a potential objection: the verses speak about the moment of death, not the grave. He argues that this does not weaken the evidence, because the death experience is part of the broader reality of afterlife punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the author's method: he states a principle, then provides evidence.
The author calls these 'unseen realities' (حقائق غيبية) which require special evidence.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Locate the two Quranic citations. Understand the context of each: Surah Al-An'am 6:93 and Surah Muhammad 47:27. Both describe the angels striking the wrongdoers at death.
3
Understand the objection and response
The author anticipates that someone might say these verses are about death, not the grave. His response is that this does not damage the proof because the death experience is connected to grave punishment.
The footnote refers to al-Ghazali's Ihya' for further discussion.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why is it important that the author starts with the claim that these are unseen realities? This sets the epistemological framework: we rely on revelation, not reason.

ج - عذاب القبر ونعيمه : وهما من الحقائق الغيبية التي ثبت الدليل عليها أيضاً بالخبر اليقيني المتواتر. ولنذكر لك طائفة من هذه الأخبار، إذ هي العمدة في موقفنا من المغيبات التي لا مجال للمشاهدة والعقل في الخوض فيها. 1 - يقول الله تعالى: ( ولو ترى إذ الظالمون في غمرات الموت والملائكة باسطوا أيديهم أخرجوا أنفسكم، اليوم تجزون عذاب الهون ) [الأنعام: 93]. ومثله قوله تعالى: ( فكيف إذا توفتهم الملائكة يضربون وجوههم وأدبارهم ) [محمد: 27]. ولا يخدش في دلالة الآيتين على ما نقول، أن العذاب كائن - في (1) إحياء علوم الدين: 4-500
C - Punishment and Bliss of the Grave: Both are among the unseen realities whose evidence has been established also by certain (يقيني) mutawatir report. And we will mention for you a group of these reports, for they are the mainstay in our position regarding the unseen matters for which there is no room for observation and intellect to delve into. 1 - Allah the Exalted says: 'And if you could see when the wrongdoers are in the agonies of death and the angels extend their hands, "Discharge your souls! Today you will be awarded the punishment of humiliation."' [Al-An'am: 93]. And similar is His saying: 'Then how will it be when the angels take them in death, striking their faces and their backs?' [Muhammad: 27]. And the fact that the punishment occurs at [the time of death] does not mar the indication of the two verses regarding what we say, that the punishment is – in (1) Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din: 4-500.

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section on the punishment and bliss of the grave. The author declares that both are unseen realities proven by certain mutawatir (متواتر) reports. He then begins listing these reports, starting with two Quranic verses. The first verse (Quran 6:93) describes the agony of death for wrongdoers, with angels striking them. The second verse (Quran 47:27) similarly describes angels striking faces and backs at death. The author preemptively notes that these verses describe punishment at death, not specifically in the grave, but he argues that this does not detract from their proof of grave punishment, because the death experience is part of the broader reality of the afterlife. The passage ends with a footnote reference to al-Ghazali's Ihya'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The verses describe the agony of death and the angels striking the wrongdoers. If you were in that moment, what would you wish you had done differently? Write one concrete action you will take today to prepare for that hour.
?
The author emphasizes that these unseen realities are known only through reports, not reason. Where in your life do you rely more on your own reasoning than on what Allah and His Messenger have told you? Are you willing to submit even when you cannot see?
?
Imagine you are the one being told 'Discharge your souls!' because of your own wrongdoings. Does that thought change how you treat others today? What is one relationship you need to mend before death arrives?

The Reality of Resurrection and the Unseen Grave
Al-Buti argues for the reality of resurrection and the unseen nature of the grave's questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the events of the grave and resurrection must be accepted as unseen realities beyond scientific analysis, based on the same principle that underlies belief in angels and revelation.

Core Idea
Belief in the unseen grave follows the same logic as belief in angels.

This lesson tackles a common doubt: how can we believe in events like resurrection and the questioning in the grave if we cannot perceive them? Al-Buti explains that Allah can easily restore life, but the deeper point is that these realities belong to a completely different order—the malakut (angelic realm). He quotes Imam al-Ghazali, who argues that the physical eye is not suited for such matters, just as the Companions believed in Jibril's descent without seeing him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the main claim: Allah can restore life, and the deceased experiences question and answer with an angel.
Pay attention to how al-Buti shifts from the physical possibility to the epistemological barrier.
2
Identify the epistemological argument
Al-Buti says 'there is no hope in knowing how that is analytically.' He argues that the afterlife follows a completely different system from the visible world. This is a key point.
Why is analysis impossible? Because the afterlife is not part of this worldly system.
3
Analyze al-Ghazali's analogy
Al-Ghazali says the eye is not fit for malakut. He uses the Companions as an example: they believed the Prophet saw Jibril without seeing him themselves. If you accept that, you should accept that the deceased sees the angel.
The analogy links belief in unseen grave events to belief in revelation itself.
4
Reflect on the principle
The underlying principle is that we must accept unseen realities when confirmed by revelation. This is not blind faith but a rational extension of our belief in the unseen aspects of Islam.
Consider: if you deny the grave's events, you might undermine your belief in angels and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فليس عسيراً على الله جل جلاله أن يعكس الحياة مرة أخرى على ذرات الجسم سواء كانت مجتمعة في قبر، أم موزعة في فلاة أم متفرقة في بطن سبع بذلك السؤال والجواب، ويرى الملك الذي يسأله ويكلمه. وليس ثمة مطمع في أن تعلم كيفية ذلك تحليلاً، إذ إن حقائق ما بعد الموت متعلقة بنظام آخر مختلف كل الاختلاف عن نظام هذا العالم المرئي للأحياء، ولننقل لك في بيان هذه المسألة ما يقوله الإمام الغزالي رحمه الله: إن هذه العين لا تصلح لمشاهدة الأمور الملكوتية، وكل ما يتعلق بالآخرة فهو من عالم الملكوت. أما ترى الصحابة رضي الله عنهم كيف كانوا يؤمنون بنزول جبريل، وما كانوا يشاهدونه، ويؤمنون بأنه عليه السلام يشاهده. فإن كنت لا تؤمن بهذا فتصحيح أصل الإيمان بالملائكة والوحي أهم عليك، وإن كنت آمنت به وجوزت أنه يشاهد النبي مالا تشاهده الأمة فكيف لا تجوز هذا في الميت؟
It is not difficult for Allah, exalted be His majesty, to revert life again to the atoms of the body, whether they are gathered in a grave, or scattered in a desert, or dispersed in the belly of a beast, with that question and answer, and he sees the angel who questions him and speaks to him. And there is no hope in knowing how that is analytically, for the realities of the afterlife are related to another system completely different from the system of this visible world of the living. And we will quote for you in explaining this issue what Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'This eye is not fit to observe the malakut (angelic realm) matters, and everything related to the Hereafter is from the world of malakut. Do you not see the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) how they used to believe in the descent of Jibril, and they did not see him, and they believed that he (peace be upon him) sees him? If you do not believe in this, then correcting the foundation of belief in angels and revelation is more important for you. And if you believe in it and accept that he sees what the nation does not see, then why do you not accept this regarding the deceased?'
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage argues for the reality of resurrection and the questioning in the grave from an epistemological perspective. The author first states that it is easy for Allah to restore life to atoms regardless of their location, and that the deceased perceives the angel of death and answers questions. He then emphasizes that the exact nature of these events cannot be known through analysis because the afterlife follows a completely different order from the visible world. To clarify, he quotes Imam al-Ghazali: the physical eye is incapable of perceiving the malakut (angelic realm); every afterlife matter belongs to that realm. Al-Ghazali draws an analogy with the Companions: they believed in Jibril's descent without seeing him, and they believed that the Prophet saw him. If one cannot accept that the deceased sees what the living cannot, then the very foundation of belief in angels and revelation is at stake. Thus, the argument is that belief in unseen realities, including the grave's events, is required by the same principle that underlies belief in revelation.

Key Terms
السؤال والجواب
الملكوت
جبريل
العين لا تصلح
نظام آخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The events of the grave (questioning, seeing angels) can be scientifically analyzed or empirically verified.
Correction: The passage clarifies that these events belong to a completely different system (malakut) that is beyond sensory perception; they must be accepted through revelation, not analysis.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali's quote, why should we accept that the deceased sees the angel even though we cannot see it?
A) Because it is physically proven.
B) Because the Companions saw the Prophet seeing Jibril, and the same principle applies to the deceased.
C) Because everyone sees it in the grave.
D) Because the eye can be trained to see angels.

Key Takeaway
The events of the grave and resurrection are unseen realities that must be accepted by the same principle of faith that accepts angels and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you honestly say that your belief in the events of the grave is as firm as your belief in angels? If not, what does that reveal about your reliance on sensory evidence over revelation? Today, commit to strengthening your iman in all unseen matters by reflecting on the principle al-Ghazali lays out.
?
When you think about your own grave and the questioning that awaits, do you find yourself demanding proof or comfort from the physical world? How does the lesson's reminder that the afterlife belongs to a different system challenge you to trust Allah's word alone? What practical step can you take to make that trust more real?
?
The Companions believed that the Prophet saw Jibril without seeing him themselves. Do you accept that same principle for the deceased? If there is any hesitation, what is its root? Pray to Allah to remove that hesitation and to grant you true, unshakeable faith in the unseen.
