وَقُلْنَا إِنَّ الْمَيْتَ يَتَعَرَّضُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِمَّا لِلَوْنٍ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ أَوْ لِلَوْنٍ مِنَ النَّعِيمِ. وَأَوْضَحْنَا أَنَّ الْبُرْهَانَ الْعِلْمِيَّ فِي هَذَا، هُوَ عَيْنُ الْبُرْهَانِ الْعِلْمِيِّ الْمُتَعَلِّقِ بِوُجُودِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَبِنُبُوَّةِ مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وَبِأَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ الْمُعْجِزَ كَلامُ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، وَأَنَّ الْعَقْلَ لَا يَحْتَاجُ - بَعْدَ أَنْ يَسْتَيْقِنَ كُلَّ ذَلِكَ - إِلَّا إِلَى الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى خَبَرٍ مَوْصُولِ السَّنَدِ إِلَى الْقُرْآنِ أَوِ السُّنَّةِ يَرْتَقِي فِي تَعْدَادِ طُرُقِهِ إِلَى التَّوَاتُرِ لِيَكْتَسِبَ دَرَجَةَ الْيَقِينِ وَالْقَطْعِ فِي حُكْمِ الْعَقْلِ. وَلَقَدْ رَأَيْتَ الْخَبَرَ الْمُتَوَاتِرَ عَنِ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ، قَاضِيًا بِثُبُوتِ كُلٍّ مِنْ سُؤَالِ الْقَبْرِ وَعَذَابِهِ، فَلَا يَسَعُكَ، وَقَدْ آمَنْتَ بِكُلِّ مَا مَرَّ ذِكْرُهُ فِي قِسْمِ الإِلَهِيَّاتِ وَالنُّبُوَّاتِ، إِلَّا أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِمَضْمُونِ هَذِهِ الأَخْبَارِ الْمُتَوَاتِرَةِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّكَ قَدْ عَلِمْتَ بِأَنَّ السُّؤَالَ وَالْعَذَابَ وَارِدَانِ عَلَى رُوحِ الْمَيِّتِ بِيَقِينٍ، إِذْ لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ بِدُونِ ذَلِكَ خِطَابٌ أَوْ نَعِيمٌ أَوْ عَذَابٌ، وَإِذًا فَالرُّوحُ مَشْغُولَةٌ بِصَاحِبِهَا مَحْبُوسَةٌ لَهُ أَوْ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: {كُلُّ نَفْسٍ بِمَا كَسَبَتْ رَهِينَةٌ} [المدثر: 38] وَلَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ تَنْصَرِفَ مُوَلِّيَةً عَنْهُ لِتَسْكُنَ جَسَدًا آخَرَ تَسْتَقْبِلُ فِيهِ سُلُوكًا جَدِيدًا وَوُجُودًا آخَرَ بَدِيعًا. وَلَا يُمْكِنُ لِأَيِّ عَاقِلٍ أَنْ يَجْمَعَ عَلَى فِكْرِهِ كُلًّا مِنَ الإِيمَانِ بِالتَّنَاسُخِ، وَالإِيمَانِ بِمَا يَكُونُ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ مِنَ السُّؤَالِ وَالْعَذَابِ، إِذْ هُمَا مُتَنَاقِضَانِ تَنَاقُضًا وَاضِحًا: فَلَا جَرَمَ أَنَّ الإِيمَانَ بِأَحَدِهِمَا مَظْهَرُ إِنْكَارِ الآخَرِ. فَهَذَا هُوَ الدَّلِيلُ الْخَبَرِيُّ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ التَّنَاسُخِ.
And we said that the deceased is exposed after that either to a kind of torment or a kind of bliss. And we explained that the scientific proof for this is the very same scientific proof related to the existence of Allah Almighty and the prophethood of Muhammad peace be upon him, and that the miraculous Quran is the speech of Allah Almighty, and that the intellect does not need - after it is certain of all that - except to come upon a report whose chain is connected to the Quran or Sunnah, whose paths rise in number to tawatur (mass transmission) to acquire the degree of certainty and decisiveness in the judgment of the intellect. And indeed you have seen the mutawatir (massively transmitted) report from the Book and Sunnah, deciding the establishment of both the questioning of the grave and its punishment. So it is not possible for you, having believed in everything mentioned in the section on Divinity and Prophethood, except to believe in the content of these mutawatir reports. Then you have known that the questioning and torment occur upon the soul of the deceased with certainty, for without that no address, bliss, or torment can be conceived. And thus the soul is occupied with its companion, imprisoned for it or against it, as Allah Almighty said: {Every soul is held in pledge for what it earns} [al-Muddaththir: 38]. And it cannot turn away from it to dwell in another body to receive a new conduct and another novel existence. And it is not possible for any rational person to combine in his thought both belief in reincarnation and belief in what occurs after death of questioning and torment, for they are clearly contradictory: inevitably, belief in one is a manifestation of denial of the other. So this is the transmitted proof from the Book and Sunnah for the invalidity of reincarnation.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted proof (dalil khabari) for the reality of the grave's questioning and punishment, and consequently refutes reincarnation. The author begins by reminding that the deceased faces either torment or bliss after death. He states that the scientific proof for this is identical to the proof for God's existence, prophethood, and the miraculous Quran. After certainty in those fundamentals, the intellect needs only a report connected to Quran or Sunnah that reaches tawatur (mass transmission) to attain certainty. He then asserts that there is a mutawatir report from Quran and Sunnah establishing the questioning and punishment of the grave, so anyone who believes in the earlier sections (Ilahiyyat and Nubuwwat) must also believe in these reports. Next, he explains that the soul is attached to the body, as per Quran 74:38, and cannot leave to inhabit another body. Therefore, belief in reincarnation (tanasukh) is contradictory to belief in the grave's events; one implies denial of the other. He concludes that this is the transmitted proof from Quran and Sunnah for the invalidity of reincarnation.

الدليل الخبري
سؤال القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the grave's punishment is not proven by revelation but only by rational inference.
Correction: The passage shows it is proven by mutawatir transmitted reports, which are authoritative.

Checkpoint
What does the intellect need after certainty in God and prophethood to be certain about the grave?
A) A rational proof
B) A personal spiritual experience
C) A mutawatir report from Quran or Sunnah
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
The questioning and punishment of the grave are established by mutawatir reports that every believer must accept.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have believed in Allah and His Messenger, yet have you ever doubted the reality of the grave's questioning? This passage tells you that your doubt is a contradiction of your own logic. Will you now confess that you were living with an inconsistency in your faith, and commit to renewing your certainty in this unseen reality?
?
The intellect, once certain of the fundamentals, demands belief in all mutawatir reports. Have you truly submitted your intellect to the authority of revelation, or do you still pick and choose which parts of the unseen you accept? What does that say about the completeness of your iman?
?
If you truly believe that the proof for the grave's punishment is the same as the proof for the Quran being the speech of Allah, then how seriously do you take the warnings of the grave? Are you living as if you will face that questioning, or are you living as if the grave is just a rest? What change must you make today?

Unseen Matters

Refutation of Reincarnation from the Grave's Reality
Al-Buti refutes reincarnation by showing its contradiction with the grave's reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in reincarnation is incompatible with the Islamic doctrine of the grave's questioning and punishment.

Core Idea
Reincarnation and the grave's torment are logically incompatible.

Having established the transmitted proof for the grave, Al-Buti now refutes reincarnation. He argues that the soul remains tied to the body after death, as the Quran states, and cannot migrate to another body. Therefore, belief in reincarnation directly contradicts belief in the grave's events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the soul's attachment
Read the Arabic passage. Focus on the argument that the soul is occupied with its body.
The Quranic verse is key: {Every soul is held in pledge for what it earns}.
2
Understand the impossibility of soul migration
Al-Buti argues that the soul cannot leave to inhabit another body. This is based on the nature of the soul's relation to the body.
The soul is 'imprisoned for it or against it'.
3
Recognize the contradiction
Belief in reincarnation and belief in the grave's events cannot coexist because they are contradictory.
One implies denial of the other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقُلْنَا إِنَّ الْمَيْتَ يَتَعَرَّضُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِمَّا لِلَوْنٍ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ أَوْ لِلَوْنٍ مِنَ النَّعِيمِ. وَأَوْضَحْنَا أَنَّ الْبُرْهَانَ الْعِلْمِيَّ فِي هَذَا، هُوَ عَيْنُ الْبُرْهَانِ الْعِلْمِيِّ الْمُتَعَلِّقِ بِوُجُودِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ وَبِنُبُوَّةِ مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وَبِأَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ الْمُعْجِزَ كَلامُ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، وَأَنَّ الْعَقْلَ لَا يَحْتَاجُ - بَعْدَ أَنْ يَسْتَيْقِنَ كُلَّ ذَلِكَ - إِلَّا إِلَى الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى خَبَرٍ مَوْصُولِ السَّنَدِ إِلَى الْقُرْآنِ أَوِ السُّنَّةِ يَرْتَقِي فِي تَعْدَادِ طُرُقِهِ إِلَى التَّوَاتُرِ لِيَكْتَسِبَ دَرَجَةَ الْيَقِينِ وَالْقَطْعِ فِي حُكْمِ الْعَقْلِ. وَلَقَدْ رَأَيْتَ الْخَبَرَ الْمُتَوَاتِرَ عَنِ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ، قَاضِيًا بِثُبُوتِ كُلٍّ مِنْ سُؤَالِ الْقَبْرِ وَعَذَابِهِ، فَلَا يَسَعُكَ، وَقَدْ آمَنْتَ بِكُلِّ مَا مَرَّ ذِكْرُهُ فِي قِسْمِ الإِلَهِيَّاتِ وَالنُّبُوَّاتِ، إِلَّا أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِمَضْمُونِ هَذِهِ الأَخْبَارِ الْمُتَوَاتِرَةِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّكَ قَدْ عَلِمْتَ بِأَنَّ السُّؤَالَ وَالْعَذَابَ وَارِدَانِ عَلَى رُوحِ الْمَيِّتِ بِيَقِينٍ، إِذْ لَا يُتَصَوَّرُ بِدُونِ ذَلِكَ خِطَابٌ أَوْ نَعِيمٌ أَوْ عَذَابٌ، وَإِذًا فَالرُّوحُ مَشْغُولَةٌ بِصَاحِبِهَا مَحْبُوسَةٌ لَهُ أَوْ عَلَيْهِ كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: {كُلُّ نَفْسٍ بِمَا كَسَبَتْ رَهِينَةٌ} [المدثر: 38] وَلَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ تَنْصَرِفَ مُوَلِّيَةً عَنْهُ لِتَسْكُنَ جَسَدًا آخَرَ تَسْتَقْبِلُ فِيهِ سُلُوكًا جَدِيدًا وَوُجُودًا آخَرَ بَدِيعًا. وَلَا يُمْكِنُ لِأَيِّ عَاقِلٍ أَنْ يَجْمَعَ عَلَى فِكْرِهِ كُلًّا مِنَ الإِيمَانِ بِالتَّنَاسُخِ، وَالإِيمَانِ بِمَا يَكُونُ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ مِنَ السُّؤَالِ وَالْعَذَابِ، إِذْ هُمَا مُتَنَاقِضَانِ تَنَاقُضًا وَاضِحًا: فَلَا جَرَمَ أَنَّ الإِيمَانَ بِأَحَدِهِمَا مَظْهَرُ إِنْكَارِ الآخَرِ. فَهَذَا هُوَ الدَّلِيلُ الْخَبَرِيُّ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ التَّنَاسُخِ.
And we said that the deceased is exposed after that either to a kind of torment or a kind of bliss. And we explained that the scientific proof for this is the very same scientific proof related to the existence of Allah Almighty and the prophethood of Muhammad peace be upon him, and that the miraculous Quran is the speech of Allah Almighty, and that the intellect does not need - after it is certain of all that - except to come upon a report whose chain is connected to the Quran or Sunnah, whose paths rise in number to tawatur (mass transmission) to acquire the degree of certainty and decisiveness in the judgment of the intellect. And indeed you have seen the mutawatir (massively transmitted) report from the Book and Sunnah, deciding the establishment of both the questioning of the grave and its punishment. So it is not possible for you, having believed in everything mentioned in the section on Divinity and Prophethood, except to believe in the content of these mutawatir reports. Then you have known that the questioning and torment occur upon the soul of the deceased with certainty, for without that no address, bliss, or torment can be conceived. And thus the soul is occupied with its companion, imprisoned for it or against it, as Allah Almighty said: {Every soul is held in pledge for what it earns} [al-Muddaththir: 38]. And it cannot turn away from it to dwell in another body to receive a new conduct and another novel existence. And it is not possible for any rational person to combine in his thought both belief in reincarnation and belief in what occurs after death of questioning and torment, for they are clearly contradictory: inevitably, belief in one is a manifestation of denial of the other. So this is the transmitted proof from the Book and Sunnah for the invalidity of reincarnation.

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted proof (dalil khabari) for the reality of the grave's questioning and punishment, and consequently refutes reincarnation. The author begins by reminding that the deceased faces either torment or bliss after death. He states that the scientific proof for this is identical to the proof for God's existence, prophethood, and the miraculous Quran. He then asserts that there is a mutawatir report from Quran and Sunnah establishing the questioning and punishment of the grave, so anyone who believes in the earlier sections (Ilahiyyat and Nubuwwat) must also believe in these reports. Next, he explains that the soul is attached to the body, as per Quran 74:38, and cannot leave to inhabit another body. Therefore, belief in reincarnation (tanasukh) is contradictory to belief in the grave's events; one implies denial of the other. He concludes that this is the transmitted proof from Quran and Sunnah for the invalidity of reincarnation.

?

?

The Hidden Timing of the Hour
Buti asserts the exact time of the Hour is hidden from all creatures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the exact time of the Hour is known only to God and how to evaluate claims about it.

Core Idea
Only God knows when the Hour will come.

This lesson explores a fundamental Islamic belief: the exact timing of the Day of Resurrection is known solely to Allah. The author, Muhammad Sa'id Ramadan al-Buti, explains that even prophets and angels do not possess this knowledge. He supports his argument with Quranic verses and a famous hadith, and warns against anyone who claims to know the specific time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Buti begins by stating the key point: the time of the Hour is unknown to all except God.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses and the hadith he cites.
2
Understand the Quranic proofs
Buti quotes two verses: Surah al-A'raf 7:187 and Surah al-Mulk 67:25-26. Reflect on how each verse emphasizes that knowledge of the Hour belongs to Allah alone.
The phrase 'بغتةً' (suddenly) in the first verse highlights the unexpected nature of the Hour.
3
Analyze the prophetic hadith
The Prophet's response to Gabriel ('The one asked about it is no more knowledgeable than the one asking') shows that even the Prophet himself did not know the exact time.
This hadith is authentic and agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Apply the warning
Buti concludes with a strong warning: anyone who sets a specific date for the Hour is either ignorant or a deceitful enemy of Islam. Consider how this applies to modern claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موعد ثانيا أشراط الساعة قيام الساعة مجهول لا يعرفه من دون الله أحد : الحادثة الكونية العظمى والساعة من أسماء يوم القيامة ، ويوم القيامة هو التي تطوى عندها السماوات والأرض وينتثر فيها هذا النظام الكوني أجمع . فأما عن موعد هذا الحدث وزمنه والوقت الذي يكون فيه ، فذلك ما أخفى الله تعالى علمه عن الناس كلهم بما فيهم الرسل والأنبياء ، فليس لأحد ـ كائناً كان من سبيل إلى معرفة مابقي من عمر الدنيا ولقد صرح من القرآن بهذا مكرراً ومؤكداً ، فقال مرة : و يسألونك عن السَّاعَةِ أَيَّانَ مُرساها ، قُل إِنَّا عِلمُها عِندَ رَبِّي لا يُجَلِّيها لِوَقتها إِلا هُوَ ، ثَقُلَت فِي السَّمواتِ والأرض ، لا تأتيكُمْ إِلا بَغتَةً ، يَسألونَكَ كَأَنَّكَ حَفِيٌّ عَنها ، قُلْ إِنَّا عامها عند الله ولكن أكثر الناس لا يعلمون ﴾ [الأعراف : ۱۸۷] . وقال مرة أخرى : ( ويقولون متى هذا الوَعْدُ إن كنتم صادقين ، قُل إنا العلم عند الله وإنا أنا نذير مبين و [ الملك ٢٥ - ٢٦ ] وأوضح النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام هذا في الحديث الصحيح المتفق عليه عندما سأله جبريل : « متى الساعة ؟ » حيث أجابه : « ما المسؤول عنها بأعلم من السائل » فإن سمعت من يحدد للدهر عمراً معيناً أو يضع ليوم القيامة ميقاتاً محدوداً فاعلم أنه إما مغمور في جهل عميق بالدين ، أو هو كاذب دساس وضع بين عينـيه سبيلاً معينة لحرب الإسلام والكيد له
Appointment. Second: The Signs of the Hour. The standing of the Hour is unknown; no one besides God knows it. The great cosmic event: The Hour is one of the names of the Day of Resurrection, and the Day of Resurrection is that at which the heavens and the earth are folded up and in which this entire cosmic order is scattered. As for the appointment of this event, its time and the moment when it will occur, God has hidden knowledge of it from all people, including messengers and prophets. So no one, whoever he may be, has any way to know how much remains of the world's lifespan. Indeed, the Qur'an has stated this repeatedly and emphatically. He said once: 'They ask you about the Hour, when is its arrival? Say, "Its knowledge is only with my Lord; none will reveal it at its time except Him. It weighs heavily upon the heavens and the earth; it will not come upon you except suddenly." They ask you as if you are well-informed of it. Say, "Its knowledge is only with Allah, but most people do not know."' [Al-A'rāf 187]. And He said another time: 'And they say, "When will this promise be fulfilled, if you are truthful?" Say, "The knowledge is only with Allah, and I am only a clear warner."' [Al-Mulk 25-26]. And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, clarified this in the authentic agreed-upon hadith when Gabriel asked him: 'When is the Hour?' He answered: 'The one asked about it is no more knowledgeable than the one asking.' So if you hear someone who sets a specific age for the world or places a limited time for the Day of Resurrection, know that he is either immersed in deep ignorance of religion, or he is a deceitful liar who has set before his eyes a particular way to wage war against Islam and plot against it.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of the signs of the Hour (Ashrāṭ al-Sāʿah) but immediately emphasizes that the exact timing of the Hour is unknown to anyone except God. The author defines the Hour as the Day of Resurrection when the cosmos is destroyed. He then argues that God has concealed this knowledge from all creatures, including prophets and messengers. As proof, he cites two Quranic verses: Surah al-A'raf 187 and Surah al-Mulk 25-26, which state that knowledge of the Hour is with God alone. He also cites the well-known hadith from Gabriel's question, where the Prophet responds that the questioner and the answered are equally ignorant. Finally, he warns against anyone who claims to know the exact time, labeling them either ignorant or malicious enemies of Islam. This reinforces the Islamic doctrine that the Hour is a matter of the unseen (ghayb) known only to God.

بغتة

Correction: Buti explicitly states that God has hidden this knowledge from all people, including messengers and prophets, and the Prophet himself affirmed he does not know.

Key Takeaway
The exact time of the Hour is known only to God; anyone claiming otherwise is ignorant or malicious.

The exact time of the Hour is known only to Allah
Buti asserts that the time of the Hour is unknown to all except Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge of the Hour is exclusively with Allah, as established by Quranic verses and prophetic hadith, and why claiming otherwise is a serious error.

Core Idea
Only Allah knows the Hour; all claims to know are ignorance or enmity.

This lesson addresses a fundamental belief in Islam: that the exact timing of the Day of Resurrection is known only to Allah. Buti presents the scriptural evidence and issues a stern warning against anyone who presumes to know. As you read, notice how the Qur'an and Sunnah consistently direct such questions back to Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and verses
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the two Quranic verses and the hadith of Jibril.
The verses are from al-A'raf and al-Mulk.

أشراط الساعة
قيام الساعة مجهول لا يعرفه من دون الله أحد :
الحادثة الكونية العظمى
والساعة من أسماء يوم القيامة ، ويوم القيامة هو التي تطوى عندها السماوات والأرض وينتثر فيها هذا النظام الكوني أجمع .
فأما عن موعد هذا الحدث وزمنه والوقت الذي يكون فيه ، فذلك ما أخفى الله تعالى علمه عن الناس كلهم بما فيهم الرسل والأنبياء ، فليس لأحد ـ كائناً كان من سبيل إلى معرفة مابقي من عمر الدنيا
ولقد صرح من القرآن بهذا مكرراً ومؤكداً ، فقال مرة : ﴿ يَسأَلونَكَ عَنِ السَّاعَةِ أَيَّانَ مُرساها ، قُل إِنَّما عِلمُها عِندَ رَبِّي لا يُجَلِّيها لِوَقتِها إِلا هُوَ ، ثَقُلَت فِي السَّمواتِ والأرض ، لا تَأتيكُم إِلا بَغتَةً ، يَسأَلونَكَ كَأَنَّكَ حَفِيٌّ عَنها ، قُل إِنَّما عِلمُها عِندَ اللهِ وَلٰكِنَّ أَكثَرَ النَّاسِ لا يَعلَمونَ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٨٧] .
وقال مرة أخرى : ﴿ وَيَقولونَ مَتىٰ هٰذَا الوَعدُ إِن كُنتُم صادِقينَ ، قُل إِنَّما العِلمُ عِندَ اللهِ وَإِنَّما أَنا نَذيرٌ مُبينٌ ﴾ [الملك : ٢٥-٢٦] .
وأوضح النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام هذا في الحديث الصحيح المتفق عليه عندما سأله جبريل : « متى الساعة ؟ » حيث أجابه : « ما المسؤول عنها بأعلم من السائل » .
فإن سمعت من يحدد للدهر عمراً معيناً أو يضع ليوم القيامة ميقاتاً محدوداً فاعلم أنه إما مغمور في جهل عميق بالدين ، أو هو كاذب دساس وضع بين عينيه سبيلاً معينة لحرب الإسلام والكيد له
Signs of the Hour. The occurrence of the Hour is unknown; none knows it besides Allah. The great cosmic event. And the Hour is one of the names of the Day of Resurrection, and the Day of Resurrection is that at which the heavens and the earth are folded up and this entire cosmic system is scattered. As for the time of this event, its moment, and the hour when it will occur, that is what Allah the Exalted has concealed knowledge of from all people, including the messengers and prophets. So no one—whoever he may be—has any way to know how much of the lifespan of the world remains. And the Qur'an has stated this repeatedly and emphatically. He said once: 'They ask you about the Hour: when is its arrival? Say: Its knowledge is only with my Lord; none will reveal it at its time except Him. It is heavy upon the heavens and the earth; it will not come upon you except suddenly. They ask you as if you are well-informed of it. Say: Its knowledge is only with Allah, but most people do not know' [7:187]. And He said another time: 'And they say: When will this promise come if you are truthful? Say: The knowledge is only with Allah, and I am only a clear warner' [67:25-26]. And the Prophet (peace and blessings upon him) clarified this in the authentic hadith agreed upon when Jibril asked him: 'When is the Hour?' He answered: 'The one questioned about it is not more knowledgeable than the questioner.' So if you hear someone who assigns a specific age to the world or sets a specific time for the Day of Resurrection, know that he is either immersed in deep ignorance of the religion or he is a lying schemer who has placed before his eyes a specific path to wage war against Islam and plot against it.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is an assertion and proof that the exact time of the Hour is known only to Allah. The author begins by defining the Hour as a great cosmic event—the Day of Resurrection when the entire universe will be dismantled. He then states that knowledge of its timing has been concealed from all people, including prophets. To support this, he cites two Quranic verses: Surah al-A'raf 7:187, which emphasizes that only Allah knows when it will come suddenly, and Surah al-Mulk 67:25-26, where the Prophet is told to respond that knowledge is with Allah alone. He then references the well-known hadith of Jibril asking about the Hour, and the Prophet's reply that he is no more knowledgeable than the questioner. Finally, the author warns strongly against anyone who claims to know the remaining lifespan of the world, labeling such a person as either ignorantly misguided or a deliberate enemy of Islam.

Major Signs of the Hour: Certainty via Mutawatir Reports
Buti divides the major signs into two categories based on certainty of transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author divides the major signs into two categories based on transmission certainty, and why only the mutawatir category is discussed for creedal belief.

Core Idea
Certainty for creedal belief requires mutawatir reports, not ahad.

The author establishes that the major signs of the Hour are known from revelation and must be believed in. However, a detailed analysis requires distinguishing between signs transmitted through mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and ahad (single-chain) reports. In this passage, he clarifies that only the first category carries the definitive certainty needed for obligatory belief, setting the methodological foundation for his discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the author's division of signs.
Notice the technical terms 'mutawatir' and 'ahad'.
2
Identify the two categories
The passage divides the signs into two categories. Find them and note the basis of division (transmission certainty).
3
Understand the author's focus
Ask yourself why the author only discusses the first category. The answer lies in the requirement of definitive evidence for creedal belief.
This connects to the learning objective about certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علاماتها الكبرى :
وأما عن علامات الساعة وأشراطها التي تكون بين يديها ، فقد حدثنا كل من الكتاب والسنة عن أشراط لها ، ولا شك أن جملة هذه الأشراط مما هو معروف من الدين بالضرورة فلا يجوز للمسلم أن ينكرها أو يمتري بها وإن كانت داخلة في المغيبات التي لم تقع بعد .
وأما النظر التفصيلي في كل منها فإن ذلك يقتضينا أن نقسم هذه الأشراط إلى قسمين :
فأما القسم الأول منها ، فثابت بالخبر المتواتر الذي يورث القطع واليقين . وأما القسم الثاني فمنقول إلينا عن طريق الآحاد .
ونحن لم نعرّج في حديثنا هذا على القسم الثاني من الأشراط ، وإن كان الكثير منها وارداً بطريق صحيحة متفق على صحتها ، إذ هي لا تتجاوز على كل حال حدود الظنيات ، وإنما يشترط لضرورة الاعتقاد قيام الدليل القطعي كما قد علمت .
وإنما نحدثك عن القسم الأول منها فقط وهو الذي ورد به الخبر القطعي فكان الإيمان به ، بسبب ذلك واجباً
Its major signs: As for the signs of the Hour and its portents that occur before it, both the Book and the Sunnah have told us about signs of it. There is no doubt that the totality of these signs is known from the religion by necessity, so it is not permissible for a Muslim to deny them or doubt them, even though they are among the unseen matters that have not yet occurred. As for detailed examination of each of them, that requires us to divide these signs into two parts: As for the first part, it is established by the mutawatir report that produces certainty and conviction. As for the second part, it is transmitted to us via ahad reports. And we did not stop in our present discussion on the second part of the signs, even though many of them are narrated through authentic chains agreed upon by scholars, because they do not, in any case, exceed the realm of probabilities. Rather, for the necessity of belief, the existence of definitive evidence is required, as you have known. We are only telling you about the first part, which is that which has come through definitive report, and thus belief in it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a classification and methodological statement about the major signs of the Hour. The author first affirms that the existence of these signs is known necessarily from the Quran and Sunnah, and it is obligatory to believe in them even though they are future unseen events. He then divides them into two categories based on the certainty of their transmission: the first category is transmitted via mutawatir reports that yield certain knowledge, while the second is transmitted via ahad reports that yield only probable knowledge. He clarifies that he will only discuss the first category because belief in matters of faith requires definitive (qat'i) evidence. This establishes a method: only those signs confirmed by mutawatir reports are obligatory to believe in; ahad reports, though authentic, do not create the same level of certainty required for creedal belief.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
الخبر المتواتر
الآحاد
الدليل القطعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think all hadiths about the signs are equally binding in creed, regardless of transmission type.
Correction: The author explains that only mutawatir reports create the certainty required for obligatory belief; ahad reports, even if authentic, remain probable and do not necessitate creedal acceptance.

Checkpoint

B) Because the first category is the only one mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The author argues that only the major signs transmitted via mutawatir reports provide the definitive evidence required for obligatory belief in creedal matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Buti introduces the Dajjal, his name, origin, and characteristics.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is a real individual of extreme deception who will claim divinity.

Buti begins his discussion of the major signs of the Hour with the Dajjal, whose appearance is a certain event narrated in numerous hadiths. This lesson introduces the Dajjal's name and its significance, his origin, his deceptive strategy, and the nature of his following. The Two Categories of Major Signs and Necessity of Certainty
Buti classifies major signs into mutawatir and ahad, requiring certainty for belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's classification of major signs into mutawatir and ahad, and why only mutawatir reports demand obligatory belief.

Core Idea
Only definitive evidence yields necessary belief in eschatological matters.

Buti grounds the study of major signs in a methodological principle: belief in unseen matters requires certainty. He therefore divides the reports about the Hour into two categories and explains why only the first category—mass-transmitted (mutawatir) reports—can ground obligatory faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let Buti's own terminology sink in before analysis.
Notice the contrast between 'mutawatir' and 'ahad'.
2
Identify the two categories
Locate where Buti explicitly divides the signs into two sections. Mark what defines each.
The first section is established by mutawatir; the second by ahad.
3
Understand the criterion for obligatory belief
Buti states that necessary belief requires 'dalil qat'i' (definitive evidence). Ask yourself why ahad reports, even if authentic, do not suffice.
The reason is they yield only probability (zann), not certainty.
4
Note the exclusion of ahad reports
Buti deliberately sets aside the second category. Recognize that his focus is on what must be believed, not on what may be true.
This is a methodological choice, not a denial of their authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النظر التفصيلي في كل منها فإن ذلك يقتضينا أن نقسم هذه الأشراط إلى قسمين: فأما القسم الأول منها، فثابت بالخبر المتواتر الذي يورث القطع واليقين. وأما القسم الثاني فمنقول إلينا عن طريق الآحاد. ونحن لم نعرّج في حديثنا هذا على القسم الثاني من الأشراط، وإن كان الكثير منها وارداً بطريق صحيحة متفق على صحتها، إذ هي لا تتجاوز على كل حال حدود الظنيات، وإنما يشترط لضرورة الاعتقاد قيام الدليل القطعي كما قد علمت. وإنما نحدثك عن القسم الأول منها فقط وهو الذي ورد به الخبر القطعي فكان الإيمان به، بسبب ذلك واجباً
As for detailed examination of each of them, that requires us to divide these signs into two sections: As for the first section, it is established by the mutawatir (mass-transmitted) report that yields definitive certainty (qat' wa yaqin). As for the second section, it is transmitted to us via ahad (single) reports. We have not touched in this discourse of ours on the second section of the signs, even though many of them are reported through an authentic chain agreed upon as sound, for they do not, in any case, exceed the limits of probable matters (zanniyyat). Rather, what is required for the necessity of belief is the existence of definitive evidence (dalil qat'i), as you have already learned. We only speak to you about the first section alone, which was conveyed by definitive report (khabr qat'i), so belief in it, due to that, is obligatory.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage classifies the major signs of the Hour. Buti states that a detailed look requires dividing these signs into two categories. The first category is established by mutawatir reports, which yield definitive certainty (qat' wa yaqin). The second category comes through ahad (single) reports. Buti clarifies that he will not discuss the second category in this discourse, even though many of those reports are authentic and agreed upon, because they only reach the level of probability (zanniyyat). The underlying principle is that for necessary belief (darurat al-i'tiqad), definitive evidence (dalil qat'i) is required. Therefore, he will only speak about the first category—those conveyed by definitive report—and belief in them is obligatory.

Key Terms
مُتَوَاتِر (mutawatir)
آحَاد (ahad)
قَطْع (qat')
يَقِين (yaqin)
ظَنِّيّ (zanni)
دَلِيل قَطْعِيّ (dalil qat'i)
خبر قطعي (khabr qat'i)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any authentic hadith suffices for obligatory belief in eschatological matters.
Correction: Buti stresses that only mutawatir reports, which yield certainty (qat'), are sufficient for necessary belief. Ahad reports, even if authentic, only produce probability (zann) and thus do not qualify.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what type of evidence is required for necessary belief in the major signs of the Hour?
A) Any authentic hadith regardless of transmission
B) Definitive evidence (dalil qat'i) such as mutawatir reports
C) Ahad reports if they are agreed upon
D) Scholarly consensus (ijma')

Key Takeaway
Only mutawatir reports providing certainty demand obligatory belief in the major signs of the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the Day of Judgment, do you find yourself more moved by authentic but isolated hadith than by the mutawātir reports that demand certainty? How might this imbalance affect your readiness for the Hour?
?
If you have built beliefs about the Last Day on hadith that only reach probability (ẓann), are you willing to re-examine them in light of Buti's criterion? What would it cost you to hold only certain beliefs?
?
This lesson confronts you with the reality that not all knowledge of the unseen is created equal. Could it be that your attachment to certain signs (like the Mahdi or Dajjal) is based on ahad reports rather than definitive evidence? How would your life change if you insisted on certainty for every eschatological belief you hold?

The First Major Sign: The Emergence of the Dajjal
Buti defines the Dajjal and cites three hadiths about him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Dajjal, his deceptive tactics, and the key warnings from three authentic hadiths.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is the ultimate deceiver; his signs are a test of faith.

Buti begins the discussion of the major signs by focusing on the Dajjal, warning believers of his intense deception. The Prophet's hadiths provide crucial details to recognize and resist him. This lesson examines three of those hadiths, explaining their meanings and implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of the Dajjal
Read Buti's introduction defining the Dajjal as a title for a deceptive figure of Jewish origin who claims divinity.
Note that 'Dajjal' means extreme deceiver.
2
Examine the first hadith: one-eyed but not Allah
Study the hadith from Ibn 'Umar emphasizing that the Dajjal is one-eyed, while Allah is not — a crucial distinction.
3
Analyze the second hadith: water and fire as a test
Reflect on the hadith from Hudhayfah where the Dajjal brings apparent water that is fire, and apparent fire that is sweet water, testing believers' discernment.
4
Explore the third hadith: description and protection
Read the longer hadith from al-Nawwas describing the Dajjal's appearance, his emergence, and the instruction to recite Surah al-Kahf's opening verses.
The hadith is cut off at the end regarding his speed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - ظهور الدجال : والدجال لقب له، لب به لشدة تدجيله وكذبه، ولقدرته الخارقة على تغطية الحق بالباطل، وهو رجل يهودي الأصل، من جهة المشرق، فيدعي بين الناس الصلاح والاستقامة، ثم إنه يدعي الألوهية ويتبعه فيما يدعو الناس إليه خلق كثير معظمهم من اليهود. ولقد فاضت بالأحاديث المتعلقة به جميع كتب السنة، تحذيراً وإخباراً ووصفاً. ولننقل لك بعضاً يسيراً من هذه الأحاديث: ١ - روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال : قام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الناس، فأثنى على الله بما هو أهله، ثم ذكر الدجال، فقال: « لأنذركموه وما من نبي إلا وقد أنذر قومه، ولكني سأقول لكم فيه قولاً لم يقله نبي لقومه. إنه أعور، وإن الله ليس بأعور ». ٢ - روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن حذيفة ( واللفظ لمسلم ) أن عقبة قال له : حدثني ماسمعت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الدجال فقال : إن الدجال يخرج وإن معه ماء وناراً، فأما الذي يراه الناس ماء فنار تحرق وأما الذي يراه الناس ناراً فماء بارد عذب؛ فمن أدرك ذلك منكم فليقع في الذي يراه ناراً، فإنه عذب طيب فقال عقبة : وأنا قد سمعته، تصديقاً لحذيفة. ٣ - روى مسلم وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه وأحمد وغيرهم، حديثاً طويلاً في شأن الدجال وما يكون في وقته نسوقه لك باختصار : عن النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه، قال : ذكر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الدجال ذات غداة، فخفض فيه ورفع، حتى ظنناه في طائفة النخل ( فلما رحنا إليه عرف ذلك فينا فقال : غير الدجال أخوفني عليكم، إن يخرج وأنا فيكم فأنا حجيجه دونكم، وإن يخرج ولست فيكم فامرؤ حجيج نفسه. والله خليفتي على كل مسلم، إنه شاب قطط عينه طافئة، كأني أشبهه بعبد العزى بن قطن، فمن أدركه منكم فليقرأ عليه فواتح سورة الكهف، إنه خارج خلة بين الشام والعراق ) فعاث يميناً وعاث شمالاً، ياعباد الله فاثبتوا ». قلنا يا رسول الله وما لبثه في الأرض ؟ قال : « أربعين يوماً، يوم كسنة ويوم كشهر، ويوم كجمعة، وسائر أيامه كأيامكم » قلنا : يارسول الله فذلك اليوم الذي كسنة أتكفينا فيه صلاة يوم ؟ قال : « لا، أقدروا له قدره ». قلنا : يارسول الله وما إسراعه في الأرض ؟
1 - The emergence of the Dajjal: The Dajjal is a title given to him, due to the intensity of his deception and lying, and his extraordinary ability to cover truth with falsehood. He is a man of Jewish origin, from the direction of the east. He claims among the people righteousness and uprightness, then he claims divinity and many people follow him in what he calls them to, most of them Jews. All books of the Sunnah are overflowing with hadiths concerning him, as warning, informing, and description. We shall quote for you a small portion of these hadiths: 1 - Al-Shaykhan (Bukhari and Muslim) and others narrated from Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, stood among the people, praised Allah as He deserves, then mentioned the Dajjal and said: 'I warn you of him; there is no prophet who has not warned his people, but I shall say to you about him a saying that no prophet has said to his people: He is one-eyed, and Allah is not one-eyed.' 2 - Al-Shaykhan and others narrated from Hudhayfah (the wording is Muslim's) that 'Uqbah said to him: Tell me what you heard from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, about the Dajjal. He said: 'The Dajjal will emerge and with him will be water and fire. As for what the people see as water, it is burning fire, and as for what the people see as fire, it is cool sweet water. So whoever among you reaches that time, let him fall into that which he sees as fire, for it is sweet and pleasant.' 'Uqbah said: And I have heard it, confirming Hudhayfah. 3 - Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ahmad, and others narrated a long hadith concerning the Dajjal and what will happen at his time, which we present to you in summary: from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, mentioned the Dajjal one morning, and he lowered and raised (his voice) concerning him, until we thought he was among the palm trees (when we went to him, he noticed that in us and said: 'Other than the Dajjal, I fear more for you. If he emerges while I am among you, I will be his adversary on your behalf; if he emerges while I am not among you, then each person is his own adversary. Allah is my successor over every Muslim. He is a young man with curly hair, his eye blind, as if I liken him to 'Abd al-'Uzza ibn Qatan. Whoever among you reaches him, let him recite the opening verses of Surah al-Kahf over him. He will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq) and he will wreak havoc right and left. O servants of Allah, be steadfast.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, how long will he stay on earth? He said: 'Forty days: a day like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, for that day which is like a year, will one day's prayer suffice us? He said: 'No, measure it according to its measure.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his speed on earth? (the answer is not present in the text).
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage introduces the first major sign of the Hour: the emergence of the Dajjal (the Antichrist). Buti defines the Dajjal as a title for a person characterized by intense deception and lying, with an extraordinary ability to conceal truth with falsehood. He is described as being of Jewish origin, from the east. He initially claims righteousness, then later claims divinity, and many followers, mostly Jews, follow him. Buti notes that all books of Sunnah are full of hadiths about him. He then cites three hadiths: The first (from Ibn 'Umar) emphasizes that the Dajjal is one-eyed, while Allah is not one-eyed, a crucial point distinguishing creator from creature. The second (from Hudhayfah) warns that the Dajjal will paradoxically carry apparent water and fire—what seems water is actually fire, and what seems fire is sweet water, testing believers. The third, longer hadith (from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an) provides more details: the Prophet mentioned the Dajjal one morning, alarming the companions so much that they thought he was nearby. The Prophet then comforted them that he fears other things more for them. He described the Dajjal physically (young, curly hair, one eye blind, resembling 'Abd al-'Uzza ibn Qatan), and instructed to recite the opening of Surah al-Kahf against him. He will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq, cause widespread corruption, and stay for forty days of varying lengths. The companions asked about prayer on the day like a year, and the Prophet told them to estimate its times. The last question about his speed on earth is not completed in this text.

أَعْوَر
مَاء وَنَار
فَوَاتِح سُورَة الْكَهْف
خَلَّة
أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the Dajjal's water and fire are literal as they appear.
Correction: The hadith clarifies that what appears as water is actually burning fire, and what appears as fire is cool sweet water — a test of faith.

Checkpoint

A) Actual water and fire
B) Water that is fire, and fire that is sweet water
C) Miracles and armies
D) Gold and silver

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is a major test; recognizing his deception through prophetic guidance is essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Dajjal will offer water that is fire and fire that is water. In your own life, what 'water' (something you desire) might actually be 'fire' (harmful)? Will you trust the Prophet's warning over your own eyes and desires? Commit today to one specific area where you will choose obedience over immediate gratification.
?
The Prophet's companions feared the Dajjal so deeply that they thought he was among them. Do you feel that same urgency about the trials of faith, or are you more worried about your daily challenges? What worldly concern can you surrender to Allah today, replacing it with a sincere fear of His trials?
?
The Dajjal is a man of Jewish origin who will claim divinity. How do you guard your heart from attributing divine qualities to any human being—a leader, a scholar, or even yourself? Write down one practical step to ensure your worship is directed to Allah alone, not to any created being.

Hadith of Ibn Umar: Dajjal is One-Eyed, Allah is Not
Buti cites hadith that Dajjal is one-eyed while Allah is not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's description of the Dajjal as one-eyed serves to affirm Allah's transcendence and refute any resemblance to creation.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is one-eyed; Allah is not one-eyed.

In this lesson, we examine a powerful hadith from Bukhari and Muslim in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) gives a unique warning about the Dajjal. He emphasizes that unlike all previous prophets who also warned their nations, he reveals a distinct sign: the Dajjal is one-eyed, and Allah is absolutely free from such imperfection. This brief statement carries profound theological weight, clarifying Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the structure: the Prophet praises Allah, then warns about the Dajjal, and then gives the unique statement.
The unclear phrase 'صلى الله في [؟] الناس' likely means 'صلى الله عليه في الناس' (the Prophet stood among the people).
2
Identify the key distinction
The Prophet says: 'He is one-eyed, and Allah is not one-eyed.' This is the core teaching. Reflect on why this distinction is important: it negates any physical attribute from Allah while attributing it to the Dajjal.
3
Understand the theological significance
This hadith refutes anthropomorphism (tashbih). By explicitly stating that Allah is not one-eyed, the Prophet cuts off any attempt to liken Allah to His creation. The Dajjal's defect highlights Allah's perfection.
This is part of the science of samiyyat (transmitted matters) in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 - روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال : قام رسول الله صلى الله في [؟] الناس ، فأثنى على الله بما هو أهله ، ثم ذكر الدجال ، فقال : « لأنذركموه وما من نبي إلا وقد أنذر قومه ، ولكني سأقول لكم فيه قولاً لم يقله نبي لقومه . إنه أعور ، وإن الله ليس بأعور » .
1 - The two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) and others narrated from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood among the people, praised Allah as He deserves, then mentioned the Dajjal and said: 'I warn you of him, and there is no prophet who did not warn his people, but I will tell you about him what no prophet told his people: he is one-eyed, and Allah is not one-eyed.'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a citation of a hadith from the two Sahihs (Bukhari and Muslim) and others, narrated by Ibn Umar. The Prophet (peace be upon him) stood before the people, praised Allah, and then warned them about the Dajjal. He emphasized that although all prophets warned their nations about the Dajjal, he was giving a unique description: the Dajjal is one-eyed, whereas Allah, exalted be He, is not one-eyed. This directly refutes any anthropomorphic misconception and establishes a clear distinguishing sign of the Dajjal.

Key Terms
دجال
أعور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because the Dajjal is described as one-eyed, Allah might also have an eye or be similar to creation.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly negates that Allah is one-eyed, affirming absolute transcendence. This hadith is a clear refutation of anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
What unique information did the Prophet give about the Dajjal that no other prophet gave?
A) The Dajjal will come from the east.
B) The Dajjal is one-eyed, while Allah is not.
C) The Dajjal will be killed by Jesus.
D) The Dajjal will have water and fire.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Ibn Umar teaches that the Dajjal is one-eyed, while Allah is absolutely free from such imperfection, affirming His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the description of Dajjal as one-eyed, do you catch yourself imagining Allah with any kind of physical form? How can you actively purify your belief in Allah's transcendence today?
?
The Prophet gave a unique warning about Dajjal that no other prophet gave. Are you truly attentive to the Prophet's warnings in your daily life, or do you let them fade into background knowledge? What one warning will you act on this week?
?
If you were to meet the Dajjal tomorrow, would you recognize him as the false god he claims to be? What steps must you take to ensure your heart is anchored in the reality that only Allah is perfect and worthy of worship?

Dajjal's Deceptive Water and Fire
Buti cites a hadith about Dajjal's deceptive water and fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about Dajjal's inversion of water and fire and the prophetic instruction to act against appearances.

Core Idea
Dajjal's deception inverts reality; faith sees through the illusion.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith that illustrates one of the major signs of the Hour: the Dajjal's deceptive use of water and fire. The Prophet ﷺ warns that what appears as water is actually fire, and what appears as fire is sweet water. This inversion tests the believer's obedience to revelation over sensory perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins with Uqbah asking Hudhayfah to relate what he heard from the Prophet about the Dajjal.
Pay attention to the chain of narration: both Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Analyze the inversion
Identify the two pairs: apparent water is real fire, apparent fire is real water. Understand the purpose: the Dajjal creates an illusion to mislead people.
This inversion is a test of faith – will you trust your eyes or the Prophet's words?
3
Reflect on the command
Consider the Prophet's instruction: 'Let him fall into that which he sees as fire.' Why would he command such a counterintuitive action?
The command highlights that true knowledge comes from revelation, not from sensory experience.
4
Confirm the lesson
Note that Uqbah confirms he heard it too. This illustrates how the Companions preserved and verified prophetic teachings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
2 - روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن حذيفة ( واللفظ لمسلم ) أن عقبة قال له : حدثني ما سمعت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه في الدجال فقال : إن الدجال يخرج وإن معه ماء وناراً ، فأما الذي يراه الناس ماء فنار تحرق وأما الذي يراه الناس ناراً فماء بارد عذب ؛ فمن أدرك ذلك منكم فليقع في الذي يراه ناراً ، فإنه عذب طيب فقال عقبة : وأنا قد سمعته ، تصديقاً لحذيفة .
2 - The two Shaykhs and others narrated from Hudhayfah (the wording is from Muslim) that Uqbah said to him: Tell me what you heard from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about the Dajjal. He said: The Dajjal will emerge and with him will be water and fire. As for that which people see as water, it is fire that burns, and as for that which people see as fire, it is cool sweet water. So whoever among you reaches that time should fall into that which he sees as fire, for it is sweet and pure. Uqbah said: I too have heard it, confirming Hudhayfah.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a citation of a hadith from Hudhayfah (with wording from Muslim). It narrates that Uqbah asked Hudhayfah about what he heard from the Prophet concerning the Dajjal. Hudhayfah reports that the Dajjal will emerge accompanied by water and fire, but these are deceptive: what appears as water is actually burning fire, and what appears as fire is sweet, pure water. The Prophet instructs that whoever encounters this should jump into what appears as fire, because it is the real water. Uqbah then confirms that he too heard this from the Prophet, thus corroborating the report.

Key Terms
ماء
نار
دجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Dajjal's water and fire are literal and that one should avoid both.
Correction: The hadith explains they are inversions: the apparent water is fire, and the apparent fire is water. The Prophet commands to fall into what appears as fire, for it is sweet water. This is a test of faith.

B) Fall into what appears as fire.
C) Fall into what appears as water.
D) Wait for further instructions.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's deception inverts reality, but the believer follows revelation, not appearances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you chosen what felt good (sweet water) only to later realize it was burning fire because it contradicted Allah’s command? Will you jump into the 'fire' of obedience even when your senses scream otherwise?
?
The Dajjal will make evil look good and good look evil. What deceptions in today's world—social media, culture, peer pressure—are flipping truth and falsehood? Are you trusting your eyes or the Book of Allah?
?
Hudhayfah and Uqbah both testified to hearing this directly from the Prophet. Do you hold the revealed teachings with that same certainty, or do you water them down when they clash with your desires? Commit to one area today where you will obey Allah's words over your own judgment.

The Prophet's Description of the Dajjal
Hadith excerpt describing the Dajjal and giving instructions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Prophet's description of the Dajjal, including his appearance, the command to recite Surah al-Kahf, and where he will emerge.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is known by description; recite Surah al-Kahf as protection.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) warned his companions about the Dajjal with vivid detail. In this opening section of the hadith, he describes the Dajjal's physical traits, instructs believers on how to protect themselves, and reveals where the fitna will begin. This passage establishes the identity of the Dajjal and the first line of defense against him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Prophet's warning and description
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the Prophet first addresses the companions' fear and then gives a detailed physical description of the Dajjal.
The Prophet compares the Dajjal to 'Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan, a known man of Quraysh.
2
Identify the protective measure
Find the specific instruction the Prophet gives to anyone who encounters the Dajjal. Reflect on why Surah al-Kahf is recommended.
3
Locate the emergence point
The Prophet states where the Dajjal will appear. This geographical detail is part of the fitna.
The 'gap' between Syria and Iraq is a known route.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's own stance
Consider why the Prophet says he is more afraid of other trials than the Dajjal. How does this shape the believer's mindset?
This shows that even a great trial like the Dajjal is not the ultimate danger – neglecting faith is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
3 - روى مسلم وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه وأحمد وغيرهم ، حديثاً طويلاً في شأن الدجال وما يكون في وقته نسوقه لك باختصار : عن النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه ، قال : ذكر رسول الله الله الدجال ذات غداة ، فخفض فيه ورفع ، حتى ظنناه في طائفة النخل (1) فلما رحنا إليه عرف ذلك فينا فقال : « غير الدجال أخوفني عليكم ، إن يخرج وأنا فيكم فأنا حجيجه دونكم ، وإن يخرج ولست فيكم فامرؤ حجيج نفسه . والله خليفتي على كل مسلم ، إنه شاب قطط عينه طافئة ، كأني أشبهه بعبد العزى بن قطن ، فمن أدركه منكم فليقرأ عليه فواتح سورة الكهف ، إنه خارج خلة بين الشام والعراق (2) فعاث يميناً وعاث شمالاً ، ياعباد الله فاثبتوا » . قلنا يا رسول الله وما لبثه في الأرض ؟ قال : « أربعون يوماً، يوم كسنة ويوم كشهر ، ويوم كجمعة ، وسائر أيامه كأيامكم » قلنا : يارسول الله فذلك اليوم الذي كسنة أتكفينا فيه صلاة يوم ؟ قال : « لا ، أقدروا له قدره » . قلنا : يارسول الله وما إسراعه في الأرض ؟ قال : « كالغيث استدبرته الريح فيأتي على القوم فيدعوهم فيؤمنون به ويستجيبون له فيأمر السماء فتمطر والأرض فتنبت . ثم يدعو رجلاً ممتلئاً شباباً فيضربه بالسيف فيقطعه جزلتين رمية الغرض ، ثم يدعوه فيقبل ويتهلل وجهه يضحك . فبينما هو كذلك إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مهرودتين (1) واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين ، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر وإذا رفع تحدر منه مثل الجمان . فيطلبه ( أي يطلب الدجال ) حتى يدركه بباب لد (2) فيقتله (3) .
3 - Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ahmad and others narrated a long hadith concerning the Dajjal and what will happen in his time, which we present to you in summary: from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned the Dajjal one morning, speaking of him in a manner of varying emphasis, until we thought he was in a cluster of palm trees. (1) When we returned to him, he perceived that and said: 'Other than the Dajjal, I fear for you. If he emerges while I am among you, I will argue on your behalf; if he emerges while I am not among you, each person will argue for himself, and Allah is my successor over every Muslim. He is a young man with curly hair, his eye is blind, as if I compare him to Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan. Whoever among you reaches him should recite the opening verses of Surah al-Kahf. He will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq (2) and will wreak havoc right and left. O servants of Allah, be steadfast.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his stay on earth? He said: 'Forty days: one day like a year, one day like a month, one day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, on the day that is like a year, will one day's prayer suffice us? He said: 'No, estimate its due measure.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his speed on earth? He said: 'Like rain driven by the wind. He will come to a people and call them, they will believe in him and respond, and he will command the sky to rain and the earth to sprout. Then he will call a youth full of vitality, strike him with a sword and cut him into two pieces like a target, then call him and he will come forward with a beaming face laughing. While he is thus, Allah will send the Messiah, son of Mary, who will descend at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two garments (1), placing his hands on the wings of two angels. When he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, beads like pearls fall. He will seek him (i.e., seek the Dajjal) until he catches him at the gate of Lud (2) and kills him (3).'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a citation of a long hadith from several sources, summarized by the author. It begins with the Prophet's mention of the Dajjal, causing the companions to think he was nearby. The Prophet then lists several important points: 1) His greatest fear for the community is not the Dajjal but other trials; he instructs that if the Dajjal appears during his lifetime, he will personally argue; if not, each believer must argue for themselves. 2) He describes the Dajjal's appearance: a young man with curly hair and a blind eye, resembling Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan. 3) He recommends reciting the opening of Surah al-Kahf as protection. 4) The Dajjal will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq. 5) His stay on earth will be forty days of varying lengths (like a year, month, week, then normal days); the Prophet clarifies that on the long day, prayers must be estimated. 6) His speed is compared to rain driven by wind. 7) He will perform apparent miracles: causing rain and vegetation, and killing a youth then reviving him. 8) Jesus (peace be upon him) will descend east of Damascus, wearing two garments, and will pursue the Dajjal to the gate of Lud and kill him. The footnotes explain the phrases: (1) 'in a cluster of palm trees' means they thought he was nearby; (2) 'gap' means a road; (1) on page 320 explains 'between two garments' as two yellow garments; (2) identifies Lud as a town in Palestine near Jerusalem; (3) refers to the full text in Muslim.

Key Terms
دجال
سورة الكهف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet instruct to recite for protection against the Dajjal?
A) Surah al-Ikhlas
B) The opening verses of Surah al-Kahf
C) Surah al-Fatihah
D) The Throne Verse

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's description is known; believers are to recite Surah al-Kahf and remain steadfast.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Dajjal appeared today, would you be able to recite the opening verses of Surah al-Kahf from memory? Have you made a habit of studying and memorizing them?
?
The Prophet said each person will argue for themselves when he is not among us. Are you confident in your own understanding of truth to refute falsehood? What concrete steps are you taking to prepare?
?
The Dajjal will wreak havoc right and left. In what areas of your life are you most vulnerable to being deceived by false promises or trials? How will you 'be steadfast' starting today?

The Unusual Duration of the Dajjal's Stay
Hadith excerpt on the duration of the Dajjal's stay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique forty-day period of the Dajjal's rule, including the varying lengths of days and how prayers are to be estimated.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's days are not normal; prayer times must be estimated by proportion.

The companions asked about the length of the Dajjal's fitna. The Prophet's answer reveals that his stay will be forty days, but with days of unusual length—some like a year, a month, or a week. This passage clarifies how believers are to maintain their prayers during this extraordinary time.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer about duration
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the companions first ask about the length of stay, then about the day like a year.
2
Identify the four types of days
The Prophet lists four categories: a day like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, and the rest like normal days.
The order is important: one day equals a year, then a month, then a week, then normal.
3
Understand the prayer ruling
When asked about the day like a year, the Prophet does not suspend prayers but commands to estimate the times. Reflect on how this shows the importance of continuous worship.
This refutes a literal understanding of solar days; it's a period of trial with altered time perception.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the day like a year is a literal 365-day period where only one prayer is needed.
Correction: The Prophet's instruction to 'estimate its due measure' shows that it is not a literal solar day but a trial with altered time perception; all five daily prayers must still be observed by estimation.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about performing prayers on the day that is like a year?
A) It is sufficient to pray one fajr and one maghrib
B) Estimate the times for each prayer
C) No prayer is required on that day
D) Pray only the five obligatory prayers without Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's forty days include unusual lengths, but believers must estimate prayer times and maintain worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a period of darkness or confusion that seems endless (like a 'year-long day'), how do you ensure you still fulfill your obligations to Allah? Are you tempted to abandon or reduce your prayers because 'it's too long'? What does the Prophet's command 'estimate its measure' demand from you today?
?
The companions were concerned about prayer on an abnormally long day. Are you as vigilant about your prayers even when your schedule or circumstances feel unusual? What is one concrete change you can make to ensure you never miss a prayer, no matter how chaotic your day becomes?

The Miracles and Downfall of the Dajjal
Hadith excerpt on the Dajjal's miracles and his death by Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false miracles of the Dajjal, his speed, and the descent of Jesus to kill him, as described in the hadith.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's deceptive miracles are undone by the arrival of Jesus who kills him.

The hadith continues with the Dajjal's speed across the earth and his ability to perform apparent miracles like bringing rain, making vegetation grow, and reviving the dead. These deceptions will lead many astray until Jesus descends from heaven, catches him at the gate of Lud, and kills him. This passage lays out the final phase of the Dajjal's fitna and its conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read about the Dajjal's speed and miracles
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the comparison of his speed to rain driven by wind. Then identify the two false miracles: causing rain/vegetation and killing/reviving a youth.
2
Observe the reaction of the people
The Dajjal calls people and they believe. His miracles are convincing to those without faith.
3
Read about the descent of Jesus
Pay attention to the description of Jesus: his appearance, his location of descent (east of Damascus), and his mission to kill the Dajjal.
Jesus wears two yellow garments and has angels supporting him.
4
Reflect on the final defeat
The Dajjal is caught at the gate of Lud and killed. This ends his fitna.

?

?

?

What is one concrete action you will take this week to deepen your reliance on Allah's guidance alone, not on showy miracles, so that you remain steadfast in the face of fitan?

The Distinctive Signs of the Dajjal
Buti relates Ibn Sayyad's story and enumerates Dajjal's signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinguishing signs of the Dajjal as described in the hadith and how they clarify confusion about his identity.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is identified by a set of specific signs, not by one trait alone.

This passage presents a historical anecdote about Ibn Sayyad, a figure suspected of being the Dajjal, followed by a summary of the authentic signs of the Dajjal from the hadith. The story shows how mere claims can be misleading, while the list of signs provides clear criteria for recognizing the Dajjal.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of Ibn Sayyad
Read the narration carefully to understand the context and his arguments against being the Dajjal.
Notice how Ibn Sayyad tries to refute the prophecies about the Dajjal.
2
Identify the contradiction
Ibn Sayyad claims to have done things the Dajjal cannot do: convert to Islam, have a child, and enter Mecca. Understand why this could cause confusion.
3
Examine the list of signs
Read the summary of the Dajjal's signs. List each sign mentioned: Jewish origin, emergence from east, blind right eye, no children, cannot enter Mecca/Medina, 'kafir' on forehead, killed by Jesus.
These signs are derived from multiple hadiths.
4
Reflect on the importance of multiple signs
Consider why having many signs is important: it prevents mistaken identity and clarifies that the Dajjal is a specific being with unique characteristics.
The story of Ibn Sayyad shows how even a convincing impostor can be ruled out by the full set of signs.

4 - وروى مسلم وغيره عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : قال لي ابن صائد واسمه صاف ، يهودي الأصل يمارس الكهانة ، كان يشاع في المدينة أنه ربما كان هو الدجال : مالي ومالكم يا أصحاب محمد ، ألم يقل نبي الله إنه يهودي وقد أسلمت ، وقال لا يولد له وقد ولد لي ، وقال إنه لا يدخل مكة وقد حججت . قال فما زال حتى كاد أن يأخذ في قوله . وهذا إن مجموع الأحاديث المختلفة الواردة في حقه ، تبين أنه ذو علامات فارقة كثيرة . فهو يهودي الأصل ، ويكون ظهوره من جهة المشرق ، على خلاف في البقعة المعينة التي يكون خروجه منها ، وعينه اليمنى عوراء جاحظة وطافية بشكل منكر ، ولا يولد له ولد ، ولا يُمكن من دخول مكة والمدينة ، مكتوب على جبهته ( كافر ) يتبينها كل مسلم ، ويقتله عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام .
4 - Muslim and others narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: Ibn Sayyad, whose name was Saf, of Jewish origin, practicing divination, and it was rumored in Medina that he might be the Dajjal, said to me: What is wrong between me and you, O companions of Muhammad? Did not the Prophet of Allah say that he (the Dajjal) is Jewish, and I have become Muslim? He said he would have no children, and I have been given a child. He said he would not enter Mecca, and I have performed Hajj. He said: He kept going until he almost convinced him. And this is because the totality of the various hadiths narrated concerning him show that he has many distinguishing signs. He is of Jewish origin, his emergence will be from the east, though there is disagreement about the specific location. His right eye is blind, protuberant, and extremely ugly. He will have no children. He will not be able to enter Mecca and Medina. On his forehead is written 'kafir' (disbeliever), which every Muslim will discern. And Jesus, son of Mary (peace be upon him), will kill him.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage first narrates a hadith about Ibn Sayyad, a Jewish diviner who was suspected of being the Dajjal. He argued with Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, pointing out that some prophecies about the Dajjal did not apply to him: he had converted to Islam, had a child, and had performed Hajj, contradicting the hadith. The narrator says he almost convinced him. The author then comments that the collective hadiths about the Dajjal show many distinguishing signs. He lists them: the Dajjal is of Jewish origin; he emerges from the east; his right eye is blind and ugly; he has no children; he cannot enter Mecca and Medina; on his forehead is written 'kafir'; and he will be killed by Jesus (peace be upon him). This summary serves to clarify the true characteristics of the Dajjal, distinguishing him from impostors like Ibn Sayyad.

يهودي الأصل
عينه اليمنى عوراء
مكتوب على جبهته كافر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any one-eyed man or charismatic figure could be the Dajjal.
Correction: The Dajjal has a specific set of signs that include Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a blind right eye, childlessness, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'kafir' on his forehead, and being killed by Jesus. These signs together uniquely identify him.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is distinguished by a set of specific signs including Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a blind right eye, childlessness, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'kafir' on his forehead, and being killed by Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What does this teach you about the danger of judging by appearances instead of relying on the full prophetic description? How can you train yourself to trust the collective evidence of revelation over partial facts when evaluating truth claims in your own life?
?
The Dajjal's signs are specific and many. Yet many people today follow false prophets who exhibit only a few superficial traits. Where in your own heart do you find a tendency to accept a partial truth as the whole truth because it is comfortable or convenient? What habit can you adopt to ensure you seek the complete teaching of Islam before forming a conviction?

The Dajjal's Deceptions and the Descent of Jesus
Author recounts a hadith describing the Dajjal's miracles and Jesus' descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith describing the Dajjal's deceptive miracles and how Jesus will descend to kill him.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's miracles are tricks; only Jesus can stop him.

The author begins by presenting a prophetic hadith that vividly illustrates the Dajjal's powers and the ultimate intervention of Jesus. This story establishes the Dajjal as a deceptive figure whose apparent miracles are temporary and limited. Let's read the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the Dajjal's actions
Read the first part of the hadith describing how the Dajjal brings rain and vegetation, and kills and revives a man. Notice the deceptive nature of these acts.
These miracles are tests for believers.
2
Understand Jesus' descent
Read the description of Jesus' descent from heaven, including the specific location and his appearance. Note how he pursues and kills the Dajjal.
This emphasizes that only divine power can overcome the Dajjal.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the Prophet gave these details. The Dajjal's ability to mimic divine acts is part of his fitna, but his defeat is certain.

He said: 'Like a rain cloud driven by the wind, it comes upon a people, and he calls them, and they believe in him and respond to him. Then he commands the sky and it rains, and the earth and it grows. Then he calls a man full of youth, strikes him with a sword and cuts him into two pieces the distance of an arrow shot. Then he calls him, and he comes back with a shining face laughing. While he is like that, behold! Allah sends the Messiah, son of Mary. He descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two yellow garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels. When he lowers his head, drops fall, and when he raises it, pearls like pearls trickle from him. He seeks him (i.e., seeks the Dajjal) until he catches him at the gate of Lud and kills him.' And Muslim and others narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: Ibn Sayyad [whose name is Saf, a Jew by origin, practiced soothsaying, it was rumored in Medina that he might be the Dajjal] said to me: 'What is between me and you, O companions of Muhammad? Did not the Prophet of Allah say that he is a Jew, and I have embraced Islam? He said he would have no children, and I have had a child. He said he would not perform Hajj, and I have performed Hajj?' He said: He kept on until he almost conceded to his statement. This, and all the various hadiths reported about him, show that he has many distinguishing signs. So he is of Jewish origin, his appearance will be from the east, with a difference of opinion about the precise location from which he will emerge. His right eye is blind, bulging, and floating in a hideous manner. He will have no children, he will not be allowed to enter Mecca and Medina, on his forehead is written 'Kafir' which every Muslim will discern, and Jesus son of Mary (peace be upon him) will kill him.

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadiths describing the Dajjal and a summary of his distinguishing signs. It begins with a lengthy hadith (attributed to someone, likely the Prophet) detailing the Dajjal's actions: he brings rain and vegetation, kills and revives a man, and then Jesus descends to kill him. The description of Jesus' descent includes specific details about the location (east of Damascus, at the white minaret) and his appearance. Then a second hadith is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri concerning Ibn Sayyad, a Jewish soothsayer rumored to be the Dajjal. The hadith records a conversation where Ibn Sayyad tries to refute the Prophet's predictions about the Dajjal's Jewishness, childlessness, and inability to perform Hajj. The passage then concludes with a list of the Dajjal's definitive signs synthesised from multiple hadiths: Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a deformed right eye, no children, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'Kafir' written on his forehead, and his death at the hands of Jesus. The passage thus serves to gather scriptural evidence about the Dajjal's identity and fate.

Correction: The hadith shows his revival is a deceptive act; it is not true creation. Only Allah gives life, and Jesus, a prophet, kills him, proving his mortality.

The Distinguishing Signs of the Dajjal
Author presents a hadith about Ibn Sayyad and then lists the Dajjal's distinguishing signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the definitive signs of the Dajjal as synthesized from multiple hadiths.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's identity is unmasked by specific, unmistakable signs.

The author then presents a hadith about a historical figure (Ibn Sayyad) who was suspected to be the Dajjal, followed by a summary of the Dajjal's distinguishing signs compiled from various traditions. This lesson focuses on these signs and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ibn Sayyad incident
Read the hadith where Ibn Sayyad defends himself against allegations of being the Dajjal. Notice how he tries to refute the Prophet's predictions.
This shows that the Dajjal's signs are definitive and cannot be masked.
2
Identify the signs
Read the list of signs that follow. Each sign is a clear marker of the Dajjal's identity.
Count the signs: there are seven signs mentioned.
3
Memorize the signs
Try to commit these signs to memory. They are important for recognizing the Dajjal when he appears.
The signs include his origin, appearance, and limitations.
