How Dajjal's 'Miracles' Differ from Prophetic Signs
Ibn Hajar answers an objection about Dajjal's miracles, using his defects to distinguish them from prophetic signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Dajjal's miracles, despite being stunning, do not prove his truthfulness, as they are accompanied by clear marks of falsehood and serve as a divine trial.

Core Idea
A miracle plus a mark of falsehood is a test, not a proof.

Ibn Hajar addresses a powerful objection: if the Dajjal can revive the dead, how can he be a liar? The answer reveals a key principle: a supposed miracle is not automatically a sign of truth when accompanied by undeniable signs of falsehood. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its implications for distinguishing prophetic miracles from mere wonders.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
First, read the passage where Ibn Hajar presents the objection about reviving the dead and then provides the answer. Notice the structure: a question followed by a clear rebuttal.
The objection is a common one - anyone can perform wonders seems truthful.
2
Identify the marks of falsehood
Ibn Hajar lists several defects: being one-eyed, 'Kafir' on the forehead, inability to remove his own flaws. List each and see how they contradict any claim to divinity.
3
Contrast with prophetic miracles
Prophetic miracles are free from such contradictions. Reflect on why a true prophet's miracles would not carry defects.
This contrast helps you see the logic behind the ruling.
4
Understand the purpose: trial
The answer emphasizes that these wonders are a fitna (trial). Consider why Allah would allow such signs for a false figure.
The trial lies in choosing between clear evidence (the marks) and dazzling events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحافظ ابن حجر : فإن قلت كيف يُجري الله الآيات الباهرة على يده من مثل إحياء الموتى ، وهو من الآيات العظام التي لا تكون إلا للأنبياء ؟!.. فالجواب : إنه على سبيل الفتنة للعباد ، إذ كان عندهم ما يدل على أنـه مبطل غير محق في دعواه ، وهو أنه أعور مكتوب على جبهته كافر يقرؤه كل مسلم ، فدعواه داحضة ، مع وسم الكفر ونقص الذات والقدر ، إذ لو كان إلها لأزال ذلك عن وجهه ، وآيات الأنبياء سالمة عن المعارضة فلا يشتبهان .. ثم قال : وفي الدجال مع ذلك دلالة بينة ، لمن عقل ، على كذبه ، لأنه ذو أجزاء مؤلفة ، وتأثير الصنعة فيه ظاهر مع ظهور الآفة به من عور عينه ، فإذا دعا الناس إلى أنه ، فأسوأ حال من يراه من ذوي العقول أن يعلم أنه لم يكن ربهم ليسوّي خلق غيره ويعدله ويحسنه ، ولا يدفع النقص عن نفسه ، فأقل ما يجب أن يقول : يا من يزعم أنه خالق السماوات والأرض ، صور نفسك وعدلها ، وأزل عنها العاهة . فإن زعمت أن الربا لا يحدث في نفسه شيئاً ، فأزل ما هو مكتوب بين عينيك . قلت : وقد علمت أن الله عز وجل جعل ظهور الدجال ، فتنة خطيرة كبرى للناس ، كما بين الرسول مع الله وكما أنذر : ولو لم يكن قد مكنه الله من إحداث بعض الخوارق وجعل إليه مقاليد كثير من الخيرات والأرزاق ، لما كان فتنة إذا علمت هذا ، فاعلم أنه ليس للبحث العقلي أي سبيل إلى تحليل شخصية هذا الإنسان ودراسته ، من وراء هذا الذي أخبرت به النصوص الصحيحة . إذ إن المنفذ العقلي الوحيد إلى فهم أي شيء عنه إنما هو الخبر اليقيني ، ولولا ورود هذا الخبر لما تصورنا وجوده أصلاً فضلاً عن اعتقاده والإيمان بظهوره
Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: If you say: How does Allah manifest stunning signs at his hand such as reviving the dead, while these are among the great signs that occur only for prophets?! The answer: It is by way of trials for the servants, since they have evidence that he is false and not truthful in his claim. That is because he is one-eyed, written on his forehead is 'Kafir' which every Muslim reads. So his claim is null, along with the mark of disbelief and the defect in essence and power. For if he were a god, he would have removed that from his face. And the signs of prophets are free from contradiction, so they are not confused. Then he said: In the Dajjal, despite that, there is a clear proof for those who understand of his lying, because he is composed of parts, the effect of craftsmanship is apparent in him, and affliction is apparent in him from his blind eye. So when he calls people to [believe] that he is [god], the worst state for those of intellect who see him is that they know that he is not their lord, for he cannot create another being, nor balance and perfect it, nor remove defect from himself. The least that should be said is: O you who claim to be the creator of the heavens and the earth, form yourself and balance yourself, and remove the defect from yourself. If you claim that the Lord does not create anything in Himself, then remove what is written between your eyes. I say: You have known that Allah (Mighty and Majestic) made the emergence of the Dajjal a great and serious trial for people, as the Messenger informed from Allah and as he warned. If Allah had not empowered him to produce some miracles and placed in his hands many goods and provisions, he would not be a trial. Once you know this, know that rational inquiry has no way to analyze this man's character or study him beyond what the authentic texts have informed. For the only rational access to understanding anything about him is certain report (al-khabr al-yaqini). Were it not for this report, we would not have conceived of his existence at all, let alone believe in him and have faith in his emergence.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage contains an objection-and-answer format followed by the author's own commentary. First, Ibn Hajar raises a plausible objection: If the Dajjal performs stunning miracles like reviving the dead, which are usually only granted to prophets, how can he be an impostor? The answer is twofold: (1) These acts are a trial (fitna) for people, not a validation of truth. (2) The Dajjal bears unmistakable marks of falsehood: he is one-eyed, and 'Kafir' is written on his forehead for all Muslims to see. If he were a god, he would remove these defects. Prophetic miracles are not accompanied by such contradictions. Ibn Hajar then adds a rational proof: the Dajjal is a composite being with clear imperfections, so he cannot be the perfect creator. A rational person would challenge him to perfect his own form and remove his defect. The author (Ramadan Buti) then comments that the Dajjal is a great trial, and if he lacked miraculous powers, he would not be a trial. Finally, he asserts that rational inquiry cannot penetrate the nature of the Dajjal beyond what revelation states; the only valid source of knowledge here is authentic prophetic report (al-khabr al-yaqini). Without that report, we would not even know of his existence. Thus the passage defends the compatibility of miracles with falsehood in the context of divine trial and emphasizes the supremacy of revelation over reason in eschatological matters.

Key Terms

الفتنة
الدجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any supernatural event proves the person is truthful and from God.
Correction: A miracle is only a sign of truth when it is free from contradictions and accompanying marks of falsehood, as Ibn Hajar explains. The Dajjal's case shows that wonders can be a trial, not a proof.

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Ibn Hajar gives for why Dajjal's miracles do not prove his truthfulness?
A) The miracles are not real; they are illusions
B) The Dajjal's miracles are not witnessed by many people
C) The Dajjal bears visible defects and a mark of disbelief
D) The Dajjal's miracles cause harm instead of benefit

Key Takeaway
A miracle is not automatically a sign of truth; it must be free from accompanying marks of falsehood to be considered a prophetic sign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone claiming to have spiritual gifts or signs from Allah, do you examine their character for marks of falsehood, or are you easily impressed by outward wonders? What defect would you overlook in yourself that disproves your own authority?
?
The Dajjal's miracles will be breathtaking, yet the test is to reject them based on clear signs of falsehood. If you were faced with such a spectacle, would your love for the truth overcome your desire for the miraculous?
?
Ibn Hajar points out that the Dajjal cannot even perfect his own form. How often do you claim knowledge or leadership while failing to remove the obvious 'defects' between your own eyes—your unchecked pride, anger, or hypocrisy? What is the one defect you must remove today?

The Limits of Rational Inquiry: Dajjal and Revelation
Author Buti concludes that rational inquiry cannot penetrate the Dajjal's reality; only certain reports from revelation provide knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational inquiry cannot analyze the Dajjal's nature or existence beyond what is revealed in authentic texts, and why certain reports (khabar yaqini) are the only valid source of knowledge here.

Core Idea
Reason cannot access what revelation alone brings.

After establishing that the Dajjal's miracles are a trial, the author (Ramadan Buti) draws a crucial methodological conclusion: the Dajjal, as an eschatological figure, cannot be studied through rational inquiry. The only path to knowledge about him is through certain reports from revelation (al-khabr al-yaqini). This lesson explores why reason hits its limit and why submission to revelation is necessary in such matters.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of Dajjal's miracles
The author states that the Dajjal would not be a trial without his miraculous powers. Reflect on this: the trial includes both the wonders and the clear evidence of falsehood.
This sets the stage for why reason is insufficient.
2
Identify the limit of reason
The author explicitly says 'rational inquiry has no way to analyze this man's character or study him beyond what the authentic texts have informed.' Find this statement and see how it limits our tools.
3
Understand the role of certain report
The only 'rational access' is through al-khabr al-yaqini. Consider what makes a report certain in Islamic epistemology.
This is not a rejection of reason but an acknowledgment of its boundaries.
4
Apply the principle
Without revelation, we would not even know of the Dajjal's existence. Ask yourself: what other doctrines depend solely on revelation?
This principle applies to all sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation).

Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: If you say: How does Allah manifest stunning signs at his hand such as reviving the dead, while these are among the great signs that occur only for prophets?! The answer: It is by way of trials for the servants, since they have evidence that he is false and not truthful in his claim. Ibn Hajar's Refutation of the Dajjal's Divinity
Ibn Hajar refutes the Dajjal's claim to divinity using physical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Hajar's rational argument that the Dajjal's physical defects and composite nature disprove his claim to divinity, despite his apparent miracles.

Core Idea
Physical flaws expose the Dajjal's false divinity – a god cannot be imperfect.

Ibn Hajar addresses a critical question: if the Dajjal performs miracles like reviving the dead, how can his claim to divinity be false? He responds with a twofold argument from physical evidence: the Dajjal's one eye and the word 'kafir' on his forehead are clear signs of imperfection that no god would tolerate, and his composite nature proves he is created. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Ibn Hajar begins with an imagined objection: 'How can God allow such great miracles at the hand of the Dajjal?'
The objection is a common one – miracles seem to confirm truth.
2
Examine the first answer: the defects disprove divinity
Ibn Hajar answers that the miracles are a test (fitna), but the clear defects (being one-eyed and having 'kafir' written) show the Dajjal is false. A god would remove these imperfections.
The word 'dahida' means invalid, completely false.
3
Understand the second argument: composite nature
The Dajjal is composed of parts, showing he is created. A creator cannot be created. The effect of craftsmanship is evident in his body, and he cannot remove his own defects.
This argument relies on the principle that what is composite needs a maker.
4
Reflect on the lesson's takeaway
Consider how this argument protects believers from being deceived by false miracles. The presence of clear indicators of falsehood (defects) alongside miracles shows the miracles are a test, not a certification of truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحافظ ابن حجر : فإن قلت كيف يُجري الله الآيات الباهرة على يده من مثل إحياء الموتى ، وهو من الآيات العظام التي لا تكون إلا للأنبياء ؟!.. فالجواب : إنه على سبيل الفتنة للعباد ، إذ كان عندهم ما يدل على أنه مبطل غير محق في دعواه ، وهو أنه أعور مكتوب على جبهته كافر يقرؤه كل مسلم ، فدعواه داحضة ، مع وسم الكفر ونقص الذات والقدر ، إذ لو كان إلها لأزال ذلك عن وجهه ، وآيات الأنبياء سالمة عن المعارضة فلا يشتبهان .. ثم قال : وفي الدجال مع ذلك دلالة بينة ، لمن عقل ، على كذبه ، لأنه ذو أجزاء مؤلفة ، وتأثير الصنعة فيه ظاهر مع ظهور الآفة به من عور عينه ، فإذا دعا الناس إلى أنه ، فأسوأ حال من يراه من ذوي العقول أن يعلم أنه لم يكن ربهم ليسوي خلق غيره ويعدله ويحسنه ، ولا يدفع النقص عن نفسه ، فأقل ما يجب أن يقول : يا من يزعم أنه خالق السماوات والأرض ، صور نفسك وعدلها ، وأزل عنها العاهة . فإن زعمت أن الرب لا يحدث في نفسه شيئاً ، فأزل ما هو مكتوب بين عينيك
Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: If you say, 'How does God bring about manifest miracles at his hand, such as reviving the dead, which are among the great miracles that occur only for prophets?' The answer: It is as a trial (fitna) for the servants, since they have something that indicates that he is false and not truthful in his claim – namely, that he is one-eyed and written on his forehead is 'kafir' which every Muslim reads. So his claim is invalid, along with the brand of disbelief and the deficiency of essence and power. For if he were a god, he would remove that from his face. The miracles of prophets are safe from opposition, so they are not confused. Then he said: In the Dajjal, moreover, there is a clear indication, for one who understands, of his falsehood, because he is composed of parts and the effect of craftsmanship is apparent in him, along with the appearance of defect upon him from the blindness of his eye. So if he calls people to claim divinity, the worst state of one who sees him among the intelligent is that he knows that he is not their Lord who creates others, and equalizes and perfects them, and does not remove defect from himself. The least one should say is: 'O you who claim to be the Creator of the heavens and the earth, form yourself and perfect it, and remove the defect from it.' For if you claim that the Lord does not bring about anything in Himself, then remove what is written between your eyes.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof: Ibn Hajar refutes the claim that the Dajjal could be divine despite performing apparent miracles. He quotes an imaginary objector who asks how God could allow such miracles through a false claimant. The answer is that these miracles are a test (fitna), not a certification of truth, because there are clear indicators of falsehood: the Dajjal is one-eyed and the word 'kafir' is visibly written on his forehead for every Muslim to read. These defects prove his claim is 'dahida' (false). If he were a god, he would have removed these imperfections. Prophetic miracles are never accompanied by such contradictions. Ibn Hajar then adds a second argument: the Dajjal's composite nature (having parts) and the obvious effect of craftsmanship on him, along with his physical defect, demonstrate that he cannot be the Creator. Any intelligent person would see that he is not the Lord who perfectly creates others yet cannot perfect himself. The minimal response to his claim is a demand: if you claim to be the Creator, perfect your own form and remove your defect. If you argue that the Lord does not cause change in Himself, then change what is written on your forehead — but he cannot. Thus his claim is self-refuting.

Misconception: One might think that the Dajjal's miracles (like reviving the dead) prove that his claim to divinity is true.
Correction: Ibn Hajar shows that the Dajjal's physical defects (one eye, written 'kafir') and his composite nature are clear indicators that he is false. Miracles can be a test, not a certification of truth.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hajar, what is the primary evidence that the Dajjal is not divine despite performing miracles?
A) His miracles are weak and unconvincing.
B) He has physical defects that a god would remove.
C) The Quran declares him a liar.
D) He admits he is a liar.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's physical defects and composite nature are definitive proof that he is not divine; a true god would be free from imperfection and need no creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Hajar says the Dajjal's defects expose his falsehood. What defects in your own character are you aware of but have been ignoring, allowing them to contradict your claim to something you are not?
?
If you were to demand of yourself, 'Form yourself and perfect it, and remove the defect from yourself,' what one defect would you be most ashamed to face? Will you begin today to remove it, or will you remain like the Dajjal, unable to change?
?
The Dajjal's miracles were a trial. Think of a 'miracle' or blessing in your life that could become a test for you—something that makes you feel self-sufficient. Are you using it to draw closer to Allah or to feed your ego?

The Descent of Jesus: A Major Sign of the Hour
Buti defines the descent of Jesus and its purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of Jesus's descent as one of the major signs of the Hour, his current state of concealment, and his role in establishing the Islamic creed and implementing Islamic Sharia.

Core Idea
Jesus will descend to implement the final Islamic Sharia, not a new law.

This lesson examines a key eschatological event: the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him). It clarifies where Jesus is now, why he will descend, and what he will do. As you read, note that the passage emphasizes that Jesus will uphold the same Islamic creed all prophets proclaimed and will enforce the Islamic Sharia that supersedes all earlier laws.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to key terms like نزول عيسى, أشراط الساعة, الاحتجاب, ملكوت الله, الشريعة الإسلامية الناسخة.
The Arabic text is continuous; notice the flow from definition to purpose.
2
Identify the two purposes of Jesus's descent
The passage mentions two main tasks: establishing the pillars of the Islamic creed and implementing the Islamic Sharia that abrogates previous laws. Find these in the text.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why is this event considered one of the most important and dangerous signs of the Hour? How does it affirm Jesus's prophethood and the finality of Islamic law?
This connects to the broader Islamic eschatological narrative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲ - نزول عيسى ابن مريم : وهو من أهم أشراط الساعة ، ومن أخطر الأحداث التي تكون بين يديها ومعنى نزوله ، أنه يهبط إلى الأرض ، بعد احتجابه عنها كل هذه الحقبة الطويلة من الدهر ، في مكان ما من ملكوت الله عز وجل ، وهو لا يزال يتمتع بحياته الأولى التي أحياه الله بها إذ كان في الأرض رسولاً نبياً . فيمكث في الأرض مدة من الزمن يقيم عليها دعائم العقيدة الإسلامية التي بعث هو والأنبياء كلهم لإقامتها ، وينفذ الشريعة الإسلامية الناسخة لجميع الشرائع السابقة والتي بعث بها
2 – The descent of Jesus son of Mary: It is one of the most important signs of the Hour and one of the most dangerous events that occur during its approach. The meaning of his descent is that he will descend to earth, after being concealed from it throughout this long period of time, from some place in the dominion (malkut) of God, Mighty and Majestic, while he still enjoys his first life with which God gave him life when he was on earth as a messenger and prophet. He will remain on earth for a period of time, establishing upon it the pillars of the Islamic creed which he and all the prophets were sent to establish, and he will implement the Islamic Sharia that abrogates all previous laws and which was sent.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the descent of Jesus (Isa ibn Maryam) as a major eschatological event. The author states it is one of the most important signs of the Hour and one of the most dangerous events preceding it. The meaning of 'nuzul' (descent) is that Jesus will physically descend to earth after having been concealed (ihtijab) from it for a very long period. He is currently in some location within God's dominion (malkut), still alive with the same life he had on earth as a messenger and prophet. Upon descending, he will stay for a time, establishing the foundations of the Islamic creed — the same creed all prophets came to establish — and he will implement the Islamic Sharia which abrogates all previous laws. This passage clarifies the nature and purpose of Jesus' second coming within Islamic eschatology.

The Wisdom of Not Naming the Dajjal in the Quran
Answers why the Dajjal is not named in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Dajjal's name is not mentioned in the Quran and how this reflects Allah's wisdom and the Quran's stylistic pattern.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is too insignificant to be named in Allah's eternal speech.

An objection is raised: if the Dajjal is such a major figure of the end times, why is he not named in the Quran? In this passage, the author provides a two-part answer: first, the Dajjal is too insignificant for his name to be recorded in the Quran; second, the Quran's pattern is to only name prophets and some tyrants they were sent to. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the first part of the passage from 'والجواب' to 'بالذكر والتعيين' to see the two reasons given.
2
Reflect on the concept of hikmah
Consider why the author emphasizes that the Dajjal is 'ahwan' (more insignificant) in Allah's sight. What does this teach about Allah's majesty?
3
Compare with Quranic pattern
Notice the author's point about the Quran's general style of not naming individuals except prophets and some tyrants. How does this support the answer?
This is a common feature of Quranic narratives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب : إنه لا يبعد أن تكون الحكمة ذلك أن الدجال أهون على الله من أن يسجل اسمه في كتابه وكلامه القديم، يتلى على ألسنة الناس في كل زمان ومكان . وقد درج القرآن في أسلوبه وإخباراته على عدم ذكر الأسماء - اللهم إلا أسماء الرسل والأنبياء - وبعض الطغاة الذين أرسلوا إليهم . أفيخص الدجال وحده بالذكر والتعيين ؟! .. ومهما يكن فإن الخبر الصادق الذي يتحتم الاعتقاد بموجبه ليس محصوراً في القرآن فقط ، بل هو كما يكون في القرآن يكون في السنة أيضاً ، إذا وصل إلينا بطرق صحيحة متواترة وقد شاعت أخيراً ( تقليعة ( بين بعض المتفيقهين المنافقين الذين يظهرون ما لا يبطنون وهي أن أحدهم يمسك بحكم من أحكام الشريعة المجمع عليها ، ثم يطالبك أن تأتيه بنص عليه في القرآن : والقرآن فقط ، وإلا فهو لا يعتد به ! ..
وهو
ومن أجل هذا فإنك تجد الواحد منهم يسأل مثل هذه الأسئلة لا يؤدي صلاة ولا صوماً ولا يلتزم شعيرة من شعائر الإسلام. إذ كان عذره أن القرآن لم يترح له كيفية الصلاة والصيام وبقية الأحكام ! .. ومقتضى منطق هؤلاء أن يتركوا القرآن الذي تنزل على محمد الله ، ولا يعتمدوا إلا على قرآن ينزل على كل منهم مباشرة ، فذلك أقطع للشك وأنفى للريبة
The answer: It is not far that the wisdom is that the Dajjal is too insignificant in the sight of Allah for his name to be recorded in His book and His ancient speech, to be recited on the tongues of people at all times and places. The Quran has been accustomed in its style and reports to not mentioning names - except for the names of messengers and prophets - and some of the tyrants to whom they were sent. Should the Dajjal be singled out for mention and specification?! ... However, the truthful report which it is obligatory to believe is not confined to the Quran only, but just as it is in the Quran, it is also in the Sunnah, if it reaches us through authentic and mutawatir chains. Recently a trend has spread among some hypocritical pseudo-faqihs who show what they do not conceal, which is that one of them holds onto a ruling of the Sharia that is unanimously agreed upon, then demands that you bring him a text for it in the Quran: only the Quran, otherwise he does not consider it! ... For this reason, you find one of them asking such questions, not performing prayer or fasting or adhering to any ritual of Islam, because his excuse is that the Quran did not mention for him the method of prayer, fasting, and the rest of the rulings! ... The logic of these people requires that they abandon the Quran which was revealed to Muhammad, and rely only on a Quran revealed to each of them directly, for that is more conclusive for doubt and more repelling of suspicion.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objection, implied, is why the Dajjal is not mentioned by name in the Quran. The author's answer gives two reasons: first, the Dajjal is too insignificant to be named in the eternal speech; second, the Quran's style is not to mention names except for prophets and some tyrants. Then the author expands to a broader principle: the 'truthful report' (al-khabr al-sadiq) that must be believed is not limited to the Quran but includes the Sunnah when authentically and mutawatirly transmitted. This leads to a critique of a recent trend among hypocritical pseudo-jurists who demand a Quranic text for every sharia ruling, rejecting hadith entirely. The author exposes the absurdity of their position by noting that even basic obligations like prayer and fasting have their detailed methods described not in the Quran but in the Sunnah. He concludes that such logic would force them to abandon the Quran and seek a personal revelation, which is absurd.

Key Terms
الدجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the Dajjal not named in the Quran?
A) Because the Quran only names prophets and angels.
B) Because the Dajjal is too insignificant and the Quran's style is to rarely name individuals.
C) Because the Dajjal's name is too sacred.
D) Because the Dajjal will appear in the future.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is not named in the Quran because of his insignificance and the Quran's general pattern of not naming individuals except prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Dajjal is too insignificant to be named in Allah's eternal speech, how does that change the weight you give to your own fears and trials? Will you today recite a verse that reminds you of Allah's greatness whenever you feel overwhelmed?
?
The Quran only names prophets and their adversaries. Where do you see yourself in that divide? Take a moment to sincerely repent if you find your heart inclining towards the ways of the tyrants.
?
What is one specific fear about the future that you need to surrender to Allah right now, realizing it may be trivial in His sight? Write it down and commit to relying on Him alone.

The Authority of the Sunnah and the Refutation of the Quran-Only Trend
Asserts the authority of the Sunnah and refutes the Quran-only trend.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sunnah is an equally binding source of religious obligations when authentically transmitted, and the fallacy of rejecting it.

Core Idea
The truthful report is not limited to the Quran; the Sunnah is also binding.

The author moves from the specific case of Dajjal to a broader methodological issue. He asserts that the 'truthful report' (al-khabr al-sadiq) includes the Sunnah when transmitted via authentic and mutawatir chains. Then he critiques a contemporary trend of people who claim to follow the Quran alone and reject hadith, highlighting the absurdity by noting that the Quran itself does not detail the methods of prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read from 'ومهما يكن' to the end to understand the authority of Sunnah and the critique of Quran-only trend.
2
Understand 'khabar sadiq'
The author explains that the 'truthful report' which must be believed is not only in the Quran but also in the Sunnah if it reaches us via authentic mutawatir chains. Why is mutawatir important?
Mutawatir means transmitted by so many narrators that collusion on a lie is impossible.
3
Reflect on the critique
The author uses strong language to describe those who demand Quranic text for every ruling, calling them hypocrites and pseudo-faqihs. Why does he say their logic would force them to seek a personal Quran?
Because the Quran does not detail the methods of prayer, fasting, etc., so their position is self-defeating.

The Descent of Jesus and Its Implications
Defines the descent of Jesus and clarifies it does not contradict Muhammad's finality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of Jesus' descent, its purpose, and why it does not contradict Muhammad being the Seal of the Prophets.

Core Idea
Jesus returns to implement Muhammad's law, not to bring a new one.

One of the major signs of the Hour is the descent of Jesus. This passage from al-Buti explains its meaning and addresses a common concern: does it conflict with the finality of prophethood? Let's see how the author answers this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the key components
Notice that the passage defines the descent, states its purpose, and then addresses a potential objection regarding Muhammad's finality.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يناقض' (does not contradict).
3
Understand the argument
The author argues that Jesus descends to implement the Islamic Sharia without new revelation, so it does not contradict Muhammad being the final prophet.
This is a common point of confusion that the passage clarifies.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this doctrine is important for Islamic eschatology and how it reinforces the finality of Muhammad's prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ - نزول عيسى ابن مريم :
،
وهو من أهم أشراط الساعة ، ومن أخطر الأحداث التي تكون بين يديها ومعنى نزوله ، أنه يهبط إلى الأرض ، بعد احتجابه عنها كل هذه الحقبة الطويلة من الدهر ، في مكان ما من ملكوت الله عز وجل ، وهو لا يزال يتمتع بحياته الأولى التي أحياه الله بها إذ كان في الأرض رسولاً نبياً . فيمكث في الأرض مدة من الزمن يقيم عليها دعائم العقيدة الإسلامية التي بعث هو والأنبياء كلهم لإقامتها ، وينفذ الشريعة الإسلامية الناسخة لجميع الشرائع السابقة والتي بعث بها
محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، دون أن يؤيد خلال ذلك بوحي جديد من الله عز وجل .
وبذلك تعلم أن نزوله ، لا يناقض كون محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام هو خاتم الأنبياء وآخرهم ، كما لا يناقض أن شريعته ناسخة لجميع الشرائع وباقية إلى يوم القيامة .
2 - The Descent of Jesus Son of Mary: It is one of the most important signs of the Hour, and one of the most dangerous events that occur before it. The meaning of his descent is that he descends to the earth, after being concealed from it for this long period of time, in a place from the dominion of Allah Almighty, while he still enjoys his first life which Allah granted him when he was on earth as a messenger and prophet. He will remain on earth for a period of time to establish the foundations of the Islamic creed which he and all the prophets were sent to establish, and he will implement the Islamic Sharia which abrogates all previous laws, and which was sent with Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, without being supported during that by a new revelation from Allah Almighty. Thus you know that his descent does not contradict that Muhammad is the Seal of the Prophets and the last of them, just as it does not contradict that his Sharia abrogates all previous laws and remains until the Day of Resurrection.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage defines the descent of Jesus (nuzul 'Isa) and explains its significance. It begins by identifying it as a major sign of the Hour. The author then explains the meaning: Jesus will physically descend to earth after a long period of concealment, still alive in his original human life. His purpose is to establish the Islamic creed and implement the Islamic Sharia (shari'a islamiyya) that abrogates all previous laws, the same Sharia sent with Muhammad. Importantly, Jesus will not bring new revelation; he follows Muhammad's law. The author then directly addresses a potential objection: this does not contradict Muhammad being the Seal of the Prophets (khatam al-anbiya') or the finality of his Sharia. Thus, the descent is not a new prophetic mission but a reaffirmation of the existing message.

Key Terms
نزول عيسى
أشراط الساعة
خاتم الأنبياء
شريعة ناسخة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe Jesus' descent implies he brings a new law or contradicts Muhammad's finality.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Jesus descends to implement the existing Islamic Sharia without new revelation, so it does not contradict Muhammad being the final prophet.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of the descent of Jesus?
A) He will come as a new prophet with a new revelation.
B) He will descend to earth still alive and implement the Islamic Sharia.
C) He will abrogate the Sharia of Muhammad.
D) He will be born again.

Key Takeaway
The descent of Jesus reaffirms the Islamic creed and Sharia without contradicting Muhammad's finality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage emphasizes that Jesus will not bring new revelation. Does your heart fully accept that Islam is complete and final? What might you be unknowingly seeking outside of it?

The Major Signs of the Hour
Al-Buti enumerates ten major eschatological signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the list of major signs of the Hour as enumerated by Al-Buti, including the Smoke, Dajjal, Beast, and others.

Core Idea
Ten major signs precede the Hour, ending with a fire from Yemen.

Al-Buti begins by listing the major signs of the Hour, starting with the Smoke and ending with the fire that drives people to their gathering. This enumeration sets the eschatological context for the detailed discussion of each sign, especially the descent of Jesus.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration
Read the list of signs in Arabic and English. Notice the order: from cosmic signs to geographical sinkings to the final fire.
2
Identify each sign
Make a mental note of each sign: Smoke, Dajjal, Beast, sun rising from west, descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three sinkings, and the fire.
3
Reflect on the classification
Consider that these are the 'major' signs, distinct from minor signs. Al-Buti does not discuss minor signs here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدخان، والدجال، والدابة، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، ونزول عيسى بن مريم، ويأجوج ومأجوج، وثلاثة خسوف: خسف بالمشرق، وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب، وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم. ٣ - ما رويناه آنفاً عن مسلم وأبي داود والترمذي وأحمد وابن ماجه من حديث النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه عن رسول الله، بشأن الدجال، وفيه: فبينما هو كذلك إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم، فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مهرودتين واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر، وإذا رفعه تحدر منه جمان كاللؤلؤ، فلا يحل لكافر يجد ريح نفسه إلا مات، ونفسه ينتهي حيث ينتهي طرفه فيطلبه حتى يدركه بباب لد فيقتله ثم يأتي عيسى قوم قد عصمهم الله منه، فيمسح عن وجوههم ويحدثهم بدرجاتهم في الجنة ... الحديث ٤ - ما رواه أحمد وأبو داود وابن جرير بطرق مختلفة عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله: «الأنبياء إخوة لعلات، أمهاتهم شتى ودينهم واحد، صلى الله عليه وسلم وإني أولى الناس بعيسى بن مريم لأنه لم يكن نبي بيني وبينه، وإنه نازل فإذا رأيتموه فاعرفوه، رجل مربوع، إلى الحمرة والبياض، عليه ثوبان ممصران كأن رأسه يقطر وإن لم يصبه بلل: فيدق الصليب، ويقتل الخنزير، ويضع الجزية، ويدعو الناس إلى الإسلام، ويهلك الله في زمانه الملل كلها إلا الإسلام، ويهلك المسيح الدجال، فيمكث في الأرض أربعين سنة ثم يتوفى ويصلي عليه المسلمون فهذه أربعة أحاديث تنص على نزول عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وهنالك أحاديث كثيرة أخرى لا مجال لسردها هنا، والخلاصة أنها أحاديث متواترة عن رسول الله، من رواية أبي هريرة، وابن مسعود، وعثمان بن أبي العاص، وأبي أمامة، والنواس بن سمعان، وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص ومجمع بن حارثة، وحذيفة بن أسيد رضي الله عنهم وقد وقفت قبل ذلك على نصوص الآيات المحكمة من كتاب الله تعالى الناطقة بمثل ما دلت عليه هذه الأحاديث؛ فمن أجل ذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على الاعتقاد بنزول عيسى ابن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمن، على النحو وبالصفة التي ذكرها لنا رسول الله، وأنه إنما رفع ببدنه حياً إلى السماء كما بين الله عز وجل صريحاً في محكم بيانه
The Smoke, and the Dajjal, and the Beast, and the rising of the sun from its west, and the descent of Jesus son of Mary, and Gog and Magog, and three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that comes out of Yemen driving the people to their gathering place. 3 - What we related previously from Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ahmad, and Ibn Majah from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Messenger of Allah, concerning the Dajjal, and in it: 'While he is thus, Allah sends the Messiah son of Mary, and he descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two dyed garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels; when he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, drops fall from it like pearls; no disbeliever who smells his breath dies but he dies, and his breath reaches as far as his sight reaches; so he pursues him until he catches him at the gate of Ludd and kills him. Then Jesus comes to a people whom Allah has protected from him, and he wipes their faces and tells them of their ranks in Paradise... the hadith.' 4 - What Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Jarir narrated through various chains from Abu Hurayra, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The prophets are paternal brothers; their mothers are different but their religion is one. And I am the nearest of people to Jesus son of Mary because there was no prophet between me and him, and he will descend. When you see him, recognize him: a man of medium height, reddish-white, wearing two light-yellow garments, his head as if it is dripping though no moisture touches him. He will break the cross, kill the pig, impose the jizya, and call people to Islam. Allah will destroy in his time all religions except Islam, and he will destroy the Dajjal. Then he will remain on earth for forty years, then he will die, and the Muslims will pray over him.' So these are four hadiths that state the descent of Jesus son of Mary. There are many other hadiths which cannot be enumerated here. The summary is that they are hadiths of tawatur (mass transmission) from the Messenger of Allah, narrated by Abu Hurayra, Ibn Mas'ud, Uthman ibn Abi al-As, Abu Umama, al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Mujammi' ibn Haritha, and Hudhayfa ibn Usayd, may Allah be pleased with them all. And before that, we have examined the definitive verses from the Book of Allah Almighty that speak of the same as these hadiths indicate. Therefore, the Muslims have achieved consensus (ijma') on the belief in the descent of Jesus son of Mary at the end of time, in the manner and description that the Messenger of Allah told us, and that he was raised bodily alive to heaven as Allah Almighty clearly stated in His decisive declaration.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument that begins with a classification of the major signs of the Hour, then focuses on the descent of Jesus as one of those signs, provides two detailed hadiths as proofs, and concludes with the affirmation of the doctrine based on tawatur and ijma'. The author first enumerates ten major events: the Smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from the west, the descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three land sinkings (east, west, and Arabian Peninsula), and finally a fire from Yemen that drives people to their gathering place. This enumeration sets the eschatological context. Then he presents a lengthy hadith from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, which describes the Dajjal and Jesus' descent at the white minaret east of Damascus, his killing of the Dajjal at the gate of Ludd, and his care for the believers. The second hadith from Abu Hurayra emphasizes Jesus' role in breaking the cross, killing pigs, abolishing jizya, and calling to Islam, and states that he will remain on earth forty years. The author then asserts that these two hadiths, along with two others mentioned but not quoted, constitute a body of mutawatir (mass transmitted) reports, listing multiple companions as narrators. He further appeals to Quranic verses (unquoted) as supporting evidence and declares that the Muslims have reached consensus (ijma') on the literal bodily descent of Jesus at the end of time, confirming his bodily ascension. Thus, the passage establishes the doctrine through textual proof (hadith and Qur'an) and communal consensus, refuting any metaphorical interpretation.

Misconception: Some think the major signs are only a few events, but this list shows ten distinct signs.
Correction: Al-Buti's enumeration includes ten signs, and each is a separate major event.

Key Takeaway
The Hour is preceded by ten major signs, including the Dajjal, Jesus' descent, and the fire from Yemen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Smoke is described as a sign that will suffocate the disbelievers. If you saw the sky filled with such smoke tonight, would you be among those who recognize it and repent, or would you be among the heedless? What is holding you back from turning to Allah fully right now?
?
The Beast will speak to people and distinguish believers from disbelievers. Do you have certainty in all the unseen matters of the Hour, including this sign? Is there any doubt in your heart that you need to remove by seeking knowledge and strengthening your faith?
?
The last sign is a fire that will drive all of humanity to their gathering place. Imagine that fire behind you, pushing you forward. Are you living today as if you will face that gathering with faith and good deeds? What one change can you make tonight to ensure you are among the successful on that day?

The Hadith of al-Nawwas on Jesus' Descent
Al-Buti quotes the hadith of al-Nawwas detailing Jesus' descent and battle with the Dajjal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed description of Jesus' descent from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, including his appearance, location, and his killing of the Dajjal.

Core Idea
Jesus descends at the white minaret east of Damascus and kills the Dajjal at Lod.

Al-Buti presents a lengthy hadith narrated by al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an that describes the Dajjal's appearance and the subsequent descent of Jesus. This hadith is one of the primary textual proofs for the physical descent of Jesus at the end of time.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic and translation of the hadith from al-Nawwas. Focus on the sequence of events.
2
Identify key details about Jesus
Note where Jesus descends, his description (hands on angel wings, dripping head), and the effect of his breath on disbelievers.
3
Trace the events after descent
Follow the narrative: Jesus pursues the Dajjal, kills him at the gate of Ludd, and then addresses the protected believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدخان، والدجال، والدابة، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، ونزول عيسى بن مريم، ويأجوج ومأجوج، وثلاثة خسوف: خسف بالمشرق، وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب، وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم. ٣ - ما رويناه آنفاً عن مسلم وأبي داود والترمذي وأحمد وابن ماجه من حديث النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه عن رسول الله، بشأن الدجال، وفيه: فبينما هو كذلك إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم، فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مهرودتين واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر، وإذا رفعه تحدر منه جمان كاللؤلؤ، فلا يحل لكافر يجد ريح نفسه إلا مات، ونفسه ينتهي حيث ينتهي طرفه فيطلبه حتى يدركه بباب لد فيقتله ثم يأتي عيسى قوم قد عصمهم الله منه، فيمسح عن وجوههم ويحدثهم بدرجاتهم في الجنة ... الحديث ٤ - ما رواه أحمد وأبو داود وابن جرير بطرق مختلفة عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله: «الأنبياء إخوة لعلات، أمهاتهم شتى ودينهم واحد، صلى الله عليه وسلم وإني أولى الناس بعيسى بن مريم لأنه لم يكن نبي بيني وبينه، وإنه نازل فإذا رأيتموه فاعرفوه، رجل مربوع، إلى الحمرة والبياض، عليه ثوبان ممصران كأن رأسه يقطر وإن لم يصبه بلل: فيدق الصليب، ويقتل الخنزير، ويضع الجزية، ويدعو الناس إلى الإسلام، ويهلك الله في زمانه الملل كلها إلا الإسلام، ويهلك المسيح الدجال، فيمكث في الأرض أربعين سنة ثم يتوفى ويصلي عليه المسلمون فهذه أربعة أحاديث تنص على نزول عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وهنالك أحاديث كثيرة أخرى لا مجال لسردها هنا، والخلاصة أنها أحاديث متواترة عن رسول الله، من رواية أبي هريرة، وابن مسعود، وعثمان بن أبي العاص، وأبي أمامة، والنواس بن سمعان، وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص ومجمع بن حارثة، وحذيفة بن أسيد رضي الله عنهم وقد وقفت قبل ذلك على نصوص الآيات المحكمة من كتاب الله تعالى الناطقة بمثل ما دلت عليه هذه الأحاديث؛ فمن أجل ذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على الاعتقاد بنزول عيسى ابن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمن، على النحو وبالصفة التي ذكرها لنا رسول الله، وأنه إنما رفع ببدنه حياً إلى السماء كما بين الله عز وجل صريحاً في محكم بيانه
The Smoke, and the Dajjal, and the Beast, and the rising of the sun from its west, and the descent of Jesus son of Mary, and Gog and Magog, and three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that comes out of Yemen driving the people to their gathering place. 3 - What we related previously from Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ahmad, and Ibn Majah from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Messenger of Allah, concerning the Dajjal, and in it: 'While he is thus, Allah sends the Messiah son of Mary, and he descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two dyed garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels; when he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, drops fall from it like pearls; no disbeliever who smells his breath dies but he dies, and his breath reaches as far as his sight reaches; so he pursues him until he catches him at the gate of Ludd and kills him. Then Jesus comes to a people whom Allah has protected from him, and he wipes their faces and tells them of their ranks in Paradise... the hadith.' 4 - What Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Jarir narrated through various chains from Abu Hurayra, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The prophets are paternal brothers; their mothers are different but their religion is one. And I am the nearest of people to Jesus son of Mary because there was no prophet between me and him, and he will descend. When you see him, recognize him: a man of medium height, reddish-white, wearing two light-yellow garments, his head as if it is dripping though no moisture touches him. He will break the cross, kill the pig, impose the jizya, and call people to Islam. Allah will destroy in his time all religions except Islam, and he will destroy the Dajjal. Then he will remain on earth for forty years, then he will die, and the Muslims will pray over him.' So these are four hadiths that state the descent of Jesus son of Mary. There are many other hadiths which cannot be enumerated here. The summary is that they are hadiths of tawatur (mass transmission) from the Messenger of Allah, narrated by Abu Hurayra, Ibn Mas'ud, Uthman ibn Abi al-As, Abu Umama, al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Mujammi' ibn Haritha, and Hudhayfa ibn Usayd, may Allah be pleased with them all. And before that, we have examined the definitive verses from the Book of Allah Almighty that speak of the same as these hadiths indicate. Therefore, the Muslims have achieved consensus (ijma') on the belief in the descent of Jesus son of Mary at the end of time, in the manner and description that the Messenger of Allah told us, and that he was raised bodily alive to heaven as Allah Almighty clearly stated in His decisive declaration.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument that begins with a classification of the major signs of the Hour, then focuses on the descent of Jesus as one of those signs, provides two detailed hadiths as proofs, and concludes with the affirmation of the doctrine based on tawatur and ijma'. The author first enumerates ten major events: the Smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from the west, the descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three land sinkings (east, west, and Arabian Peninsula), and finally a fire from Yemen that drives people to their gathering place. This enumeration sets the eschatological context. Then he presents a lengthy hadith from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, which describes the Dajjal and Jesus' descent at the white minaret east of Damascus, his killing of the Dajjal at the gate of Ludd, and his care for the believers. The second hadith from Abu Hurayra emphasizes Jesus' role in breaking the cross, killing pigs, abolishing jizya, and calling to Islam, and states that he will remain on earth forty years. The author then asserts that these two hadiths, along with two others mentioned but not quoted, constitute a body of mutawatir (mass transmitted) reports, listing multiple companions as narrators. He further appeals to Quranic verses (unquoted) as supporting evidence and declares that the Muslims have reached consensus (ijma') on the literal bodily descent of Jesus at the end of time, confirming his bodily ascension. Thus, the passage establishes the doctrine through textual proof (hadith and Qur'an) and communal consensus, refuting any metaphorical interpretation.

Misconception: Some claim Jesus' descent is symbolic or spiritual, not physical.
Correction: This hadith describes a physical descent with specific location, bodily actions, and tangible effects (breath killing disbelievers).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Jesus will descend at a specific location and kill the Dajjal with his very breath, how would that change your certainty about the unseen? Are you living as if the Hour could come at any moment, or do you let doubt creep in?
?
The hadith says no disbeliever who smells Jesus's breath dies. How does this vivid, physical description affect your conviction that these events are real? Do you struggle to accept the literal details, and if so, what does that reveal about your faith in the Prophet's report?
?
When the protected believers are told their ranks in Paradise, they receive immediate comfort. What rank are you striving for now? Are your daily actions deliberately preparing you for that moment, or are you hoping to be saved without effort?

The Consensus on Jesus' Descent: Hadith of Abu Huraira and Conclusion
Al-Buti provides a second hadith and concludes with tawatur and ijma'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional proofs for Jesus' descent from the hadith of Abu Huraira and the basis for the Muslim consensus on this doctrine.

Core Idea
The descent of Jesus is confirmed by mutawatir hadith and the unanimous agreement of Muslims.

Al-Buti presents a second hadith from Abu Huraira that describes Jesus' actions after his descent, then argues that the hadith on this topic are mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and that the Muslim community has reached consensus (ijma') on the belief in his literal descent.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith of Abu Huraira
Read the hadith carefully. Note the description of Jesus' appearance and his actions after descent.
2
Understand the arguments for authenticity
Al-Buti lists multiple narrators and claims the hadith are mutawatir. He also cites Quranic verses (not quoted) as support.
3
Grasp the concept of consensus
Al-Buti concludes that because of these proofs, Muslims have unanimously accepted the belief in Jesus' descent. Reflect on the role of ijma' in Islamic doctrine.

Hadith and Consensus on the Descent of Jesus
Buti presents hadith evidence for Jesus's descent and states Muslim consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith evidence and Muslim consensus regarding the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The descent of Jesus is established by mutawatir hadith and unanimous consensus.

Buti presents the prophetic description of Jesus's return, then demonstrates that these hadith are mass-transmitted (mutawatir) and supported by Quranic verses, leading to the consensus of the entire Muslim community. This lesson explores how these sources together make the belief in Jesus's descent a definitive article of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith description
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the prophetic description of Jesus's appearance and actions come through.
Notice the vivid details: he breaks the cross, kills the pig, etc.
2
Note the claim of tawatur
Buti states that these hadith are mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and lists the Companions who narrated them. This elevates the level of certainty.
If hadith are mutawatir, they must be believed.
3
Understand how Quran and consensus reinforce
Buti mentions Quranic verses and then states that the entire Ummah has reached consensus (ijma') on this belief. This shows the doctrine is not based on hadith alone.
Consensus is a third source of certainty.

وإني أولى الناس بعيسى بن مريم لأنه لم يكن نبي بيني وبينه ، وإنه نازل فإذا رأيتموه فاعرفوه ، رجل مربوع ، إلى الحمرة والبياض ، عليه ثوبان ممصران كأن رأسه يقطر وإن لم يصبه بلل : فيدق الصليب ، ويقتل الخنزير ، ويضع الجزية ، ويدعو الناس إلى الإسلام ، ويهلك الله في زمانه الملل كلها إلا الإسلام ، ويهلك المسيح الدجال ، فيمكث في الأرض أربعين سنة ثم يتوفى ويصلي عليه المسلمون فهذه أربعة أحاديث تنص على نزول عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وهنالك أحاديث كثيرة أخرى لا مجال لسردها هنا ، والخلاصة أنها أحاديث متواترة عن رسول الله الله ، من رواية أبي هريرة ، وابن مسعود ، وعثمان بن أبي عليوة العاص ، وأبي أمامة ، والنواس بن سمعان ، وعبـد الله بن عمرو بن العاص ومجمع بن حارثة ، وحذيفة بن أسيد رضي الله عنهم ( وقد وقفت قبل ذلك على نصوص الآيات المحكمة من كتاب الله تعالى الناطقة بمثل ما دلت عليه هذه الأحاديث ؛ فمن أجل ذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على الاعتقاد بنزول عيسى ابن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمن ، على النحو وبالصفة التي ذكرها لنا رسول الله الله ، وأنه إنما رفع ببدنه حياً إلى السماء كما بين الله عز وجل صريحاً في محكم بيانه
And I am the most entitled of people to Jesus son of Mary, because there was no prophet between me and him. And indeed he is descending; so when you see him, recognize him: a man of medium stature, tending to redness and whiteness, wearing two garments lightly dyed with saffron, as if his head is dripping even though no wetness touches him. He will break the cross, kill the pig, abolish the jizya, and call people to Islam. And Allah will destroy in his time all religions except Islam, and will destroy the Dajjal. He will remain on earth forty years, then die, and the Muslims will pray over him. These are four hadiths that state the descent of Jesus son of Mary (peace and blessings be upon him), and there are many other hadiths for which there is no room to list here. The summary is that they are mutawatir hadiths from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), narrated by Abu Huraira, Ibn Mas'ud, Uthman ibn Abi al-As, Abu Umama, al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Mujammi' ibn Haritha, and Hudhayfa ibn Asid (may Allah be pleased with them). And I have previously reviewed the clear verses from the Book of Allah Almighty that speak of the same thing that these hadiths indicate. Therefore, the Muslims have reached consensus on the belief in the descent of Jesus son of Mary (peace be upon him) at the end of time, in the manner and description that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) told us, and that he was raised bodily alive to heaven, as Allah Almighty clearly stated in His clear revelation.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents a composite hadith describing the descent of Jesus, then asserts that these (four) hadiths are mutawatir and are supported by Quranic verses, leading to the consensus of Muslims on the belief in Jesus's bodily ascension and future descent. Buti begins by quoting a well-known prophetic tradition that details Jesus's physical appearance and actions upon his return: he will break the cross, kill the pig, abolish the jizya, and call to Islam, and will remain on earth for forty years before dying a natural death and being buried by Muslims. Buti then states that this is one of four hadiths on the topic, and that there are many others which he does not list. He emphasizes that these hadiths are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), naming several Companions as narrators. He then mentions that Quranic verses also support this, and as a result, the entire Muslim ummah has reached consensus (ijma') on the belief that Jesus was raised bodily to heaven and will descend at the end of time exactly as the Prophet described. The passage thus establishes the doctrinal certainty of Jesus's nuzul (descent) through tawatur of hadith and ijma' of the community.

Refuting the Denial of Jesus' Descent and Critiquing Shaltut's Method
Refutes denial of Jesus' descent and criticizes Shaltut's method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the denial of Jesus' descent is a consequence of a broader rejection of miracles, and how scholars like Shaltut rely on weak arguments and a fringe school's approach.

Core Idea
Denial of Jesus' descent stems from a school that rejects miracles, not from Islamic evidence.

This passage critiques the method of Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut, who attempted to reinterpret Quranic verses and reject numerous authentic hadiths to deny the descent of Jesus (AS). The author argues that this denial is not an isolated opinion but a natural outgrowth of a school that undermines miracles while claiming to uphold Islam. By examining Shaltut's approach, we see the dangers of selective interpretation and reliance on a fringe group's authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify Shaltut's claims
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note Shaltut's argument about ahad hadith and his reinterpretation of verses.
Shaltut claims that the hadith on Jesus' descent are ahad and cannot form belief.
2
Understand the author's linking to the anti-miracle school
The author reminds you of a previous discussion about a school that denies miracles. See how he connects Shaltut's denial to that school as a 'natural echo.'
This is a key argument: the denial is not original but derivative.
3
Recognize the critique of Shaltut's method
The author points out the contradiction in trying to reconcile Islam with denial of miracles. He criticizes Shaltut for rejecting 70 hadiths and declaring all tafsir scholars wrong without evidence.
Notice the emphasis on lack of evidence for Shaltut's positions.
4
See the author's defense of the established understanding
The author mentions that he has provided hadith and Quranic verses that clearly support the descent. He ends by dismissing the fringe group's attempts to reinterpret the verse of raf'.
The conclusion is that their effort will not succeed.

ونحن لانشك في أنها محاولة من حيث الظاهر فحسب ، اتقاء لغضب المسلمين وتدرجاً في التسلل إلى موضع العقيدة من قلوبهم . فهذا التخبط في محاولة التوفيق ، هو الذي جعل واحداً مثل الشيخ شلتوت لا يبالي أن يكذِّب سبعين حديثاً مع رواتها ، وأن يخطئ عامة المفسرين لكتاب الله منذ عصر الصحابة إلى بزوغ مدرسة أستاذه - في سبيل أن تسلم له عقيدة إنكار الخوارق والمعجزات !! Also, the nearness of the Hour. Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut wrote an article in Al-Risala magazine issue 462, followed by other articles on the same topic; and what he concluded in those articles was the interpretation of the verses and the disregard of the many authentic hadiths, claiming that they are singular (ahad) hadiths that cannot be relied upon for belief!! And perhaps you have read what we wrote about the position of science and reason regarding miracles in the discussion of prophethood, and you came to know the story of the school that denied miracles without explicitly denying religion, as you came to know the secret of the emergence of that school and the circumstances that formed it. So if you recall what we said then, know that the denial of the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) despite the conclusive evidence established on that, is nothing but a natural echo of that school and a fruit that fully agrees with its principles. However, both the confusion and blind floundering that the proponents of that school and their followers do not care to fall into, are manifested in the attempt to reconcile and combine adherence to Islam and adherence to the denial of supernatural events (khawariq) and miracles!! We have no doubt that it is an attempt only in appearance, fearing the anger of Muslims and gradually infiltrating into the place of faith in their hearts. This floundering in the attempt to reconcile is what made someone like Sheikh Shaltut not care to deny seventy hadiths with their narrators, and to consider the majority of commentators of the Book of God wrong from the time of the Companions to the emergence of his teacher's school - so that his doctrine of denial of miracles and supernatural events could be preserved!! And more astonishing than that is that he denies the hadiths without evidence, or the semblance of evidence, for their denial... And he declares the commentators wrong without evidence, or the semblance of evidence for their error. Yes, there is one evidence: the deviance of that fringe group that arose for known reasons and motives, denying miracles and supernatural events. This is the evidence that justifies uprooting the texts of the Sunnah and the indications of the Book from their roots and disregarding them entirely and in detail!! As for the Sunnah, we have transmitted to you a small part of it, and you have seen its explicit indication that does not accept any 'he said' and 'they said' around it. As for the Book, we have transmitted to you two verses, each of which has a clear indication of the meaning that the majority of commentators and the noble Companions adopted, except that this fringe group focuses all its attention on interpreting the verse of the raising (raf') and pulling it to the meaning of raising in spirit or raising in rank, imagining that if the paint of interpretation coheres on the texts of raising, then it will cohere afterwards with all ease on the texts of descent. Far be it from them to achieve that.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the denial of the descent of Jesus (AS) and a critique of the method of Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut and his school. The author begins by referencing Shaltut's articles where he interpreted verses and rejected many authentic hadiths, claiming they are ahad (solitary) and not suitable for belief. The author then reminds the reader of previous discussions about the school that denied miracles while not explicitly denying religion. He states that the denial of Jesus' descent is a natural consequence of that school. He points out the contradiction in attempting to reconcile Islam with denial of miracles, calling it a mere facade to avoid Muslim anger. He then criticizes Shaltut for rejecting seventy hadiths without evidence and declaring all tafsir scholars wrong, relying only on the deviance of a fringe group. Finally, he mentions that he has provided some hadith and two verses from the Quran that clearly support the meaning held by the majority of commentators and Companions, but the fringe group focuses on interpreting the verse of the raising (raf') to avoid the meaning of descent. The author concludes that their attempt will not succeed.

Linguistic Refutation of 'Tawaffi' as Death in Jesus Verse
Linguistically refutes claiming 'mutawaffika' means death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Arabic word 'tawaffi' literally means 'to take completely' and that its use for death is metaphorical, thus refuting the claim that the verse indicates Jesus died.

Core Idea
'Tawaffi' does not mean death; it means taking completely.

This lesson examines a key linguistic argument used to refute the claim that Jesus died. The verse 'Inni mutawaffika' is often misunderstood by those who take 'tawaffi' as synonymous with 'death'. The author clarifies the true meaning of the word and shows that death is only one metaphorical application.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the claim
Read the verse from Ali Imran 55 and the claim that 'mutawaffika' means 'causing your death'.
2
Understand the linguistic refutation
The author argues that 'tawaffi' means taking something completely, not necessarily death. Note the example 'istawfaytu haqqi'.
The root w-f-y means to complete.
3
See why the misconception arose
Common people use 'tawaffi' only for death, but its original meaning is broader. Scholars like al-Zamakhshari confirm that using it for death is metaphorical.
This is a key point: metaphorical usage does not cancel the literal meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكثر ما يتعلقون به ، في هذا الصدد ، كلمة « متوفيك « من قوله تعالى : إذ قال اللهُ يَاعيسَى إِنِّي مُتَوَفِّيكَ وَرافِعُكَ إِلَيَّ ومُطَهِّرُكَ مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا * [ آل عمران : ٥٥ ] ظناً بأن متوفيك مرادفة لميتك ! ولم يقل أحد من علماء اللغة ذلك ، بل التوفي معناه أخذ الشيء وقبضه تماماً ، ومرادفه الاستيفاء . نقول : استوفيت حقي وتوفيته أي قبضته كاملاً . أما الإماتة التي هي أخذ الروح، فهي نوع من أنواع التوفي الذي يشملها وغيرها وإنما سرى الوهم إلى هؤلاء من كثرة استعمال عامة الناس هذه الكلمة بمعنى الموت فقط وغفلة عن معناها الأصلي في اللغة . ولو رجع هؤلاء إلى اللغة لرأوا أن التعبير بالتوفي عن الموت يأتي في الدرجة الدلالة اللغوية ، كما يقول العلامة مصطفى صبري . ولذلك نص الزمخشري في كتابه أساس البلاغة على أن التعبير بالوفاة عن الموت من المجاز .
And what they cling to most, in this regard, is the word 'mutawaffika' from His statement: 'When Allah said, O Jesus, I will take you (mutawaffika) and raise you to Me and purify you from those who disbelieve.' (Ali Imran 55) supposing that 'mutawaffika' is synonymous with 'mumituka' (causing your death)! But none of the linguists have said that. Rather, 'tawaffi' means taking something and seizing it completely, and its synonym is 'istifa' (receiving in full). We say: 'istawfaytu haqqi wa tawaffaytuhu' meaning I received it completely. As for causing death (imata), which is the taking of the soul, it is a type of 'tawaffi' that includes it and others. The illusion only entered into them from the frequent use of this word by common people only in the sense of death, and heedlessness of its original meaning in the language. If they had referred to the language, they would have seen that the expression of 'tawaffi' for death comes in the second degree of linguistic signification, as the scholar Mustafa Sabri says. Therefore, al-Zamakhshari stated in his book Asas al-Balagha that the expression of 'wafat' for death is metaphorical.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic refutation of the misinterpretation of the word 'mutawaffika' in the verse. The author states that the deniers cling to this word thinking it means 'causing death'. He refutes this by explaining that linguistically, 'tawaffi' means to take something completely, not necessarily death. He gives the example of 'istawfaytu haqqi' (I received my right fully). He explains that death (imata) is only one type of tawaffi, as it is the taking of the soul. The confusion arose because common people use the word mainly for death. The author cites the scholar Mustafa Sabri and al-Zamakhshari to show that the use of 'tawaffi' for death is metaphorical, not literal. Therefore, the verse does not prove that Jesus died; rather, it means Allah took him up entirely.

Linguistic Proof that Jesus Was Physically Raised to Heaven
The author uses Arabic grammar to prove the literal meaning of the ascension verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Arabic particle 'bal' in Quran 4:158 necessitates a literal physical raising of Jesus to heaven, and why metaphorical interpretations are linguistically invalid.

Core Idea
The particle 'bal' demands a real negation and opposite, not a mere shift in meaning.

This lesson examines a key Quranic verse (4:157-158) that describes Jesus' fate. Using Arabic grammar, the author demonstrates that the word 'bal' (rather) forces a literal interpretation: if the Jews did not kill Jesus, then Allah must have physically raised him. This linguistic argument refutes metaphorical interpretations that claim only his rank was raised.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Start by reading verses 4:157-158 in Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: a negation ('they did not kill him') followed by 'bal' then a positive statement.
The verse is the foundation of the argument.
2
Understand the function of 'bal'
The author gives three examples showing that 'bal' must cancel the preceding clause and assert a contrary reality. Reflect on why 'I am not hungry, but I am lying down' is incorrect while 'I am not hungry, but I am full' is correct.
The key is that 'bal' requires a direct opposite.
3
Apply the rule to the verse
Apply the logic of 'bal' to 'They did not kill him, but Allah raised him to Himself.' The opposite of killing is not raising rank but physical preservation. Conclude that the raising must be literal.
The contrast must be real: physical death vs. physical ascension.
4
Examine Sheikh Shaltut's interpretation
Consider the author's refutation of Shaltut's claim that the raising is of rank. The author poses rhetorical questions: what does 'to Him' mean? Why restrict it to the crucifixion context?
These questions show the metaphorical reading is inconsistent.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
The author concludes that denying miracles leads to flawed interpretation. Consider how linguistic rules protect correct theological understanding.
This highlights the importance of sound methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي ينفي احتمال المجاز في (متوفيك) في هذه الآية، دلالة الآية القاطعة الأخرى التي لا مجال للتأويل فيها:
يقول الله عز وجل في سورة النساء: 157 و158: ﴿ وَقَولِهِمْ إِنَّا قَتَلْنَا الْمَسِيحَ عِيسَى ابْنَ مَرْيَمَ رَسُولَ اللهِ وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ وَمَا صَلَبُوهُ وَلَٰكِن شُبِّهَ لَهُمْ وَإِنَّ الَّذِينَ اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ لَفِي شَكٍّ مِّنْهُ مَا لَهُم بِهِ مِنْ عِلْمٍ إِلَّا اتِّبَاعَ الظَّنِّ وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ يَقِينًا بَل رَّفَعَهُ اللهُ إِلَيْهِ وَكَانَ اللهُ عَزِيزًا حَكِيمًا ﴾
فأما عقل العاقل الذي يفهم الكلام العربي عن طريق قواعد اللغة العربية ودلالاتها اللغوية، فهو يفهم من قوله تعالى: (وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ يَقِينًا بَل رَّفَعَهُ اللهُ إِلَيْهِ) أن الله عز وجل أخفى نبيه عنهم بأن رفعه إلى سمائه فلم يقعوا منه على شيء يقتلونه أو يصلبونه. يدلك على هذا المعنى ألفاظ الآية ودلالاتها اللغوية وضرورة التقابل الذي ينبغي أن يكون بين ما قبل بل وما بعدها. فليس لك أن تقول، وأنت عربي: لست جائعاً بل أنا مضطجع، وإنما تقول: لست جائعاً بل أنا شبعان. وليس لك أن تقول: ما مات خالد بل هو رجل صالح، وإنما تقول: بل هو حي. وليس لك أن تقول: ما قتل الأمير بل هو ذو درجة عالية عند الله، لأن كونه ذو درجة عالية عند الله لا ينافي أن يقتل، وإنما تأتي بل لإبطال ما قبلها بدليل مما بعدها.
لا جرم إذاً أن معنى الآية: ما قتله اليهود كما زعموا بل إن الله استلبه من بينهم ورفعه إلى السماء، ولكن الشيخ شلتوت يأبى إلا أن يكون المعنى: ما قتلوه، بل رفع الله درجته إليه، وذلك على الرغم من أنف القواعد العربية ودلالاتها وعلى الرغم من أنف العرب والمفسرين كلهم.
ولك أن تسأل أمثال الشيخ شلتوت، وهم يذهبون في تفسير الآية هذا المذهب: فما معنى «إليه» في الآية مادام أن الرفع هو رفع الدرجة؟ هل المعنى أن الله جعله إلها مثله؟!
إذ لا معنى لقولك: إن الله رفع مقام فلان إليه، إلا أنه قد جعله في مرتبته؟!
ثم ما معنى تقييد رفع الدرجة بحال قصد الصلب أو القتل؟ أو لم يكن مرفوع الدرجة قبل ذلك؟!
أسئلة لا جواب عليها، إلا استجرار الكلام والتأويل التي لا معنى لها، خدمة لما استقر في نفوسهم من مرض إنكار الخوارق والمعجزات ورحم الله من أبدع المثل القائل: بأن رجلاً نظر إلى حمار يافع فاشتهى لحمه، فالتفت إلى من حوله قائلاً: ما أشبه أذنيه بأذني الأرنب!
And that which negates the possibility of metaphor in 'mutawaffīka' in this verse is the indication of the other decisive verse which allows no interpretation: Allah Almighty says in Surah an-Nisa, 157-158: "And their saying, 'Indeed, we have killed the Messiah, Jesus, the son of Mary, the messenger of Allah.' And they did not kill him, nor did they crucify him; but [rather] it was made to appear to them. And indeed, those who differ over it are in doubt about it. They have no knowledge of it except the following of assumption. And they did not kill him, for certain. Rather, Allah raised him to Himself. And ever is Allah Exalted in Might and Wise." As for the mind of the intelligent person who understands Arabic speech through the rules of the Arabic language and its linguistic indications, he understands from His saying: "And they did not kill him, for certain. Rather, Allah raised him to Himself" that Allah Almighty concealed His prophet from them by raising him to His heaven, so they did not obtain from him anything to kill or crucify. This meaning is indicated to you by the words of the verse and its linguistic indications and the necessity of the contrast that must exist between what precedes 'bal' and what follows it. For you cannot say, while being Arab: 'I am not hungry, but rather I am lying down.' Rather, you say: 'I am not hungry, but rather I am full.' And you cannot say: 'Khalid did not die, but rather he is a righteous man.' Rather, you say: 'Rather, he is alive.' And you cannot say: 'The prince was not killed, but rather he has a high rank with Allah,' because his being of high rank with Allah does not negate that he was killed. Rather, 'bal' comes to invalidate what precedes it by evidence from what follows it. Therefore, inevitably, the meaning of the verse is: The Jews did not kill him as they claimed, but rather Allah snatched him from among them and raised him to heaven. But Sheikh Shaltut insists that the meaning be: They did not kill him, but rather Allah raised his rank to Him, this despite the nose of the Arabic rules and their indications and despite the nose of the Arabs and all the commentators. And you may ask the likes of Sheikh Shaltut, while they go in interpreting the verse this way: So what is the meaning of 'ilayhi' (to Him) in the verse, since the raising is the raising of rank? Does it mean that Allah made him a god like Him?! For there is no meaning to your saying: 'Allah raised the rank of so-and-so to Him,' unless He made him in His rank?! Then what is the meaning of restricting the raising of rank to the situation of intending crucifixion or killing? Was he not of high rank before that?! Questions that have no answer, except dragging speech and interpretation which have no meaning, serving the illness that has settled in their hearts of denying miracles and marvels. And may Allah have mercy on the one who invented the saying: A man looked at a young donkey and desired its meat, so he turned to those around him saying: 'How similar are its ears to the ears of a rabbit!'
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents a linguistic argument defending the literal interpretation of the Quranic verse about Jesus being raised to heaven. The author begins by citing the Quranic verses 4:157-158, then explains how an Arabic speaker would understand the function of the particle 'bal' (بل). He gives three examples showing that 'bal' must negate the preceding clause and affirm the opposite: e.g., 'I am not hungry, but rather I am full' (contrast: lying down would be illogical). He applies this to the verse: the Jews did not kill Jesus; rather, Allah raised him to Himself. He then refutes Sheikh Shaltut's claim that the raising is merely of rank, using rhetorical questions: if the raising is of rank, what does 'to Him' mean? And why would it be restricted to the context of the crucifixion attempt? He concludes that such interpretations stem from a psychological denial of miracles and dismisses them with a satirical analogy about a man who sees a donkey and compares its ears to a rabbit's.

Key Terms

مُتَوَفِّيك
رفع
تأويل
مجاز
شلتوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the particle 'bal' can be used simply to contrast without fully negating the previous statement.
Correction: The author shows that 'bal' demands complete negation and the establishment of a direct opposite, as demonstrated by the examples.

Checkpoint
What linguistic function does the author attribute to 'بل' (bal) in the verse?
A) It indicates a mere addition.
B) It invalidates what precedes and establishes the opposite.
C) It provides a reason for the preceding.
D) It marks a change of topic.

Key Takeaway
The Arabic particle 'bal' forces a literal reading of Jesus' ascension as a physical event, and denying this leads to linguistically and theologically unsound interpretations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse of the Quran whose apparent meaning conflicts with your rational expectations or desires, do you immediately seek a metaphorical interpretation? How does the rule of 'bal' challenge your tendency to soften the Quran's clear statements?
?
The author attributes metaphorical interpretations to an 'illness of denying miracles.' Is there any area of your faith where you resist believing in the miraculous because it seems too extraordinary? What would it cost you to simply submit to the literal meaning of Allah's words?
?
Imagine you are confronted with a clear text from the Quran that contradicts a deeply held assumption. Would you be willing to revise your assumption, or would you twist the text to fit your prior beliefs? What does your answer reveal about the state of your heart towards revelation?
