The Emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj: A Major Sign of the Hour
Buti explains the Quranic account of Ya'juj and Ma'juj and their appearance before the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic account of Ya'juj and Ma'juj, their nature as a major sign of the Hour, and that the timing of their appearance is known only to Allah.

Core Idea
Ya'juj and Ma'juj are a great nation whose sudden emergence is a major sign of the approaching Hour, but only Allah knows when.

In this lesson, we explore the Quranic description of Ya'juj and Ma'juj (Gog and Magog). Buti explains that these terms refer to a vast, destructive nation that will appear suddenly as one of the major signs of the Hour. The Quran conceals the timing, but affirms their emergence as a portent of the end. We will examine the Quranic verses that describe their release and the barrier built by Dhul-Qarnayn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of Buti's explanation.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses quoted.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice the three main points: the definition of Ya'juj and Ma'juj, the concealment of their timing, and their role as a major sign of the Hour.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Consider how the verses from Surah Al-Anbiya' and Al-Kahf support Buti's explanation. What do they say about the emergence and the barrier?
The verses describe both the release and the eventual destruction of the barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳ - ظهور يأجوج ومأجوج : يأجوج ومأجوج : هاتان الكلمتان عبر بها القرآن عن أمة كبيرة من الناس يفاجأ بها العالم تنسل إليه من كل حدب، تنشر الفساد والدمار في الأرض، على نحو مذهل وبطريقة مرعبة. غير أن القرآن أخفى عن الناس ميعاد ظهورهم. فلا يعلم أجل ذلك أحد إلا الله عز وجل. ولكنه نص على أن ظهورهم علامة من العلامات الكبرى لاقتراب الساعة. وهذا هو إخبار القرآن عنهم: حتى إذا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُم مِن كُلِّ حَدَبٍ يَنسِلُونَ * وَاقتَرَبَ الوَعدُ الحَقُّ فَإِذَا هِيَ شَاخِصَةٌ أَبْصَارُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا يَا وَيلَنَا قَد كُنَّا فِي غَفلَةٍ مِن هَذَا بَل كُنَّا ظَالِمِينَ [الأنبياء: ٩٦-٩٧]. قالُوا يَا ذَا القَرنَينِ إِنَّ يَأجُوجَ وَمَأجُوجَ مُفسِدُونَ فِي الأَرضِ فَهَل نَجعَلُ لَكَ خَرجًا عَلَى أَن تَجعَلَ بَينَنَا وَبَينَهُم سَدًّا * قَالَ مَا مَكَّنِي فِيهِ رَبِّي خَيرٌ فَأَعِينُونِي بِقُوَّةٍ أَجعَل بَينَكُم وَبَينَهُم رَدْمًا * آتُونِي زُبَرَ الحَدِيدِ حَتَّى إِذَا سَاوَى بَينَ الصَّدَفَينِ قَالَ انفُخُوا حَتَّى إِذَا جَعَلَهُ نَارًا قَالَ آتُونِي أُفرِغ عَلَيهِ قِطرًا * فَمَا اسطَاعُوا أَن يَظهَرُوهُ وَمَا استَطَاعُوا لَهُ نَقبًا * قَالَ هَذَا رَحمَةٌ مِن رَبِّي فَإِذَا جَاءَ وَعدُ رَبِّي جَعَلَهُ دَكَّاءَ وَكَانَ وَعدُ رَبِّي حَقًّا * وَتَرَكنَا بَعضَهُم يَومَئِذٍ يَمُوجُ فِي بَعضٍ [الكهف: ٩٤-٩٩]. أما أخبار السنة عنهم، فتأكيد للذي أخبر عنهم القرآن.
3 - The emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj: Ya'juj and Ma'juj: these two words the Quran uses to describe a great nation of people with which the world will be suddenly confronted, slipping out from every hill, spreading corruption and destruction on the earth, in an astounding manner and a terrifying way. However, the Quran concealed from people the appointed time of their emergence. So no one knows its term except Allah Almighty. But He stated that their emergence is a major sign of the approach of the Hour. And this is the Quran's report about them: "Until when Ya'juj and Ma'juj are let loose and they swoop down from every hill. And the true promise draws near; then behold, the eyes of those who disbelieved stare fixedly: 'Woe to us! We were indeed heedless of this; nay, we were wrongdoers.'" [Al-Anbiya': 96-97]. They said: "O Dhul-Qarnayn, indeed Ya'juj and Ma'juj are corrupting on the earth; so may we assign to you a tribute that you may make a barrier between us and them?" He said: "That wherein my Lord has established me is better; so assist me with strength; I will make between you and them a rampart. Bring me blocks of iron." Until when he had leveled between the two cliffs, he said: "Blow," until when he had made it fire, he said: "Bring me, that I may pour over it molten copper." So they were not able to scale it, nor were they able to pierce it. He said: "This is a mercy from my Lord; but when the promise of my Lord comes, He will level it to the ground; and the promise of my Lord is ever true." And on that Day, We will leave them surging like waves over one another [Al-Kahf: 94-99]. As for the reports of the Sunnah about them, they are a confirmation of what the Quran reported about them.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a Quranic lesson about Ya'juj and Ma'juj (Gog and Magog). Buti begins by defining the term, stating that the Quran uses these words to refer to a great nation of people whose sudden emergence from every direction will cause widespread corruption and destruction in a stunning and terrifying manner. He then notes that the exact time of their appearance is hidden by the Quran; only Allah knows it. However, the Quran explicitly states that their emergence is one of the major signs of the approaching Hour. To support this, Buti quotes two sets of Quranic verses. First, from Surah Al-Anbiya' (21:96-97), which describes the release of Ya'juj and Ma'juj and the reaction of the disbelievers when the true promise (the Hour) approaches. Second, from Surah Al-Kahf (18:94-99), which recounts the story of Dhul-Qarnayn and the building of a barrier against Ya'juj and Ma'juj, but also indicates that this barrier will be destroyed when the promise of the Lord comes, leading to chaos. Finally, Buti mentions that the hadith reports about them simply confirm what the Quran has already stated.

Key Terms

العلامات الكبرى
الساعة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ya'juj and Ma'juj have already appeared or are a specific historical tribe.
Correction: The Quran describes their emergence as a future major sign of the Hour, not a past event.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what does the Quran say about the timing of the emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj?
A) It is known to the scholars
B) It is concealed and known only to Allah
C) It will be announced by the Prophet
D) It occurs regularly throughout history

Key Takeaway
Ya'juj and Ma'juj are a great nation whose sudden, destructive emergence is a major sign of the Hour, but their exact time of appearance is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that the emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj is a sign of the Hour, your heart may feel distant from that reality. But if you are honest with yourself, do you live today as if the Hour could come at any moment, or do you behave like the heedless disbelievers who will say 'We were heedless of this'? What one concrete change will you make this week to prepare for that Day?
?
The barrier of Dhul-Qarnayn was a mercy from Allah, yet it was ultimately temporary and will be destroyed. What barriers have you built in your life to protect yourself from sin—your routines, your environment, your self-discipline? Are you relying on those barriers or on the One who controls their destruction? How can you shift your trust from your own efforts to Allah's promise that His decree will come?
?
The exact time of Ya'juj and Ma'juj is known only to Allah. If He were to unveil to you that the Hour would begin one month from today, what would you do differently? Why are you not doing that now? Do not let yourself ignore the urgency of this lesson—write down one action you will start doing today as if the signs are already unfolding.

Yajuj and Majuj: Definition and Quranic Evidence
Defines Yajuj and Majuj and quotes Quranic verses about them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic definition of Yajuj and Majuj as a real nation whose emergence is a major sign of the Hour, supported by two Quranic passages.

Core Idea
Yajuj and Majuj are a literal nation whose sudden release marks the approach of the Hour.

This lesson introduces Yajuj and Majuj, a people mentioned in the Quran. The author defines them as a vast nation that will cause widespread destruction. He also presents two key Quranic passages that describe their emergence and the barrier built by Dhul-Qarnayn. Let's read the source passage and explore its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author combines definition with direct Quranic quotation.
2
Identify the definition of Yajuj and Majuj
Find how the author defines Yajuj and Majuj: they are a great nation that will suddenly emerge, spreading corruption. Note that their time is unknown but their appearance is a major sign.
The definition is in the first few lines before the verses.
3
Study the first Quranic passage
Read Al-Anbiya' 96-97. Notice how it describes their release and the reaction of the disbelievers. The verse emphasizes the suddenness and terror of the event.
This passage highlights the eschatological significance.
4
Study the second Quranic passage
Read Al-Kahf 94-99. This passage narrates the story of Dhul-Qarnayn building a barrier against Yajuj and Majuj, which will be levelled at the appointed time.
This shows that their containment is temporary and that their release is decreed by Allah.
5
Reflect on the significance as a major sign
Connect these passages to the broader topic of the major signs of the Hour. Consider why the author emphasizes that the time of appearance is hidden but the fact of appearance is certain.
This reinforces the Quranic teaching on the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يأجوج ومأجوج : هاتان الكلمتان عبر بها القرآن عن أمة كبيرة من الناس يفاجأ بها العالم تنسل إليه من كل حدب ، تنشر الفساد والدمار في الأرض ، على نحو مذهل وبطريقة مرعبة . غير أن القرآن أخفى عن الناس ميعاد ظهورهم . فلا يعلم أجل ذلك أحد إلا الله عز وجل . ولكنه نص على أن ظهورهم علامة من العلامات الكبرى لاقتراب الساعة . وهذا هو إخبار القرآن عنهم : حتى إذا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُم مِنْ كُلِّ حَدَبٍ يَنْسِلُونَ واقتَرَبَ الوَعدُ الحَقُّ فَإذا هِيَ شاخِصَةٌ أَبْصَارُ الَّذِينَ كَفَروا ، يَا وَيْلَنَا قَدْ كُنَّا فِي غَفْلَةٍ مِن هذا بَل كُنَّا ظالمين ) [ الأنبياء : ٩٦ - ٩٧ ] . ل .. قالُوا يَا ذَا القَرْنَيْنِ إِنْ يَأْجُوجَ وَمَأْجُوجَ مُفْسِدُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ ، فَهَل نَجْعَلُ لَكَ خَرْجاً على أن تَجْعَلَ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَهُم سَداً قال ما مكني فِيهِ رَبِّي خَيْرٌ ، فأعينُونِي بقوَّةٍ أَجْعَلْ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَهُمْ رَدماً . آتُونِي زُبَرِ الحَديدِ حَتَّى إذا ساوى بينَ الصَّدَفَيْنِ قال انفُخُوا حَتَّى إذا جَعَلَهُ ناراً قَالَ أَتُونِي أُفْرِغْ عَلَيْهِ قطراً . فا اسطاعُوا أن يَظْهَرُوهُ وَما استطاعُوا لَهُ نَقْباً قالَ هَذا رَحْمَةٌ مِنْ رَبِّي فَإِذَا جَاءَ وَعدُ رَبِّي جَعَلَهُ دَكّاءَ وَكان وعد ربي حقاً
Yajuj and Majuj: these two words, the Qur'an used to refer to a great nation of people that the world will suddenly be surprised by, emerging from every elevated place, spreading corruption and destruction on the earth, in a staggering manner and terrifying way. But the Qur'an concealed from people the time of their appearance. No one knows its appointed time except Allah Almighty. Rather, it stated that their appearance is one of the major signs of the approach of the Hour. This is the Qur'an's report about them: "Until when Gog and Magog are let loose and they race down from every elevated place. And the true promise has drawn near; then behold, the eyes of those who disbelieved will be staring in horror, [saying], 'Woe to us! We were indeed heedless of this; rather, we were wrongdoers.'" [Al-Anbiya': 96-97]. They said, "O Dhul-Qarnayn, indeed Gog and Magog are corrupting the earth; so may we assign for you an expenditure that you might make between us and them a barrier?" He said, "That in which my Lord has established me is better; but assist me with strength; I will make between you and them a fortification. Bring me sheets of iron until, when he had leveled [them] between the two mountain sides, he said, 'Blow [with bellows],' until when he had made it fire, he said, 'Bring me molten copper to pour over it.' So they were not able to scale it, nor were they able to penetrate it. He said, 'This is a mercy from my Lord; but when the promise of my Lord comes, He will make it level, and ever is the promise of my Lord true.'" [Al-Kahf: 94-99]
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage defines Yajuj and Majuj and presents the Quranic evidence. The author begins by explaining that 'Yajuj and Majuj' are Quranic terms for a vast nation whose sudden emergence will bring destruction. The time of their appearance is unknown, but their emergence is a major sign of the approaching Hour. The author then quotes two Quranic passages. The first (Al-Anbiya' 96-97) describes their release and the reaction of the disbelievers. The second (Al-Kahf 94-99) narrates the story of Dhul-Qarnayn building a barrier against them, which will be levelled when the promise of the Lord comes. The interpretation follows the apparent meaning: Yajuj and Majuj are real people, and their escapement is a future event. The author does not comment on allegorical interpretations.

Correction: This passage affirms their literal existence as a real nation mentioned in the Quran.

Checkpoint
What is the Quranic description of how Yajuj and Majuj will emerge?
A) They will appear gradually over time.
B) They will race down from every elevated place.
C) They will come from the sea.
D) They will emerge from behind a barrier peacefully.

Key Takeaway
Yajuj and Majuj are a real people whose sudden emergence is a major sign of the end times, as affirmed by two Quranic passages.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The exact time of Yajuj and Majuj's appearance is hidden. Are you living as if the Hour could come tomorrow, or does your daily routine reveal that you are comfortable thinking it is far off? Be honest with yourself.
?
Dhul-Qarnayn called the barrier a mercy from Allah. What barrier has Allah placed in your life to protect you from corruption that you have been ungrateful for? How will you thank Him today?

Hadith Evidence on Yajuj and Majuj as a Major Sign
Presents three hadiths confirming Yajuj and Majuj and emphasizes the limits of creedal certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key hadith evidence establishing Yajuj and Majuj as a major sign of the Hour and the principle that only certain details are creedally binding.

Core Idea
The Qur'an and authentic hadiths confirm Yajuj and Majuj's emergence; most details come from weak sources.

This lesson presents three authentic hadiths that confirm what the Qur'an states about Gog and Magog. These reports are foundational for Muslim belief in this major sign. At the same time, the lesson draws an important boundary: while the general fact of their emergence is certain, many circulating details are unreliable and not part of creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths with attention
Read the three hadiths: the one from Zaynab bint Jahsh, the long hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an (excerpt), and the list of ten signs from Hudhayfa ibn Asid. Note the key elements each adds.
The first shows the Prophet's alarm, the second describes their effect on Lake Tiberias, the third lists them among ten major signs.
2
Understand the author's conclusion
The author states that these hadiths provide conclusive evidence (dalala qati'a) that the appearance of Gog and Magog is a sign of the Hour. Belief in this is necessary for faith in the Book and Sunnah.
3
Distinguish between certain and speculative
The author warns that most details about their attributes, physical forms, and specific reports come from weak or fabricated hadiths. In matters of creed, we must not rely on such sources.
This is a key principle: only what is authentically established is binding in 'aqida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما أخبار السنة عنهم ، فتأكيد للذي أخبر عنهم القرآن . روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن زينب بنت جحش أن النبي استيقظ من نومه وهو يقول : لا إله إلا الله ، ويل للعرب من شر قد اقترب ، فتح اليوم من ردم يأجوج ومأجوج مثل هذه . وعقد الراوي بيده عشرة . قلت : يارسول الله أنهلك وفينا الصالحون ؟ قال : نعم إذا كثر الخبث . وروى مسلم والترمذي وابن ماجه وأحمد عن النواس بن سمعان الحديث الطويل الذي ذكرناه آنفاً والذي فيه خبر الدجال وعيسى بن مريم ، وفيه : « ويبعث يأجوج ومأجوج وهم من كل حدب ينسلون فيمر أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية فيشربون ما فيها ، ويمر آخر هم فيقولون : لقد كان بهذه مرة ماء . وروى مسلم وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه عن حذيفة بن أسيد الغفاري عنه ، قال : طلع علينا النبي ونحن نتذاكر ، فقال : مــا تذاكرون ؟ قالوا : نذكر الساعة ، قال : إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آیات : الدخان ، والدجال ، والدابة ، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ، ونزول عيسى بن مريم ، ويأجوج ومأجوج ، وثلاث خسوف : خسف بالمشرق وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب ، وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من أرض اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم . فتلك الآيات وهذه الأحاديث ، ذات دلالة قاطعة على أن من أشراط الساعة ظهور هذه الأمة التي تعثو فساداً في الأرض . فكان الإيمان بذلك من الضروريات التي لابد منها للإيمان بالكتاب والسنة . أما علم ما وراء ذلك من التفصيلات المتعلقة بصفاتهم وكيفياتهم ، وتفصيل أخبارهم معظم ما ورد من تفاصيل أخبارهم وصفاتهم وأشكال جسومهم ، إنما تناقله الناس عن طريق أحاديث واهية أو منكرة أو باطلة ، فلا مطمع في باب العقيدة في الوصول إلى شيء من ذلك .
As for the reports of the Sunnah about them, they are confirmation of what the Qur'an reported about them. Al-Bukhari and Muslim and others narrated from Zaynab bint Jahsh that the Prophet woke up from his sleep saying: 'There is no god but Allah, woe to the Arabs from an evil that has drawn near. Today a gap has been opened in the barrier of Gog and Magog like this.' And the narrator clasped his hand to indicate ten. I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, will we be destroyed while there are righteous among us?' He said: 'Yes, when wickedness increases.' And Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Ahmad narrated from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an the long hadith we mentioned earlier which includes the story of the Dajjal and Jesus son of Mary, and in it: 'Gog and Magog will be sent forth and they will race down from every elevated place, and their first ones will pass by Lake Tiberias and drink what is in it, and their last ones will pass and say: There was once water here.' And Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah narrated from Hudhayfa ibn Asid al-Ghifari, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Prophet came upon us while we were discussing. He said: 'What are you discussing?' We said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: 'It will not come until you see before it ten signs: the smoke, the Dajjal, the beast, the rising of the sun from its west, the descent of Jesus son of Mary, Gog and Magog, three landslides: a landslide in the east, a landslide in the west, and a landslide in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that will emerge from the land of Yemen driving the people to their gathering place.' So these verses and these hadiths are conclusive evidence that among the signs of the Hour is the appearance of this nation that spreads corruption in the earth. Thus belief in that is among the necessities that are indispensable for belief in the Book and the Sunnah. As for knowledge beyond that of the details concerning their attributes and modalities, and detailed accounts of their reports—most of the details of their reports, attributes, and forms of their bodies have been transmitted by people through weak, objectionable, or false hadiths—there is no aspiration in the matter of creed to arrive at any of that.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage presents three hadiths that confirm the Quranic report about Yajuj and Majuj. First, the hadith of Zaynab bint Jahsh: the Prophet woke up alarmed, declaring that a gap had been opened in the Gog and Magog barrier, indicating that their emergence has begun. When asked if the righteous will be destroyed, he answered yes when wickedness increases. This shows that the appearance of Gog and Magog is a sign of widespread corruption. Second, the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, part of a longer narration about the Dajjal and Jesus, mentions that Gog and Magog will be sent forth, and their enormous numbers will drink up Lake Tiberias. Third, the hadith of Hudhayfa ibn Asid lists ten major signs of the Hour, including Gog and Magog. The author concludes that these Quranic verses and hadiths constitute decisive evidence (dalala qati'a) that the appearance of Gog and Magog is a sign of the Hour, and belief in this is a necessary component of faith in the Book and Sunnah. Then the author adds a crucial caveat: detailed descriptions of their attributes and physical forms, which are often circulated via weak or fabricated hadiths, should not be relied upon in creedal matters ('aqida). The author thus distinguishes between what is established as necessary belief (that they will appear) and what is speculative or unreliable (specific details).

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
أشراط الساعة
العلامات الكبرى
بحيرة طبرية
حديث واه
باب العقيدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All details about Gog and Magog, such as their size, shape, and specific adventures, are part of Islamic belief.
Correction: Only the general fact of their emergence is certain from the Qur'an and authentic hadiths; most details rely on weak or fabricated narrations and are not binding in creed.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Authentic hadiths confirm that Gog and Magog will appear as a major sign of the Hour, but detailed descriptions from weak narrations are not part of Islamic belief.

?

Do you live as if the Hour could be tomorrow, or have you become numb to these warnings? What would change if you truly believed that a gap has already been opened?
?
The author tells us that most details about Gog and Magog come from weak hadiths and are not part of creed. Yet many people confidently repeat those details. Are you careful in what you spread about the unseen, or do you pass along information without verifying its source? How can you ensure your talk about the Last Day is grounded in certainty?
?
The hadith mentions that destruction comes when wickedness increases even among the righteous. If the righteous among us today do not stand against corruption, are we already on the path to that destruction? What is one concrete way you can increase goodness in your community starting this week?

The Correct Approach to Ya'juj and Ma'juj
Author advises stopping at definitive evidence and refutes identifying them with Mongols.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct methodological approach to eschatological signs like Ya'juj and Ma'juj, and why identifying them with historical peoples is incorrect.

Core Idea
Do not speculate about unseen matters; rely only on definitive texts.

This passage from Dr. Ramadan al-Buti provides crucial guidance on how to approach the subject of Ya'juj and Ma'juj. He warns against relying on weak traditions or personal deductions, and emphasizes the need to stop at what is definitively established. He also refutes the common claim that they were the Mongols and Tatars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the literal translation to understand the author's exact words.
Pay attention to the key terms like 'dalalah qat'iyyah' and 'rajm bil-ghayb'.
2
Identify the methodological principles
Look for the author's instructions: stop at definitive indication, wait for reality, and avoid weak traditions. These form the core advice.
3
Understand the refutation
The author rejects the identification of Ya'juj and Ma'juj with the Mongols/Tatars. Note how he uses authentic hadiths to show they appear after the Dajjal and during Jesus' descent.
This corrects a common misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخير من الخوض في ذلك أن نقف عند حدود الدلالة القطعية التي ثبتت بصريح القرآن وصحاح الأحاديث الواردة عن الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ثم تنتظر في معرفة الكنه والتفاصيل، الواقع الزمني نفسه ، فهو الذي سيتكفل وحده بشرح كل شيء عنهم . وذلك لأن يأجوج ومأجوج غيب من الغيوب التي أخبرنا الله عن ظهورهم بين يدي الساعة ، وهو أمر لم يظهر بعد ، فهو لا يزال في تلافيف الغيب لم يتبد لنا منه إلا الإخبار عنه بشكل إجمالي . إذ لا عبرة بالتفصيلات التي وصلتنا بالطرق الباطلة أو الواهية . وإذا فلا معنى للخوض في شيء لا سبيل إلى العلم بتفصيلاته اللهم إلا سبيل الرجم بالغيب ومن هنا تعلم ، أن ماقد يقوله بعضهم استنتاجاً واجتهاداً ، من أن يأجوج ومأجوج هم التتر والمغول الذين جاؤوا وانتهوا - كلام لا معتمد له ولا داعي إليه ، بل هو فيما يبدو مخالف لنصوص الأحاديث الصحيحة الدالة على أنهم إنما يظهرون في وقت نزول عيسى بن مريم وبعد ظهور الدجال . وحسبنا أن نعلم بأن هذه الأمة إذا ظهرت فإن ظهورها سيتكفل بالتعريف بها للناس كلهم تعريفاً لا يشوبه شك أو احتمال ولا يحوج إلى استنتاج أو اجتهاد .
And the best thing than delving into that is that we stop at the limits of definitive indication that has been established by the clear text of the Qur'an and the sound hadiths from the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him), then we wait for the knowledge of the essence and details, the actual temporal reality itself, for it alone will undertake to explain everything about them. That is because Ya'juj and Ma'juj are an unseen from the unseen things that Allah informed us of their appearance before the Hour, and it is a matter that has not yet appeared, so it still remains in the folds of the unseen; nothing has become clear to us from it except the general report about it. For there is no consideration for the details that have reached us through false or weak ways. And if so, there is no meaning in delving into something for which there is no way to know its details, except the way of casting at the unseen. And from this you learn that what some people say by deduction and ijtihad, that Ya'juj and Ma'juj are the Tatars and Mongols who came and ended—it is a statement that has no reliance and no need for it; rather, it appears to contradict the texts of the authentic hadiths indicating that they only appear at the time of the descent of Jesus son of Mary and after the appearance of the Dajjal. And it is sufficient for us to know that when this nation appears, its appearance will undertake to introduce itself to all people with an introduction that is free of any doubt or probability and does not require deduction or ijtihad.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage provides methodological guidance for dealing with eschatological signs like Ya'juj and Ma'juj. The author argues that we must confine ourselves to definitive proofs from the Qur'an and sound hadith, and not engage in speculation. He explains that Ya'juj and Ma'juj are an unseen matter that has not yet occurred; therefore, details from weak sources are worthless. He then refutes the claim that they are the extinct Mongols and Tatars, noting that authentic hadiths place their appearance after the Dajjal and during the time of Jesus. Finally, he reassures that when they do appear, their identity will be unmistakable, leaving no room for doubt or interpretation.

غيب
الدلالة القطعية
الرجم بالغيب
التتر والمغول
الدجال
عيسى بن مريم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ya'juj and Ma'juj were the historical Tatars and Mongols who have already come and gone.
Correction: Authentic hadiths indicate they appear after the Dajjal and during the time of Jesus (peace be upon him), so they are still future.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The proper approach to eschatological signs is to rely on definitive texts and avoid speculation; false identifications like the Mongols are refuted by authentic hadiths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What unseen matter in your life—whether about the future, the afterlife, or others—do you find yourself speculating about instead of submitting to what Allah has revealed? Will you repent and stop that speculation today?
?
The author warns against 'casting at the unseen.' When have you engaged in such speculation about religious matters, perhaps about eschatological signs or other unseen events? Commit now to seek only authentic knowledge and to remain silent on what you do not know.
?
If you knew that the exact time and details of Ya'juj and Ma'juj's appearance are not for you to know, how would that change the way you spend your time and energy? Will you redirect your focus to actions that are certain and beneficial for your faith?

The Beast of the Earth: Definition and Proofs
Author defines the Beast of the Earth and provides Quranic and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Beast of the Earth and the Quranic and hadith evidence for its appearance as a major sign of the Hour.

Core Idea
The Beast of the Earth is a literal creature that will mark believers and disbelievers before the Hour.

The author now turns to one of the major signs of the Hour: the Beast of the Earth (Dabbat al-Ard). He begins by defining it based on the Quran, then supports the definition with multiple authentic hadiths. Pay attention to how the author uses both primary sources to establish this as a factual event in Islamic creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the entire Arabic passage and its translation. Note the author's style: he first gives a definition, then quotes the Quranic verse, and then cites three hadiths.
The passage combines definition and evidence in one flow.
2
Understand the definition
Identify the key elements in the author's definition: the Beast is an animal whose specific nature is known only to Allah, it will appear before the Hour, speak to people, and mark each person according to their faith.
The marking (wasm) is a physical sign of faith or disbelief.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse from Surah An-Naml (27:82). Notice how it directly states that Allah will bring forth a creature from the earth that speaks to people.
The verse is the primary Quranic evidence for the Beast.
4
Analyze the three hadiths
The author quotes three hadiths from Sahih Muslim. The first establishes the Beast as one of the first signs alongside the rising sun from the west. The second lists it among six signs to hasten with deeds. The third includes it among ten signs before the Hour.
These hadiths reinforce the Beast's reality and timing.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the author presents this as a matter of 'aqidah: belief in the Beast is part of belief in the unseen. Reflect on the common misconception that it is allegorical.
The author treats it as a literal, physical event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- ظهور دابة الأرض :
ودابة الأرض تعبير قرآني عن حيوان نكل علم نوعه وشكله وهيئته إلى الله عز وجل ، يظهر للناس قبيل الساعة يكلمهم ويصف كلاً منهم بصفته من الإيمان أو الكفر ، فيَسِمُ الكافر بوسم الكفر ، ويطبع المؤمن بطابع الإيمان . وحينئذ لا تنفع نفساً إيمانها إن لم تكن قد آمنت من قبل
يقول الله عز وجل في ذلك : ﴿ وَإِذَا وَقَعَ القَوْلُ عَلَيْهِم أَخْرَجْنَا لَهُم دَابَّةٌ مِنَ الأرضِ تُكَلِّمُهُم أَنَّ النّاسَ كانوا بِآيَاتِنا لا يُوقِنُون ﴾ [النمل : ۸۲]
وروى مسلم بسنده عن عبد الله بن عمرو ، قال : حفظت من رسول الله حديثاً لم أنسه بعد ، سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : « إن أول الآيــات خروجاً طلوع الشمس من مغربها وخروج الدابة على الناس ضحى وأيتها كانت قبل صاحبتها فالأخرى على أثرها قريباً »
وروى مسلم أيضاً عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال : قال رسول الله بادروا بالأعمال ستة : طلوع الشمس من مغربها والدخان والدجال ، والدابة وخاصة أحدكم وأمر العامة
وروينا آنفاً عن مسلم وغيره حديث : ما تذاكرون ؟ قالوا : نذكر الساعة ، قال : إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آيات وعد منها دابة الأرض
- Appearance of the Beast of the Earth:
And the Beast of the Earth is a Quranic expression for an animal whose type, form, and appearance we consign to Allah Almighty; it appears to people before the Hour, speaking to them and describing each one of them with his attribute of faith or disbelief; so it marks the disbeliever with the mark of disbelief, and stamps the believer with the stamp of faith. And then no soul's faith will benefit if it had not believed before.
Allah Almighty says concerning that: {And when the Word is fulfilled against them, We will bring forth for them a creature from the earth speaking to them, that the people were not certain of Our signs} [An-Naml: 82].
And Muslim narrated with his chain from Abdullah ibn Amr, who said: I memorized from the Messenger of Allah a hadith that I have not forgotten afterwards: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Indeed the first of the signs to appear is the rising of the sun from its west and the emergence of the Beast to the people in the forenoon; whichever of them appears first, the other follows it closely.'
And Muslim also narrated from Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Hasten with deeds before six [things]: the rising of the sun from its west, the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the death of one of you, and the general matter.'
And we have previously narrated from Muslim and others the hadith: 'What are you discussing?' They said: 'We are mentioning the Hour.' He said: 'It will not be established until you see before it ten signs,' and he counted among them the Beast of the Earth.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage defines and provides evidence for one of the major signs of the Hour: the Beast of the Earth (Dabbat al-Ard). The author first gives its Quranic definition: a creature whose exact nature is known only to Allah, which will emerge before the Hour, speak to people, and distinguish believers from disbelievers by marking them. He then quotes the Quranic verse from Surah An-Naml. Following this, he cites three hadiths: one from Muslim about the Beast appearing alongside the rising sun from the west, another from Abu Huraira listing six signs including the Beast, and a final hadith mentioning the Beast among ten signs. These hadiths establish the Beast as a literal, future event.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people interpret the Beast of the Earth allegorically, as a symbol for a movement or ideology.
Correction: The author presents the Beast as a literal physical creature that will appear before the Hour, based on clear Quran and hadith texts.

Key Takeaway

?

?

If you were to die tonight, would your faith be accepted? Ask yourself honestly and seek Allah's forgiveness for any complacency.

The Rising of the Sun from the West: A Major Portent of the Hour
Author explains hadith evidence and meaning of sun rising from west.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith evidence for the sun rising from the west as a major sign of the Hour, its meaning, and the theological caution against speculating on the mechanism.

Core Idea
The sun rising from the west is a definitive sign of the Hour that renders subsequent faith useless.

In this passage, the author discusses one of the major portents of the Hour explicitly mentioned only in the Sunnah. He cites the famous hadith from Bukhari and explains the meaning of this sign. He also cautions against over-speculating on the exact mechanism, leaving that knowledge to Allah. This lesson will walk you through the evidence and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
The passage ends with a footnote that is cut off; focus on the complete argument before it.
2
Identify the hadith evidence
Notice that the author identifies this sign as exclusive to the Sunnah and quotes the Bukhari hadith about the sun rising from the west.
The hadith includes the statement that faith will not benefit after this sign.
3
Understand the explanation
The author explains that the sun will appear to rise from the west, possibly due to a change in Earth's rotation. Grasp this as a miraculous alteration of natural laws.
4
Reflect on the author's caution
The author warns against trying to determine the exact mechanism, stating that knowledge of it is with Allah alone.
This reinforces the importance of accepting the sign as a supernatural event.

ه - طلوع الشمس من مغربها :
وهو من الآيات التي تفردت السنة بذكرها صراحة ، روى البخاري عن النبي حديثاً طويلاً عن أشراط الساعة ، وفيه ، لاتقوم الساعة حتى تطلع الشمس من مغربها . فإذا طلعت ورآها الناس آمنوا أجمعون فذلك حين لا ينفع نفساً إيمانها لم تكن آمنت من قبل أو كسبت في إيمانها خيراً .
ومثل ذلك ما رويناه من الأحاديث السابقة في معرض الحديث عن دابة الأرض
ومعنى طلوع الشمس من مغربها أنها تظهر للناس طالعة من جهة المغرب في وقت الصباح بدلاً من ظهورها لهم من ناحية المشرق كما كان دأبها كل يوم . وذلك كأن يجعل الله دوران الأرض عندها في اتجاه آخر يتراءى معه للناس انعكاس سير الشمس بالنسبة إليهم
(1) ليس هذا تقريراً لبيان الوسيلة التي بها تخرج الشمس من مغربها ، فعلم ذلك عند الله . ولكنه
E - The Rising of the Sun from its West:
And it is among the signs that the Sunnah alone mentioned explicitly. Al-Bukhari narrated from the Prophet a long hadith about the portents of the Hour, in which it says: 'The Hour will not be established until the sun rises from its west. When it rises and the people see it, they will all believe; then is the time when no soul's faith will benefit if it had not believed before or earned good in its faith.'
And similar to that is what we have narrated in the previous hadiths in the context of discussing the Beast of the Earth.
And the meaning of the sun rising from its west is that it appears to people rising from the direction of the west in the morning instead of appearing to them from the direction of the east as was its custom every day. That is as if Allah makes the earth rotate then in another direction so that the reflection of the sun's movement relative to them appears to them.
(1) This is not a statement to explain the means by which the sun comes out from its west; rather, knowledge of that is with Allah. But it...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage discusses the sign of the sun rising from the west, which is a major portent of the Hour. The author notes that this sign is explicitly mentioned only in the Sunnah, not in the Qur'an, and cites a hadith from Bukhari. The hadith states that when the sun rises from the west, all people will believe, but that faith will no longer be accepted. The author explains the meaning: the sun will appear to rise from the west, which can be understood as a change in the earth's rotation. He then adds a clarifying footnote (incomplete in our text) stating that this explanation is not a definitive account of the mechanism, which is known only to Allah.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
أشراط الساعة
لا ينفع نفساً إيمانها
دوران الأرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some deny the sign of the sun rising from the west because modern astronomy shows that the sun does not actually move around the earth.
Correction: The author accepts this sign as a supernatural miracle that overrides normal laws; the explanation about earth's rotation is merely an illustration, not a scientific claim.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens immediately after the sun rises from the west?
A) The Dajjal appears
B) The Beast emerges
C) All people believe, but faith becomes useless
D) The earth is destroyed

Key Takeaway
The sun rising from the west is a definitive sign of the Hour, and when it occurs, faith will no longer be accepted from those who had not believed earlier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the sun were to rise from the west tomorrow, would you be among those who believe for the first time? What does that tell you about the current state of your faith? What specific step will you take today to ensure your faith is not delayed until it is too late?
?
The author leaves the mechanism of this miracle unknown, submitting to Allah's power. Is there an area of your life where you are withholding submission because you demand to understand first? What would it look like for you to submit now, even without full understanding?
?
You have heard this sign before now. Does knowing that faith after seeing it will not benefit move you to examine your heart? What is one belief or action you will change today because you still have the chance to believe before the signs appear?

Unseen Matters
intermediate
6 min
Prophetic Narrations on Major Signs of the Hour
Buti cites hadiths about the sun rising from the west and the beast as signs of the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific hadith evidence for the sun rising from the west and the beast as major signs of the Hour, and the necessity of believing in them based on the Sunna and consensus.

Core Idea
The Sunna explicitly mentions the sun rising from the west and the beast as real signs we must believe in.

Buti now turns to the major eschatological signs (ashrat al-sa'ah) that are explicitly mentioned in sound hadiths. He focuses on two key signs: the rising of the sun from the west and the emergence of the beast. By quoting multiple authentic hadiths, he establishes that these are not metaphorical but real events that will occur, and that belief in them is obligatory by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from hadith to conclusion.
The passage begins with a hadith about the first signs, then lists more hadiths, then focuses on the sun rising.
2
Identify each hadith and its source
List the hadiths quoted: the first from the Prophet directly, the second from Muslim via Abu Hurairah, the third also from Muslim, and the fourth from Bukhari. Note their content.
Pay attention to the narrators and the key phrases like 'first of the signs' and 'hasten to do good deeds before six things'.
3
Examine the subsection on the sun rising
Read the part starting with 'ه - طلوع الشمس من مغربها'. Note that it says this sign is explicitly mentioned in the Sunna, and quotes Bukhari's hadith about faith not benefiting after this sign.
This hadith emphasizes the finality of the sign and the cutoff for acceptance of faith.
4
Understand the conclusion on belief
Read the concluding sentences about 'truthful report' and 'consensus'. Why does Buti emphasize these are from al-khabar al-sadiq and that Muslims agree on the necessity of belief?
This shows the source of knowledge and the binding nature of these signs.
5
Reflect on the broader context
Consider Buti's mention that many other signs have already occurred. What does this imply about the approach to eschatology?
It affirms that prophetic reports about the unseen are to be accepted as they are.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حديثاً لم أنسه بعد ، سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : « إن أول الآيات خروجاً طلوع الشمس من مغربها وخروج الدابة على الناس ضحى وأيتها كانت قبل صاحبتها فالأخرى على أثرها قريباً » . وروى مسلم أيضاً عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « بادروا بالأعمال ستة : طلوع الشمس من مغربها والدخان والدجال ، والدابة وخاصة أحدكم وأمر العامة » . وروينا آنفاً عن مسلم وغيره حديث : « ما تذاكرون ؟ » قالوا : نذكر الساعة ، قال : « إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آيات » وعد منها دابة الأرض . ه - طلوع الشمس من مغربها : وهو من الآيات التي تفردت السنة بذكرها صراحة ، روى البخاري عن النبي حديثاً طويلاً عن أشراط الساعة ، وفيه : « لا تقوم الساعة حتى تطلع الشمس من مغربها . فإذا طلعت ورآها الناس آمنوا أجمعون فذلك حين لا ينفع نفساً إيمانها لم تكن آمنت من قبل أو كسبت في إيمانها خيراً » . ومثل ذلك ما رويناه من الأحاديث السابقة في معرض الحديث عن دابة الأرض . فهذه الأمور ، من أهم أشراط الساعة التي وصل إلينا علمها عن طريق الخبر الصادق ، وأجمع المسلمون على ضرورة الاعتقاد بها . وللساعة أشراط وعلامات أخرى تحدث عنها النبي في كثير من أحاديثه ، وكثير منها ظهر وتحقق كما أخبر ولا مجال لذكرها والتوسع في الحديث عنها في هذا المقام . والله تعالى أعلم
I have not forgotten a hadith recently: I heard the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) say: 'The first of the signs to emerge is the rising of the sun from its west and the emergence of the beast upon the people in the forenoon, and whichever of them comes before the other, the other follows it closely.' And Muslim also narrated from Abu Hurairah (may God be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: 'Hasten to do good deeds before six things: the rising of the sun from its west, the smoke, the Dajjal, the beast, the death of one of you, and the general matter.' And we narrated recently from Muslim and others the hadith: 'What are you discussing?' They said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: 'It will not be established until you see ten signs before it,' and he counted among them the beast of the earth. Section 5: The rising of the sun from its west: It is among the signs that the Sunna has mentioned explicitly. Al-Bukhari narrated from the Prophet a long hadith about the signs of the Hour, in which he said: 'The Hour will not be established until the sun rises from its west. When it rises and people see it, they will all believe, but that is the time when the faith of a soul that had not believed before will not benefit it, nor will it have earned good through its faith.' And similar to that is what we have narrated from the previous hadiths in the context of discussing the beast of the earth. These matters are among the most important signs of the Hour that have reached us through the truthful report, and the Muslims have agreed upon the necessity of believing in them. The Hour has other signs and portents that the Prophet mentioned in many of his hadiths, many of which have appeared and been fulfilled as he informed, and there is no room to mention and elaborate on them in this context. And God Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadithic evidence and a statement of consensus regarding major signs of the Hour, specifically the rising of the sun from the west and the beast. It begins by quoting a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that the first sign to emerge is the sun rising from the west and the beast. Then a hadith from Muslim lists six things to hasten to do good deeds before, including the sun from the west and the beast. Next, a hadith about ten signs before the Hour includes the beast. The author then introduces a specific subsection on the rising of the sun from the west, stating that it is among the signs mentioned explicitly in the Sunna, and quotes a hadith from Bukhari that the Hour will not occur until that happens, and that at that time faith will not benefit those who had not believed before. He notes that similar narrations about the beast have been mentioned earlier. The author then concludes that these matters are among the most important signs conveyed by truthful reports, and there is consensus among Muslims on the necessity of believing in them. He further mentions that there are other signs that the Prophet spoke of, many of which have already occurred, but their detailed discussion is beyond the scope of this work. The passage ends with 'And God knows best.' The author follows the order: presenting the hadith evidence, then affirming the authority of the Sunna and consensus.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
دابة الأرض
الخبر الصادق
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think these signs are metaphorical or that belief in them is optional.
Correction: Buti emphasizes they are explicit in the Sunna and mandatory to believe by consensus.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith from Bukhari, what happens after the sun rises from the west?
A) The Hour immediately occurs
B) All people believe but their faith does not benefit them if they had not believed before
C) The beast emerges immediately after
D) The sun stays in the west forever

Key Takeaway
The rising of the sun from the west and the beast are explicitly mentioned in authentic hadiths, and Muslims must believe in them as real signs of the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet commanded: 'Hasten to do good deeds before six things' — among them the sun rising from the west. When that happens, no new faith will be accepted. Are you truly hastening to good deeds right now, or are you assuming you still have time before the sun rises from the west?
?
If you were to die today, would the good deeds you have earned through your faith be enough? The hadith warns that at the sign of the sun rising from the west, even those who never believed will declare faith, but it will not benefit them. How does your current level of faith and action compare to that last desperate moment?
?
You have just read that the Muslims have unanimously agreed that believing in these signs is obligatory. But belief is not just intellectual assent — it must transform how you live. What specific change in your daily routine will you make today to prove that you truly believe the sun will one day rise from the west?
